2:24:1453:0:14:72:514:700:12:Times:12:Times:C:The Production of Human Capital in Developed Countries: Evidence from 196 Randomized
2:25:1537:14:14:72:160:686:12:Times:12:Times:C:Field Experiments
2:26:1554:14:14:72:165:672:12:Times:12:Times:C:Roland G. Fryer, Jr

2:30:1628:28:28:273:338:602:12:Times:12:Times:C:ABSTRACT
2:31:1636:28:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:C:Randomized  field  experiments  designed  to  better  understand  the  production  of  human  capital 
2:32:1738:14:14:72:546:560:12:Times:12:Times:C:have increased  exponentially  over  the  past  several  decades.  This  chapter  summarizes  what  we 
2:33:1840:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:C:have  learned about  various  partial  derivatives  of  the  human  capital  production  function,  what 
2:34:1944:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:C:important partial derivatives are left to be estimated, and what – together – our collective efforts 
2:35:2044:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:C:have  taught  us  about  how  to  produce human  capital  in  developed  countries.  The  chapter 
2:36:2141:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:C:concludes with a back of the envelope simulation of how much of the racial wage gap in America 
2:37:2235:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:C:might  be  accounted  for  if  human  capital  policy  focused on  best  practices  gleaned  from 
2:38:2332:14:42:72:218:476:12:Times:12:Times:C:randomized field experiments.
2:39:2361:42:14:72:165:434:12:Times:12:Times:C:Roland G. Fryer, Jr
2:40:2380:14:14:72:198:420:12:Times:12:Times:C:Department of Economics
2:41:2403:14:14:72:165:406:12:Times:12:Times:C:Harvard University
2:42:2421:14:14:72:166:392:12:Times:12:Times:C:Littauer Center 208
2:43:2440:14:14:72:187:378:12:Times:12:Times:C:Cambridge, MA  02138
2:44:2460:14:14:72:124:364:12:Times:12:Times:C:and NBER
2:45:2468:14:250:72:184:350:12:Times:12:Times:C:rfryer@fas.harvard.edu
2:46:2490:250:0:72:447:100:12:Times:12:Times:C:A Online appendix is available at http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w22130
3:47:2564:0:44:99:388:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:“The True Method of Knowledge is Experiment” – William Blake
3:48:2624:44:32:72:171:667:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:1    Introduction
3:49:2641:32:20:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Racial and ethnic inequality is a stubborn empirical reality across the developed world. Blacks in the United
3:50:2750:20:20:72:540:615:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:States earn twenty-four percent less, live five fewer years, and are six times more likely to be incarcerated on
3:51:2862:20:21:72:540:595:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:any given day (Fryer 2010). Black men in the United Kingdom are three times more likely to be unemployed
3:52:2966:21:20:72:540:574:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and as full-time workers, earn twenty percent less (Hatton 2011). The Roma in Hungary are over two years
3:53:3070:20:20:72:539:554:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:less educated, have worse self-reported health, and earn twenty-eight percent less (K ́antor 2011).  Turkish
3:54:3178:20:21:72:540:534:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:immigrants  in  Germany  are  almost  twice  as  likely  to  be  unemployed  and  earn  thirty-eight  percent  less
3:55:3293:21:20:72:540:513:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(von Loeffelholz 2011).  African immigrants in Spain are less educated than natives, have a 4.9 percentage
3:56:3399:20:20:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:point higher unemployment rate, and earn thirty-five percent less (de la Rica 2011). The income difference
3:57:3505:20:21:72:492:473:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:between natives and second generation immigrants in Sweden is 11% (Nordin and Rooth 2007).
3:58:3595:21:20:88:539:452:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Gaining a better understanding of the underlying causes of such stark racial and ethnic inequality is of
3:59:3699:20:20:72:540:432:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tremendous importance for public policy.  Using data from the U.S., O’Neill (1990) and Neal and Johnson
3:60:3802:20:21:72:540:412:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(1996) demonstrate that blacks, Hispanics, and whites are paid similar prices for similar pre-market skill
3:61:3908:21:20:72:540:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:bundles – yet, there are large differences in skills. Similarly, Nordin and Rooth (2007) show that differences
3:62:4018:20:20:72:540:371:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in income between natives and second generation immigrants in Sweden depend strongly on a skill gap –
3:63:4119:20:21:72:540:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:when controlling for scores on the Swedish Military Enlistment Test, the income gap decreases by more
3:64:4220:21:20:72:164:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:than seventy percent.
3:65:4241:20:20:88:539:310:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:An important question then, is what obstacles preclude the acquisition of productive skills.  Using ten
3:66:4344:20:21:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:large datasets which together, include students that range in age from eight months to 17 years old, Fryer
3:67:4450:21:20:72:540:269:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and  Levitt  (2013)  show  that  the  racial  achievement  gap  is  remarkably  robust  across  time,  samples,  and
3:68:4566:20:20:72:540:249:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assessments.  The achievement gap does not exist in the first year of life, but black students in the U.S. fall
3:69:4677:20:21:72:540:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:behind by age two (in the raw data) and these racial differences in academic achievement after kindergarten
3:70:4784:21:20:72:540:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cannot be explained by including standard controls. Similarly, controls cannot explain differences between
3:71:4890:20:20:72:540:188:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children of natives and children of immigrants on international standardized tests such as the Programme for
3:72:4998:20:20:72:540:168:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:International Student Assessment (PISA), Trends in International Mathematics and Science Study (TIMSS),
3:73:5101:20:21:72:540:148:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Progress in International Reading Literacy Study (PIRLS) in other developed countries such as France,
3:74:5206:21:20:72:377:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Switzerland, Netherlands, and Sweden (Parsons and Smeeding 2008).
3:75:5271:20:20:88:539:107:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:If the deleterious effects of labor market discrimination are in decline and the importance of productive
3:76:5376:20:0:72:540:87:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:skills are on the rise, an important public policy question is how to increase human capital – particularly for
4:77:5488:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:those who, due to accident of birth, begin life disadvantaged.  A fuller understanding would allow policy
4:78:5593:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:makers to use basic economic principles (e.g.  equating marginal return to marginal costs) in their decision
4:79:5701:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:making.  Is it more cost-effective to decrease class size or provide parents financial incentives to increase
4:80:5810:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student achievement? Should school districts increase the management skills of principals or increase early
4:81:5917:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:childhood programs?  What is a better use of resources – early childhood investments or providing high-
4:82:6020:21:20:72:209:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dosage tutoring to adolescents?
4:83:6051:20:20:88:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In an effort to answer questions like these, education researchers have spent decades trying to infer causal
4:84:6159:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:relationships from non-experimental data by examining large data sets and invoking various assumptions,
4:85:6262:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:many of which are not verifiable.  Prior to the late 1970s, research on the relationship between class size
4:86:6369:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and academic achievement was widely considered inconclusive (Porwell 1978; Glass and Smith 1978).  In
4:87:6470:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fact, some studies, including the famous Coleman Report, suggested there were greater gains in classrooms
4:88:6575:21:20:72:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:withmorestudents (Nelson 1959; Coleman et al.  1966).  These studies did not adequately account for the
4:89:6678:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fact that school districts commonly bundled better students and teachers in classrooms with more students.
4:90:6784:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:A well-designed randomized experiment would enable researchers to avoid such confounding factors and
4:91:6884:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:help settle the debate among non-experimental estimates. Using the random assignment of students to small
4:92:6989:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:classes in Project STAR, Krueger (1999) showed that students assigned to small classrooms indeed do score
4:93:7094:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:higher than students in regular sized classrooms.  The effect sizes for the K-3 students in Project STAR are
4:94:7202:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the range of 0.19-0.28 standard deviations and represent 64 to 82 percent of the white-black test score gap
4:95:7312:20:20:72:117:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the data
4:96:7323:20:20:88:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Similarly, a large body of non-experimental studies have found significant positive correlations between
4:97:7427:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:neighborhood socioeconomic status and students’ academic achievement (Aaronson 1998; Ainsworth 2002;
4:98:7527:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Chase-Lansdale and Gordon 1996; Chase-Lansdale et al. 1997; Duncan, Brooks-Gunn, and Klebanov 1994;
4:99:7626:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Halpern-Felsher et al. 1997; Kohen et al. 2002). However, randomized and quasi-experimental studies have
4:100:7730:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:failed to establish a causal link. Although Rosenbuam (1995) found that suburban students from Chicago’s
4:101:7834:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Gautreaux program outperformed urban students,  Jacob (2004) found no effects on students’ test scores
4:102:7936:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from switching neighborhoods due to housing demolitions. Further, Oreopoulous (2003) found no evidence
4:103:8038:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of long-term impacts of neighborhood quality on labor market outcomes in a quasi-experimental analysis.
4:104:8141:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:More importantly, in the short-run, the Moving to Opportunity randomized housing mobility experiment
4:105:8241:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(Ludwig et al.  2012;  Kling,  Liebman and Katz 2007;  Sanbonmatsu et al.  2011) produced no sustained
4:106:8343:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:improvements in academic achievement, educational attainment, risky behaviors, or labor market outcomes
4:107:8446:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for either female or male children, including those who were below school age at the time of random assign-
4:108:8553:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment. Interestingly though, Chetty et al. (2016) show that the Moving to Opportunity experiment had large
5:109:8659:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts on early-adulthood outcomes for children who were younger than 13 years old at randomization.
5:110:8760:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In their mid-twenties, these individuals have 31% higher income, have higher college attendance rates, are
5:111:8866:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:less likely to be single parents, and live in better neighborhoods relative to similar individuals in the control
5:112:8979:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:group.  For children who were older than 13 years old at randomization, the experiment had no positive
5:113:9081:20:21:72:154:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:long-term impacts.
5:114:9099:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In the 1920s, William McCall, an education psychologist at Columbia University, was one of the first
5:115:9199:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:supporters of using randomization to investigate the validity of education programs. His 1923 book, “How
5:116:9303:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to Experiment in Education”, developed a method for gathering data by randomly determining treatment and
5:117:9407:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control groups.  His work provided the framework for the experimental designs we see in educational field
5:118:9512:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments today.  Many of the early influential education field experiments came decades after McCall’s
5:119:9617:20:21:72:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:book with the wave of large-scale social experiments in the latter half of the 20th century.1In the 1960s we
5:120:9725:21:20:71:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:saw the Perry preschool experiment and the income maintenance experiments, in the 1970s the Abecedarian
5:121:9828:20:20:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:project was initiated, and in the 1980s there was Project STAR, the Tennessee class size experiment. The data
5:122:9937:20:21:71:539:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from these randomized experiments alone were used for decades to investigate many interesting questions
5:123:10040:21:20:71:253:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:about how to best produce human capital.
5:124:10080:20:20:88:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The inherent power of randomized field experiments is in the ability to estimate partial derivatives of
5:125:10183:20:21:71:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the educational production function.  That is, holding other variables constant, one can alter the amount of
5:126:10291:21:20:71:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:time students spend in school or the salary of their teachers, or whether or not the students receive financial
5:127:10402:20:20:71:301:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:incentives. One’s imagination is the only real bound.
5:128:10455:20:20:88:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To see the advantages of this approach, imagine the following simple production process.2LetYi jdenote
5:129:10557:20:21:72:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a measure of an academic achievementjfor individuali, wherejmight represent state test scores or other
5:130:10659:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:norm-referenced  tests  such  as  the  Peabody  Picture  Vocabulary  Tests  or  the  Woodcock-Johnson  Tests  of
5:131:10771:20:37:72:526:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Achievement. For eachj, assume a simple Education Production Function (EPF) of the following form:
5:132:10869:37:37:257:354:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f5:?:Yi=f(Ei,Si,Hi,Mi,P)
5:133:10888:37:20:71:539:190:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:where,Ei= denotes studenti′searly childhood experience,Sicaptures various school inputs,Hirepresents
5:134:10988:20:20:71:539:170:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:household and neighborhood inputs,Mi, captures “social skills” such as grit, resilience, or what psycholo-
5:135:11094:20:21:71:374:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:gists often refer to as “the Big 5.” Let P be a vector of relevant prices.
5:136:11168:21:19:88:540:129:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:We assume thatfis smooth and continuously differentiable in its arguments.  Imagine that we want
5:137:11264:19:11:87:326:110:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:1See Levitt and List (2009) for a brief history of field experiments.
5:138:11333:11:14:87:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:2The  model  is  meant  to  illuminate,  clarify,  and  contrast  estimates  in  the  literature.   It  is  not  meant  to  be  “realistic”  or  to
5:139:11480:14:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:be directly estimable.  There is a rich literature designed to better understand and empirically estimate the education production
5:140:11610:11:0:72:409:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:function (Cunha and Heckman 2007; Hanushek 1979; Krueger 1999; Todd and Wolpin 2003).
6:141:11696:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to understand the impact of important changes in home environment on student test scores, holding school
6:142:11800:20:21:72:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:quality, mindset, and early childhood experience fixed.  This is equivalent to estimating∂Y∂H.  On the other
6:143:11908:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:hand, we may want to understand the impact of investments in school-based reform on human capital holding
6:144:12013:20:20:72:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:all else equal by estimating∂Y∂S. Or, the impact of instilling more “grit” or a “growth mindset” into students,
6:145:12124:20:21:72:242:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:all else equal. This is equivalent to∂Y∂M.
6:146:12166:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Perhaps recognizing the net benefits of randomized field experiments and because of a desire to avoid
6:147:12267:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:past miscues due to biased estimates, federal and local governments, early childhood centers, entrepreneurs,
6:148:12375:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and school districts have become laboratories for randomized field experiments.  Forty-five years after the
6:149:12482:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:famous Perry Preschool experiment, families in Chicago Heights were rewarded for teaching their own chil-
6:150:12587:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dren a similar curriculum (Fryer, Levitt, and List 2015). Thirty years after the seminal class size experiment
6:151:12697:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in public elementary schools of Tennessee, school districts in both America and Europe have implemented
6:152:12800:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:various tutoring experiments,  management best practices,  and programs designed to increase the human
6:153:12902:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:capital of the adults in school buildings (e.g.  Fryer 2014; Cook et al.  2014; Clark et al.  2013; Garet et al.
6:154:13014:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2008; Carlson et al. 2011; May et al. 2013; Blachman et al. 2004). Forty years after the income maintenance
6:155:13121:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments, public policy across the developed world is being influenced by researchers investigating the
6:156:13227:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts of welfare-to-work programs, earnings supplements, and parental involvement (e.g. Hamilton et al.
6:157:13332:20:21:72:312:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2001; Michalopoulos et al. 2002; Avvisati et al. 2014).
6:158:13387:21:20:88:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Indeed, randomized control trials in education have increased exponentially over the past 50 years.  In
6:159:13490:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2000,  14 percent of reviewed education publications on What Works Clearinghouse met their standards
6:160:13590:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:without reservations, a distinction given only to well-designed studies that have comparison groups deter-
6:161:13696:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mined through a random process. By 2010, that number had tripled to over 46 percent. Figure 1 provides a
6:162:13800:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:time series of studies in education. Throughout the 1980s, these randomized education studies were sparse.
6:163:13906:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:But in the 1990s, we start seeing a steady flow of approximately 10 publications a year that utilize a random
6:164:14015:20:21:72:517:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:design and then this number increases all the way up to a high of 49 randomized experiments in 2009.
6:165:14115:21:20:88:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Given the remarkable increase in the use of randomized field trials over the past 50 years and the robust
6:166:14220:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:correlation between human capital and other economic outcomes such as income and employment, it’s time
6:167:14322:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to take stock and summarize what we have learned about various partial derivatives of the human capital
6:168:14425:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:production function, what important partial derivatives are left to be estimated, and what – together– our
6:169:14531:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:collective effort over the past several decades has taught us about how to produce human capital in developed
6:170:14640:20:23:72:118:122:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:countries.3
6:171:14651:23:14:87:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:3To be clear, randomized trials are not a panacea. There are important limitations to randomized controlled trials, which have
6:172:14777:14:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:been documented in Deaton (2010), Mosteller and Boruch (2002), Worrall (2007), and Rothstein and von Wachter (2016), the latter
6:173:14904:11:0:72:540:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:in this volume. We describe a few here. First, many questions that are potentially interesting to economists may not be answerable
7:174:15035:0:20:88:263:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:This chapter attempts to do three things.
7:175:15076:20:21:88:540:691:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f2:A:First, We conducted a relatively exhaustive search of all randomized field experiments in education. We
7:176:15179:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:define a field experiment as any intervention that uses averifiablyrandom procedure to assign participants to
7:177:15288:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment and control groups in a non-laboratory environment. This definition, while restrictive, is consistent
7:178:15399:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with the definition of a field experiment described in Harrison and List (2004) and the US Department of
7:179:15503:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Education’s What Works Clearinghouse “without reservation” standard.  Using this definition, we sourced
7:180:15606:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:almost one thousand field experiments to be included in our analysis.   We further limited the sample of
7:181:15710:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:studies to be included to studies conducted in “highly developed” countries with standardized reading or
7:182:15814:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math outcomes.4These restrictions eliminated almost three-quarters of the experiments, leaving a sample
7:183:15917:20:20:72:103:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of 199.
7:184:15924:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:We divide our sample of studies into three main categories of intervention – early childhood, school-
7:185:16025:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:based interventions, and home-based interventions – and provide a summary of the literature within each
7:186:16128:20:20:72:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:category.5Early childhood experiments investigate the impacts of preschool attendance, home-based ini-
7:187:16230:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tiatives that target pre-kindergarten children, and different preschool models on early achievement. Indeed,
7:188:16338:21:23:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:any experiment with outcomes measured before kids enter school is categorized as early childhood – inde-
7:189:16442:23:11:72:540:403:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:with a randomized trial. For instance, how much of the variance in achievement is explained by genetic endowment? Given we are
7:190:16568:11:11:72:540:392:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:not likely to alter genetics by means of a field experiment, if one is wed to randomized controlled trials (RCTs) then this question
7:191:16700:11:10:72:540:381:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:is unanswerable. Second, as with all statistics – the evaluation of field experiments has implications for the mean of the population
7:192:16833:10:11:72:540:371:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:and may have little value in predicting individual behavior. With large enough RCTs, one can alleviate some of these concerns by
7:193:16961:11:11:72:540:360:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:estimating heterogeneous treatment effects.  Third, and likely most constraining, are a host of important caveats which center on
7:194:17090:11:11:72:540:349:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:external validity. One cannot always generalize the results from a local RCT to other contexts. An obvious example of this is if an
7:195:17221:11:11:72:540:338:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:RCT finds a program has large impacts using a sample of poverty-stricken minority children, one cannot assume the program will
7:196:17347:11:11:72:540:327:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:have similar impacts on the universe of students in the U.S. However, even if the RCT uses a representative sample of the target
7:197:17475:11:11:72:540:316:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:population, there are still concerns of external validity. For example, when implementing a large-scale policy, there could possibly
7:198:17607:11:11:72:540:305:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:be general equilibrium effects that a pilot RCT did not detect. Fourth, Deaton (2010) expresses many concerns about the analyses
7:199:17735:11:11:72:540:294:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:and implementations of RCTs – exploring heterogeneous treatment effects can be viewed as data-mining and researchers should
7:200:17858:11:11:72:540:283:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:explore the implications of testing a large number of hypotheses in their studies; researchers rarely use appropriate standard errors
7:201:17991:11:11:72:540:272:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:when reporting results; exploring different combinations of baseline variables to include in regressions is another potential form of
7:202:18124:11:11:72:540:261:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:data-mining; including baseline variables can lead to substantial biases in small samples; attrition from the study must be addressed;
7:203:18258:11:11:72:540:250:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:and it is not uncommon for RCTs to have implementation and operational issues that threaten the validity of the experiment. Fifth,
7:204:18388:11:11:72:540:239:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:spillover effects could lead one to misstate a program’s overall effect. The example that Rothstein and von Wachter (2016) give is
7:205:18518:11:11:72:540:228:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:a labor market program that attempts to increase the search effort of individuals in treatment. This program may lower the chances
7:206:18648:11:11:72:540:217:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:of finding jobs for the control group and thus overstate the impact of the program’s total effect.  Sixth, RCTs evaluating programs
7:207:18779:11:11:72:540:206:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:are considered “black boxes” that do not reveal the true mechanisms of interest.  Although one can use randomized admission
7:208:18902:11:11:72:540:195:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:lotteries to estimate the causal impact of pre-existing charter schools, the causal relation between specific school inputs cannot
7:209:19032:11:11:72:540:184:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:be determined from such a study.  Finally, Deaton (2010) and others argue that in an effort to overcome the above issues, RCTs
7:210:19158:11:11:72:540:173:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:can become prohibitively expensive.  Still, with these important limitations in mind, the conventional wisdom is:  if youcando a
7:211:19286:11:11:72:540:162:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:randomized field experiment, you should.  Of the above seven issues which are commonly discussed with RCTs, five of them can
7:212:19410:11:11:72:540:151:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:be sidestepped by running more, larger, and better designed RCTs. Moreover, if one designs the RCT in a way that helps validate a
7:213:19539:11:8:72:449:140:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:model of selection for observational data, then the only limitation appears to the budget of the researcher.
7:214:19647:8:14:87:539:132:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:4We consider countries as highly developed if they received a classification of “Very High Human Development” in United
7:215:19766:14:11:72:540:118:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:Nations Development Programme (2010). A country is classified as very high if they score in the top quartile on an index of human
7:216:19895:11:11:72:540:107:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:development that includes life expectancy, mean years of schooling, expected years of schooling, and gross national income per
7:217:20021:11:8:72:96:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:capita.
7:218:20028:8:14:87:540:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:5We don’t focus on mindset experiments (Miin the production function above) due to very few of these experiments passing
7:219:20148:14:0:72:298:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:the inclusion restrictions of our meta-analysis discussed below.
8:220:20213:0:20:72:239:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:pendent of the nature of the treatment.
8:221:20252:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:School-based experiments target K-12 curricula, teachers, management practices, students in classroom
8:222:20353:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:settings, principals, and other school resources.  Any experiment where the dosage is applied in a school
8:223:20458:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:setting – such as offering families vouchers to attend private schools or after-school programs – We cate-
8:224:20564:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:gorize as a school-based intervention.  Even experiments in which K-12 resources are given at home – for
8:225:20668:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:instance tutors from the school tutor students in their living rooms – We code as a school-based experi-
8:226:20772:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment.  Home-based experiments focus on parenting, income constraints, neighborhood environment, and a
8:227:20873:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student’s access to educational resources in their household. Similar to above, if an experiment takes place
8:228:20981:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:at home and focuses on these inputs, then it is considered a home-based experiment. For example, parenting
8:229:21087:20:20:72:427:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:classes that take place in a school auditorium are considered a home intervention.
8:230:21169:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:While the above categories are mutually exclusive, collectively exhaustive, and internally consistent –
8:231:21272:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:which categories to sort experiments into is a bit arbitrary. For example, in Sumi et al. (2012), both teachers
8:232:21383:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and parents received training on how to teach students replacement behaviors. This is potentially important
8:233:21490:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:because when we combine estimates within categories across the set of experiments using the DerSimonian-
8:234:21594:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Laird meta-analysis coefficient (see DerSimonian and Laird 1986) – the labels on categories become a “lazy
8:235:21700:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:man’s” way of deciding what works and what doesn’t.  If the meta-analysis coefficient for early childhood
8:236:21805:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:studies is greater than the coefficient for home studies, this is evidence that early childhood studies have a
8:237:21915:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:higher impact on average.  In an attempt to avoid interactions of the categories in our analysis, studies that
8:238:22025:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have characteristics of more than one category are excluded from our analysis (but are still included in the
8:239:22133:20:20:72:104:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tables).
8:240:22141:20:21:88:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:With these caveats in mind, the results of this inquiry are interesting and, in some cases, quite surpris-
8:241:22247:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ing.   There is substantial heterogeneity in treatment effects across and within various categories of field
8:242:22355:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments. Experiments in early childhood and schools can be particularly effective at producing human
8:243:22459:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:capital.  The random effects meta-coefficients for early childhood experiments are 0.111σ(0.031) for stan-
8:244:22565:21:20:72:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dardized math scores and 0.165σ(0.032) for reading.  The estimates for schools are 0.052σ(0.008) and
8:245:22665:20:20:72:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.068σ(0.009) for math and reading scores, respectively. Within school-based field experiments, those that
8:246:22771:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:alter the management practices of schools, or implement “high-dosage” tutoring tend to demonstrate large
8:247:22875:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effects.  Having pooled impacts in the range of 0.507-0.655σ,  the three most successful early childhood
8:248:22979:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments were the famous Ypsilanti Perry Preschool Project (Weikart et al. 1970) and evaluations of the
8:249:23085:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Breakthrough to Literacy and Ready, Set, Leap! curricula (Layzer et al. 2007). In schools, with evaluations
8:250:23192:21:20:72:539:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:producing pooled impacts ranging from 0.779-1.582σ, the most successful programs appear to be Reading
8:251:23293:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Recovery (Center et al.  1995; Schwartz 2005) and Peer-Assisted Learning Strategies (Mathes and Babyak
9:252:23396:0:20:72:100:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2001).
9:253:23402:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Interventions that attempt to lower poverty, change neighborhoods, or otherwise alter the home envi-
9:254:23502:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ronment in which children are reared have produced surprisingly consistent and precisely estimated “zero”
9:255:23607:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:results.  Avvisati et al.  (2014) show that a comprehensive parent training program in France had large be-
9:256:23714:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:havioral impacts that spilled over to students whose parents did not participate.  However, the study found
9:257:23821:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:no impacts on academic outcomes.  The famous negative income tax experiment – which provided low-
9:258:23918:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:income families with more money while incentivizing them to work less – had no impact on children’s test
9:259:24022:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores (Maynard and Murnane 1979). As with Avvisati et al. (2014) and Maynard and Murnane (1979), the
9:260:24123:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:average home or neighborhood experiment that our search returned has math and reading impacts that are
9:261:24225:20:20:72:247:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:statistically indistinguishable from zero.
9:262:24267:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The literature – all 196 randomized field experiments discovered through our search process – is sum-
9:263:24368:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:marized in a large set of tables at the end of the chapter.  This was the most laborius part of the process.
9:264:24476:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:For each study, we collected data on sample demographics, key aspects of the research design, and effect
9:265:24580:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sizes.  The typical study published in a top economics journal has this information readily available and
9:266:24685:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:collecting the data only took a few minutes.  But, some studies published in older journals, less technical
9:267:24792:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:journals, or government reports required an exhaustive search of the publication to estimate effect sizes from
9:268:24902:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the information given. The large collection of tables provide a bird’s eye view of the set of randomized field
9:269:25012:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments that have been conducted and evaluated. We include a large set of studies that vary curriculum
9:270:25118:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:choices.  These are included in the tables but not described in the text, as they don’t align with traditional
9:271:25228:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:economic choice variables in a concise way and because of the potential effects of publication bias on these
9:272:25336:20:21:72:143:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:types of studies.
9:273:25353:21:20:88:540:284:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f2:A:Second, for every randomized field experiment found, we calculated the impact (in standard deviations)
9:274:25455:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of the intervention on standardized math and reading outcomes and collected data on features of the ex-
9:275:25558:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:periment.  These data include over forty potential explanatory variables, including length of intervention,
9:276:25665:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grade/age of subjects, location, if the sample was a majority English Language Learner (ELL), disadvan-
9:277:25768:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:taged, black, Hispanic, or of low ability, and so on.  This provides us with a novel dataset to investigate
9:278:25875:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the correlation of important sample demographics and treatment effects of experiments designed to increase
9:279:25981:21:20:72:136:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:human capital.
9:280:25995:20:20:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:An important pattern that arises in the data is the correlation between effectiveness of treatment and age
9:281:26101:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of subjects at the time of intervention.  It has also been observed that some interventions tend to be more
9:282:26208:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effective at increasing math achievement relative to reading achievement (Fryer 2014; Abdulkadiroglu et al.
9:283:26315:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2011; Angrist et al.  2011; Dobbie and Fryer 2011; Hoxby and Murarka 2009; Gleason et al.  2010).  There
10:284:26420:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:are many theories that may explain the disparity in treatment effects by subject area. A leading explanation
10:285:26528:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:posits that reading scores are influenced by the language spoken when students are outside of the classroom
10:286:26635:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(Charity et al.  2004; Rickford 1999).  Charity et al.  (2004) argue that if students speak non-standard En-
10:287:26743:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:glish at home and in their communities, increasing reading scores might be especially difficult. Research in
10:288:26851:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:developmental psychology has suggested a second possibility – that the critical period for language devel-
10:289:26957:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:opment occurs early in life, while the critical period for developing higher cognitive functions extends into
10:290:27066:20:20:72:531:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:adolescence (Hopkins and Bracht 1975; Newport 1990; Pinker 1994; Nelson 2000; Knudsen et al. 2006).
10:291:27165:20:21:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Our data suggests that the age theory has merit.  In math, the treatment effect is not strongly related to
10:292:27271:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the age of the student at the time of intervention.  The correlation coefficient is 0.0679.  In stark contrast,
10:293:27382:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:early in life, many reforms increase reading performance. Later in life, very few treatments have any effect
10:294:27490:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on reading, save “high dosage” tutoring.  Put precisely – there is a negative relationship between age and
10:295:27596:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading treatment effects.   The correlation coefficient is -0.2069.   To put this number in perspective,  the
10:296:27706:20:20:72:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:average effect on reading of interventions targeting children with an average age less than 5 is 0.177σ. The
10:297:27814:20:21:72:523:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:average effect of reading interventions targeting students with an average age greater than 14 is 0.039σ.
10:298:27919:21:20:88:540:426:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f2:A:Third, We conclude this chapter by simulating a life-cycle model that enables us to make an educated
10:299:28019:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:guess about how much of racial and ethnic wage inequality in America might be accounted for if we simply
10:300:28123:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:used  the  best  practices  gleaned  from  an  exhaustive  review  of  what  works  in  the  literature.   Although  a
10:301:28241:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:majority of the randomized field trials discussed in this chapter do not report impacts on adult outcomes, we
10:302:28350:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:are able to use correlations from the National Longitudinal Survey of Youth 1979 (NLSY79) and NLSY79
10:303:28450:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Children and Young Adults (CNLSY) datasets to simulate how shocks in a given life-stage will impact
10:304:28549:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:later outcomes. Specifically, we follow the methods described in Winship and Owen (2013) and construct a
10:305:28653:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:model similar to the Social Genome Model (SGM). Using this model, we estimate that if children were given
10:306:28758:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a successful early childhood intervention and then received successful school-based interventions in mid-
10:307:28863:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:childhood and again in adolescence, one might dramatically reduce, and under some assumptions eliminate,
10:308:28967:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:wage inequality.   Obviously,  these types of educated guesses vis-a-vis simulations must be taken with a
10:309:29072:20:20:72:174:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:proverbial grain of salt.
10:310:29097:20:21:88:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The chapter proceeds as follows.  Section 2 describes our method for culling and standardizing field
10:311:29197:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments from the education literature. Section 3 describes evidence from randomized field experiments
10:312:29302:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:across  the  three  categories:  early  childhood,  home-based  interventions,  and  school-based  interventions.
10:313:29415:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Section 4 uses the estimates from the literature to simulate a life-cycle model and provide a sense of how
10:314:29521:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:much of racial wage inequality in America might be accounted for if government policy focused on the best
10:315:29626:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:practices gleaned from the literature.  Section 5 concludes.  There are 100 pages worth of Appendix Tables
11:316:29733:0:44:72:339:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that summarize the literature in a concise and consistent way.
11:317:29795:44:32:72:442:667:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:2    A Method for Finding and Evaluating Field Experiments
11:318:29853:32:20:72:540:635:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In deciding which field experiments to include in our analysis, we first culled a reasonably exhaustive list
11:319:29961:20:20:72:540:615:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of field experiments and then narrowed our focus to studies that satisfied certain criteria.   We began by
11:320:30067:20:21:72:540:595:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:searching all “quick reviews” and “single study reviews” in the What Works Clearinghouse (WWC). WWC
11:321:30166:21:20:72:540:574:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:was created by the U.S. Department of Education’s Institute of Education Sciences in 2002.   Its goal is
11:322:30270:20:20:72:540:554:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to provide reviews of education studies, policies, and interventions in order for researchers to determine
11:323:30376:20:21:72:540:534:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:“what works” in education.  Currently,  WWC has over 10,500 reviews available in an online searchable
11:324:30477:21:20:72:540:513:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:database.  Eligible studies are reviewed by a team of WWC’s certified staff against WWC standards and
11:325:30578:20:20:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assigned a rating. The highest rating of the Clearinghouse is reserved for studies that met standards without
11:326:30687:20:21:72:540:473:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reservations.  This implies that groups compared in the study were determined through a random process,
11:327:30790:21:20:72:540:452:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:there was low overall attrition from the sample, the differential attrition across groups was low, and there
11:328:30898:20:20:72:539:432:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were no confounding factors (U.S. Department of Education 2015).6Our search of WWC produced 115
11:329:30993:20:21:72:378:412:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomized field experiments that met standards without reservations.
11:330:31062:21:20:88:539:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:We augmented the WWC search by looking through recent education literature reviews (e.g.  Almond
11:331:31158:20:20:72:540:371:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Currie 2011;  Fryer 2010;  Heckman and Kautz 2013;  Nye et al.  2006;  Yeager and Walton 2011) to
11:332:31259:20:21:72:540:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ensure that all these potential studies had been included.  In most all cases, the randomized studies were
11:333:31365:21:20:72:467:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:already in the What Works Clearhinghouse, but this process produced important additions.
11:334:31453:20:20:88:539:310:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, we conducted relatively broad searches of known databases – such as ERIC, JSTOR, EconLit –
11:335:31552:20:21:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that include education papers to augment our sample of studies. In each database, we searched for all phases
11:336:31660:21:20:72:540:269:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:generated by concatenating one element from the set of strings (“early childhood”, “education”, “housing”,
11:337:31766:20:20:72:540:249:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:“neighborhood”, “parent”, “school”, “student”, “teacher”) with one element from (“experiment”, “random
11:338:31868:20:21:72:540:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assignment”, “randomization”).  For each database, we collected all hits that searching for these 24 unique
11:339:31975:21:20:72:539:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:phrases returned.7These searches provided us with over 10,000 citations to check. To conduct this laborious
11:340:32082:20:20:71:539:188:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:task, we had a team of five research assistants skim every article and select papers that explicitly mention a
11:341:32192:20:20:71:307:168:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:random process determining the experimental sample.
11:342:32243:20:27:88:539:148:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Using these approaches, we found 859 potential studies.  Table 1 describes how we narrowed our set
11:343:32341:27:14:87:539:121:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:6That is, no factor other than the intervention itself is present that all treatment students in one group are exposed to and no
11:344:32469:14:11:72:540:107:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:students in the comparison group are exposed to. If a confounding factor is present, it would be impossible to distinguish between
11:345:32599:11:8:72:272:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:the effect of the intervention and the effect of the factor.
11:346:32659:8:14:87:539:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:7JSTOR’s search algorithm occasionally returned thousands of results.  Due to resource and time constraints, we decided to
11:347:32781:14:0:72:393:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:only collect the top 200 (as determined by “relevance”) results for each phrase in JSTOR.
12:348:32871:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of  studies  from  859  to  196.   As  discussed,  we  only  included  experiments  that  had  samples  determined
12:349:32985:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:by a verifiably random process that were pre-college;  that took place in a highly developed country (as
12:350:33089:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:determined by the Human Development Index constructed by the United Nations Development Programme);
12:351:33188:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and that reported standardized reading or mathematics test scores as an outcome measure at posttest.  The
12:352:33293:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:random process is important for causal inference – though the rise of strong quasi-experimental analyses
12:353:33397:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:makes this quite restrictive. Some experiments use non-norm referenced tests designed by the experimenter
12:354:33502:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for  the  purpose  of  the  experiment.   These  evaluations  are  not  comparable  across  experiments  and  were
12:355:33616:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:omitted. In general, the restrictions are important for comparability and allow one to synthesize the estimates
12:356:33727:21:20:72:239:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from the studies in the analysis below.
12:357:33766:20:20:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Unfortunately,  these  restrictions  lead  to  us  not  including  some  influential  experimental  studies.   For
12:358:33880:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:example, our screening excluded the exploration of the impact of teacher value-added on students in Chetty
12:359:33986:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al.  (2014) because their research design is non-experimental.  Housing demolitions in Jacob (2004) and
12:360:34092:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the famous brown and blue eye experiments performed by Jane Elliot in her classrooms in the late 1960s also
12:361:34199:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:did not utilize verifiably random processes. A well-known incentive experiment in Israel (Angrist and Lavy
12:362:34305:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2009) was excluded because the main outcome was receipt of matriculation certificates.  Similarly, many
12:363:34408:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:important social-psychological, behavioral, and “mindset” experiments (e.g. Mischel et al. 1972; Cohen et
12:364:34513:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:al. 2006; Cohen et al. 2009; Wilson and Linville 1982; Aronson et al. 2002; Miyake et al. 2010; Duckworth
12:365:34618:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al. 2013) were excluded because they did not report results for standardized math or reading outcomes or
12:366:34725:20:20:72:216:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the sample was post high school.
12:367:34757:20:20:88:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:For each experiment that passed our screening, we report estimates of the annual pooled effect sizes
12:368:34857:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on reading and math outcomes, in standard deviations.  If papers did not report results in this manner, we
12:369:34963:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attempted to use the information given to calculate standardized effect sizes.  For example, if impacts were
12:370:35071:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:presented as scale score points on a test, we would divide the coefficient by the standard deviation given
12:371:35177:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the summary statistics.  The most common calculation we performed was using the average treatment
12:372:35277:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and control posttest scores (or changes between pretest and posttest) as well as the corresponding standard
12:373:35384:20:20:72:399:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:deviations to calculate the standardized difference between the two groups.
12:374:35459:20:21:88:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Specifically, we used this information to calculate a statistic known as Hedge’sgand its corresponding
12:375:35561:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:standard error (see Hedges 1981 and Lipsey and Wilson 2000). Since this measure is just the difference be-
12:376:35667:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tween the average test scores of treatment and control groups, point estimates obtained from this method are
12:377:35775:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:identical to intent-to-treat (ITT) estimates that do not include controls and use the same standard deviation
12:378:35884:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to standardize the test scores. Note that since all studies included in this paper used a random procedure to
12:379:35993:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assign treatment and control groups, point estimates from multivariable ITT regressions should not differ
13:380:36100:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:significantly from the raw differences. If possible, when necessary information for this statistic was missing
13:381:36210:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:we would make assumptions (e.g.  equal number of students assigned to treatment and control or use the
13:382:36312:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:standard deviation from the national sample of the standardized test).8If there was not enough information
13:383:36418:20:20:72:437:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:presented in the paper for us to make credible assumptions, the study was excluded.
13:384:36501:20:21:88:539:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:One common issue we encountered was the calculation of standard errors. Unfortunately, without having
13:385:36602:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:access to the micro-data, it was not possible to calculate the appropriate standard errors for every effect size.
13:386:36715:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In an attempt to not overstate the significance of an effect size, when calculating Hedge’sg, we erred on the
13:387:36824:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conservative side and used the number of units randomized to calculate the standard errors.  For example,
13:388:36929:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:although Slavin et al. (1984) had a sample of 504 students, randomization was done at the school level (N =
13:389:37036:20:44:72:84:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:6).
13:390:37039:44:32:72:363:484:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:3    Evidence from 196 Randomized Field Trials
13:391:37085:32:28:72:252:452:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.1    Early Childhood Experiments
13:392:37119:28:20:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In the past five decades there have been many field experiments designed to increase achievement before
13:393:37222:20:21:72:539:404:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:kids enter school.9Appendix Table 1 provides an overview of 44 randomized field experiments (from 24
13:394:37322:21:20:71:539:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:papers), the ages they serve, and their treatment effects on standardized math and reading outcomes. Here,
13:395:37428:20:20:71:539:363:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:we partition the literature into interventions that are early childhood center-based and others that are more
13:396:37537:20:36:71:126:343:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:home-based.
13:397:37548:36:28:71:229:307:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.1.1    Center-Based Experiments
13:398:37581:28:20:71:539:279:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Perhaps the most famous early intervention program for children involved 123 students in Ypsilanti, Michi-
13:399:37687:20:21:71:539:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:gan, who attended the Perry Preschool program in 1962 (58 were randomly assigned to treatment).  The
13:400:37787:21:20:71:539:238:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program consisted of a 2.5-hour daily preschool program and weekly home visits by teachers, and targeted
13:401:37891:20:20:71:539:218:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children from disadvantaged socioeconomic backgrounds with IQ scores in the range of 70-85.  An active
13:402:37993:20:21:71:539:198:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:learning curriculum - High/Scope - was used in the preschool program in order to support both the cognitive
13:403:38100:21:20:71:539:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and non-cognitive development of the children over the course of two years beginning when the children
13:404:38202:20:20:71:539:157:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were three years old. Schweinhart, Barnes, and Weikart (1993) find that students in the Perry Preschool pro-
13:405:38310:20:21:71:539:137:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:gram had higher test scores between the ages of 5 and 27, 21 percent less grade retention or special services
13:406:38419:21:28:71:539:116:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:required, 21 percent higher graduation rates, and half the number of lifetime arrests in comparison to chil-
13:407:38527:28:11:87:520:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:8We documented all assumptions that were made for each study and these can be obtained from the author upon request.
13:408:38643:11:0:87:404:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:9See Carneiro and Heckman (2003) or Almond and Currie (2010) for extensive reviews.
14:409:38728:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dren in the control group.  Considering the financial benefits that are associated with the positive outcomes
14:410:38837:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of the Perry Preschool, Heckman et al. (2010) estimated that the rate of return on the program is between 7
14:411:38944:21:20:72:324:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and 10 percent, passing a traditional cost-benefit analysis.
14:412:39004:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Although an influential experiment, Heckman et al.  (2009) argues that the randomization protocol for
14:413:39105:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the Perry Preschool experiment was compromised.  Post-randomization,  some children initially assigned
14:414:39207:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to treatment whose parents were employed were swapped with control children whose parents were un-
14:415:39305:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:employed.  The researchers’ rationale for this swap was that employed mothers would find it difficult to
14:416:39409:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:participate  in  the  home  visits  that  treatment  families  received.   Heckman  et  al.   (2010)  investigates  the
14:417:39528:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:implications of these swaps and other potential issues with previously reported Perry results. Even after ac-
14:418:39637:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:counting for the compromised randomization (by correcting for the imbalance in preprogram variables and
14:419:39740:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:matching students), multiple-hypothesis testing, and small sample sizes of the original analysis, Heckman
14:420:39845:21:20:72:384:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al. (2010) still find statistically and economically significant impacts.
14:421:39921:20:20:88:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another important center-based intervention, which was initiated three years after the Perry Preschool
14:422:40023:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program is Head Start. Head Start is a preschool program funded by federal matching grants that is designed
14:423:40130:21:20:72:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to serve 3- to 5-year-old children living at or below the federal poverty level.10The program varies across
14:424:40237:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:states in terms of the scope of services provided, with some centers providing full-day programs and others
14:425:40344:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:only half-day.  In 2007, Head Start served over 900,000 children at an average annual cost of about $7,300
14:426:40450:21:20:72:113:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:per child.
14:427:40460:20:20:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Evaluations of Head Start have often been difficult to perform due to the typical non-random nature
14:428:40559:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of  enrollment  in  the  program.11Puma  et  al.   (2010),  in  response  to  the  1998  reauthorization  of  Head
14:429:40673:20:21:72:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Start, conduct an evaluation using randomized admission into Head Start.12The impact of being offered
14:430:40774:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:admission into Head Start for 3- and 4-year-olds is 0.10 to 0.34 standard deviations in the areas of early
14:431:40880:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:language and literacy. For 3-year-olds, there were also small positive effects in the social-emotional domain
14:432:40989:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(0.13 to 0.18 standard deviations) and on overall health status (0.12 standard deviations).  Yet, by the time
14:433:41098:21:25:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the children who received Head Start services had completed first grade, almost all of the positive impact on
14:434:41207:25:14:84:539:198:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:10Local Head Start agencies are able to extend coverage to those meeting other eligibility criteria, such as those with disabilities
14:435:41339:14:8:72:423:184:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:and those whose families report income between 100 and 130 percent of the federal poverty level.
14:436:41435:8:14:84:539:176:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:11Currie and Thomas (1995) use a national sample of children and compare children who attended a Head Start program with
14:437:41555:14:11:72:540:162:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:siblings who did not attend Head Start, based on the assumption that examining effects within the family unit will reduce selection
14:438:41686:11:11:72:540:151:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:bias. They find that those children who attended Head Start scored higher on preschool vocabulary tests but that for black students,
14:439:41818:11:11:72:540:140:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:these gains were lost by age ten.  Using the same analysis method with updated data, Garces et al.  (2002) find several positive
14:440:41946:11:11:72:540:129:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:outcomes associated with Head Start attendance. They conclude that there is a positive effect from Head Start on the probability of
14:441:42077:11:11:72:540:118:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:attending college and - for whites - the probability of graduating from high school.  For black children, Head Start led to a lower
14:442:42208:11:8:72:302:107:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:likelihood of being arrested or charged with a crime later in life.
14:443:42275:8:14:84:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:12Students not chosen by lottery to participate in Head Start were not precluded from attending other high-quality early child-
14:444:42402:14:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:hood centers.  Roughly ninety percent of the treatment sample and forty-three percent of the control sample attended center-based
14:445:42531:11:0:72:89:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:care.
15:446:42538:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:initial school readiness had faded. The only remaining impacts in the cognitive domain are a 0.08 standard
15:447:42644:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:deviation increase in oral comprehension for 3-year-old participants and a 0.09 standard deviation increase
15:448:42751:21:20:72:378:670:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:in receptive vocabulary for the 4-year-old cohort (Puma et al. 2010).13
15:449:42822:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Other early childhood interventions – many based on the early success of Perry Preschool and Head Start
15:450:42925:20:21:71:539:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:– include the Abecedarian Project, the Early Training Project, the Milwaukee Project, and Tulsa’s universal
15:451:43032:21:20:71:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:pre-kindergarten program. The Abecedarian Project provided full-time, high-quality center-based childcare
15:452:43137:20:20:71:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:services for four cohorts of children from low-income families from infancy through age five between 1971
15:453:43242:20:21:71:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and 1977.  Campbell and Ramey (1994) find that at age 12, those children who were randomly assigned
15:454:43341:21:20:71:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to the project scored 5 points higher on the Wechsler Intelligence Scale and 5-7 points higher on various
15:455:43446:20:36:71:431:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:subscales of the Woodcock-Johnson Psycho-Educational Battery achievement test.
15:456:43524:36:28:71:225:492:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.1.2    Home-Based Experiments
15:457:43555:28:20:71:539:464:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The most well known home-based field experiment in the early childhood years is the Nurse-Family Part-
15:458:43657:20:21:71:539:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:nership. Through this program, low-income first-time mothers received home visits from a registered nurse
15:459:43762:21:20:71:539:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:beginning early in the pregnancy and continued until the child is two years old – a total of fifty visits over the
15:460:43876:20:20:71:539:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:first two years. The program aimed to encourage preventive health practices, reduce risky health behaviors,
15:461:43983:20:21:71:539:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:foster positive parenting practices, and improve the economic self-sufficiency of the family.  In a study of
15:462:44091:21:20:71:539:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the program in Denver in 1994-95, Olds et al. (2002) found that those children whose mothers had received
15:463:44196:20:20:71:539:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:home visits from nurses (but not those who received home visits from paraprofessionals) were less likely
15:464:44300:20:20:71:539:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to display language delays and had superior mental development at age two.  In a long-term evaluation of
15:465:44404:20:21:71:539:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the program, Olds et al. (1998) found that children born to women who received nurse home visits between
15:466:44508:21:20:71:539:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:1978 and 1980 had fewer juvenile arrests, convictions, and violations of probation by age fifteen than those
15:467:44616:20:20:71:258:261:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:whose mothers had not received treatment.
15:468:44657:20:21:88:539:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The Early Training Project provided children from low-income homes with summertime experiences
15:469:44751:21:20:71:539:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and weekly home visits during the three summers before entering first grade in an attempt to improve the
15:470:44855:20:20:71:539:200:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children’s school readiness.  Gray and Klaus (1970) report that children who received these intervention
15:471:44959:20:21:71:539:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:services maintained higher Stanford-Binet IQ scores (2-5 points) at the end of fourth grade.   The Infant
15:472:45064:21:20:71:539:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Health and Development Program specifically targeted families with low-birth-weight preterm infants and
15:473:45167:20:20:71:539:139:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:provided them with weekly home visits during the child’s first year and biweekly visits through age three,
15:474:45273:20:31:71:539:119:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:as well as enhanced early childhood educational care and bimonthly parent group meetings. Brooks-Gunn,
15:475:45375:31:14:84:539:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:13The Early Head Start program, established in 1995 to provide community-based supplemental services to low-income families
15:476:45498:14:0:72:411:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:with infants and toddlers, had similar effects (Administration for Children and Families 2006).
16:477:45595:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Liaw, and Klebanov (1992) report that this program had positive effects on language development at the
16:478:45697:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:end of first grade, with participant children scoring 0.09 standard deviations higher on receptive vocabulary
16:479:45806:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and 0.08 standard deviations higher on oral comprehension. The Milwaukee Project targeted newborns born
16:480:45909:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to women with IQs lower than 80;  mothers received education,  vocational rehabilitation,  and child care
16:481:46014:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:training while their children received high-quality educational programming and three balanced meals daily
16:482:46120:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:at “infant stimulation centers” for seven hours a day, five days a week until the children were six years old.
16:483:46230:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Garber (1988) finds that this program resulted in an increase of 23 points on the Stanford-Binet IQ test at
16:484:46337:20:21:72:332:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:age six for treatment children compared to control children.
16:485:46397:21:20:88:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Although the above parenting programs have shown promise, they are not widely accessible due to the
16:486:46496:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:time demands they place on parents and high implementation costs.  York and Loeb (2014) investigate the
16:487:46599:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impact of READY4K!, a low-cost text message program that targets parents of preschoolers. The program
16:488:46700:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:helps these parents support their children’s literacy development by sending parents three text messages
16:489:46804:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:per week for an entire school year.  These texts were designed to provide parents with information on the
16:490:46909:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:importance of their children developing particular skills, tips on how to support their children’s development
16:491:47019:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in a cost-effective manner, and encouragement. York and Loeb (2014) recruited parents from 31 preschool
16:492:47122:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sites run by the San Francisco Unified School District’s Early Education Department.  Of the 874 eligible
16:493:47227:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:families, 440 enrolled and were randomly assigned to treatment group that participated in READY4K! or a
16:494:47330:21:20:72:134:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control group.
16:495:47344:20:20:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:At the end of the school year, York and Loeb (2014) collected survey responses from parents and teachers
16:496:47448:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to investigate the intervention’s impact on parental involvement. They found that treatment parents engaged
16:497:47555:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in literacy activities at home with their child 0.22 to 0.34 standard deviations more than control parents and
16:498:47665:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were 0.13 to 0.19 standard deviations more involved at preschool.  To investigate the impact the interven-
16:499:47771:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tion had on children’s literacy development, York and Loeb (2014) collected scores from the Phonological
16:500:47875:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Awareness Literacy Screening (PALS), a criterion-referenced test the school district administers to its early
16:501:47984:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:education students every spring.14They found that children in treatment families score 0.344 standard devi-
16:502:48091:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ations higher on the letter sounds subtest and 0.205 standard deviations higher on a measure of lower-case
16:503:48197:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:alphabet knowledge.  However, there were no significant impacts on measures of name writing, upper-case
16:504:48300:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:letter knowledge, beginning word sounds, print and word awareness, rhyme awareness, and a summed score
16:505:48402:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of all the PALS subtests. For the sample of students that progressed to higher level subtests of PALS, there
16:506:48510:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were significant impacts on the upper-case letter subtest and the summed score. There was limited evidence
16:507:48616:21:24:72:380:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that READY4K! had differential impacts across family characteristics.
16:508:48685:24:0:84:539:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:14Note that since this study did not report results from a norm-referenced outcome, it was not included in our tables and analysis.
17:509:48818:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Fryer, Levitt, and List (2015) conducted a parental incentive experiment in Chicago Heights – a proto-
17:510:48920:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:typical low performing urban school district – by starting a parent academy that distributed nearly $1 million
17:511:49030:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to 257 families (these numbers include treatment and control). There were two treatment groups, which dif-
17:512:49136:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fered only in when families were rewarded, and a control group.  Parents in the two treatment groups were
17:513:49241:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:paid for attendance at Parent Academy sessions which were designed as information sessions to aid parents
17:514:49346:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in educating their children, proof of homework completion, and the performance of their children on bench-
17:515:49452:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mark assessments. The only difference between the two treatment groups is that parents in one group were
17:516:49556:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:paid in cash or via direct deposits (hereafter the “cash” condition) and parents in the second group received
17:517:49665:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the majority of their incentive payments via deposits into a trust account which can only be accessed if and
17:518:49773:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:when the child enrolls in college (the “college” incentive condition).   Eleven project managers and staff
17:519:49879:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:worked together to ensure that parents understood the particulars of the treatment; that the parent academy
17:520:49986:21:20:72:528:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program was implemented with high fidelity; and that payments were distributed on time and accurately.
17:521:50088:20:20:88:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Across the entire sample, the impact on cognitive test scores of being offered a chance to participate in
17:522:50193:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the parental incentive is 0.119σ(with a standard error of 0.094). These estimates are non-trivial, but smaller
17:523:50303:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in magnitude than some classroom based interventions. For instance, the impact of Head Start on test scores
17:524:50410:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:is approximately 0.145σ. The impact of the Perry Preschool intervention on achievement at 14 years old is
17:525:50515:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.203σ. Given the imprecision of the estimates, however, our results are statistically indistinguishable both
17:526:50624:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from these programs and from zero.  The impact of the “college” and “cash” incentive schemes are nearly
17:527:50727:20:20:72:112:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:identical.
17:528:50737:20:20:88:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Fryer,  Levitt,  and  List  (2015)  report  that  the  impact  of  being  offered  a  chance  to  participate  in  our
17:529:50855:20:21:72:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:parental  incentive  scheme  on  non-cognitive  skills  is  large  and  statistically  significant  (0.203σ(0.083)).
17:530:50971:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:These results are consistent with Kautz et al.  (2014), who argue that parental investment is an important
17:531:51077:20:20:72:537:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:contributor to non-cognitive development. Again, the “cash” and “college” schemes yield identical results.
17:532:51183:20:21:88:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:They complement our main statistical analysis by estimating heterogeneous treatment effects across a
17:533:51283:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:variety of pre-determined subsamples that we blocked on experimentally.  Two stark patterns appear in the
17:534:51388:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:data.  The first pattern is along racial lines:  Hispanics (48 percent of the sample) and whites (8 percent of
17:535:51498:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the sample) demonstrate large and significant increases in both cognitive and non-cognitive domains.  For
17:536:51603:21:20:72:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:instance, the impact of the parent academy for Hispanic children is 0.367σ(0.133) on our cognitive score
17:537:51707:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:B:and 0.428σ(0.122) on our non-cognitive score. Among the small sample of whites, the impacts are 0.932σ
17:538:51809:20:21:72:539:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(0.353) on cognitive and 0.821σ(0.181) on non-cognitive.  The identical estimates for blacks are actually
17:539:51914:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:negative but statistically insignificant on both cognitive and non-cognitive dimensions:−0.234σ(0.134)
17:540:52016:20:0:71:539:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and−0.059σ(0.129), respectively.  Importantly, p-values on the differences between races are statistically
18:541:52124:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:significant at conventional levels.  We explore a range of possible hypotheses regarding the source of the
18:542:52230:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:racial differences (extent of engagement with the program, demographics, English proficiency, pre-treatment
18:543:52337:21:20:72:394:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores), but none provide a convincing explanation of the complete effect.
18:544:52411:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The second pattern of heterogeneity in treatment that we observe in the data relates to pre-treatment test
18:545:52517:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores. Students who enter our program below the median on non-cognitive skills see no benefits from our
18:546:52621:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:intervention in either the cognitive or non-cognitive domain. In stark contrast, students who enter our parent
18:547:52731:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:academy  above  the  median  in  non-cognitive  skills  experience  treatment  effects  of  roughly  0.3  standard
18:548:52845:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:deviations on both cognitive and non-cognitive dimensions.  If we segment children by both cognitive and
18:549:52949:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:non-cognitive pre-treatment scores,  the greatest gains are made on both the cognitive and non-cognitive
18:550:53053:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dimension by students who start the program above the median on non-cognitive skills and below the median
18:551:53158:20:37:72:154:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on cognitive skills.
18:552:53178:37:27:72:172:471:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.1.3    Meta-Analysis
