18:553:53200:27:21:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Early  childhood  interventions  have  amassed  considerable  popular  and  political  support.   Yet,  like  other
18:554:53315:21:20:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:initiatives to improve human capital, they are not a panacea.  For example, St.  Pierre et al.  (1997) find no
18:555:53425:20:20:72:540:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:positive effects in a national evaluation of the Comprehensive Child Development Program (CCDP). The
18:556:53525:20:21:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:CCDP delivers early and comprehensive services to low-income families with the aim of enhancing the
18:557:53624:21:20:72:540:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:development of the children in these families and helping the parents achieve economic self-sufficiency.
18:558:53728:20:20:72:540:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The CCDP model revolves around the ideas that one should intervene as early as possible in children’s lives,
18:559:53836:20:20:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:involve the entire family in an intervention, deliver comprehensive services to address the needs of young
18:560:53942:20:21:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children, enhance parents’ ability to contribute to their child’s development, help parents achieve economic
18:561:54050:21:20:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and social self-sufficiency, and ensure that families have access to all of these resources until their children
18:562:54162:20:20:72:540:261:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:enter elementary school. In their evaluation, St. Pierre et al. (1997) found no significant differences between
18:563:54273:20:21:72:540:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:families that were randomly assigned to a CCDP treatment group or a control group. CCDP had no impacts
18:564:54375:21:20:72:540:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on measures of mothers’ economic self-sufficiency or their parenting skills and CCDP had no effects on the
18:565:54481:20:20:72:419:200:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cognitive or social emotional development of the children included in the study.
18:566:54561:20:21:88:539:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Still, early childhood investments are considered to be one of the least risky ways to increase academic
18:567:54665:21:20:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement (Heckman 2008).  Combining the 44 randomized studies in early childhood over the past 50
18:568:54765:20:20:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years,  the  random  effects  coefficients  are  0.111σ(0.031)  for  math  interventions  and  0.189σ(0.027)  for
18:569:54878:20:21:71:539:119:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading.  Of the 64 treatment effects recorded in these randomized studies, 21 were statistically positive;
18:570:54985:21:21:71:448:98:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:zero were statistically negative and 43 were statistically indistinguishable from zero.15
18:571:55074:21:0:84:468:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:15We consider an effect size statistically positive or negative if it is statistically significant at the 10% level.
19:572:55192:0:28:72:199:711:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.2    Home Environment
19:573:55215:28:20:72:540:683:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:There is an ongoing debate as to whether efficient production of human capital should focus on improving
19:574:55319:20:20:72:540:663:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the environment in which a child lives or the environment in which they learn.  Proponents of the school-
19:575:55424:20:21:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:centered  approach  refer  to  anecdotes  of  excellence  in  particular  schools  or  examples  of  other  countries
19:576:55541:21:20:72:540:622:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:where poor children in superior schools outperform average Americans (Chenoweth 2007).  Advocates of
19:577:55641:20:20:72:540:602:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the community-focused approach argue that teachers and school administrators are dealing with issues that
19:578:55746:20:21:72:540:582:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:originate outside the classroom, citing research that shows racial and socioeconomic achievement gaps are
19:579:55851:21:20:72:540:561:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:formed before children ever enter school (Fryer and Levitt 2004; 2006), that mother’s IQ is highly correlated
19:580:55960:20:20:72:540:541:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with child achievement (Fryer and Levitt 2013; Wilson and Matheny 1983; Yeates et al. 1983) and that one-
19:581:56065:20:21:72:540:521:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:third to one-half of the racial achievement gap can be explained by family-environment indicators (Phillips
19:582:56172:21:20:72:540:500:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al.  1998; Fryer and Levitt 2004).  In this scenario, combating poverty and having more constructive out-
19:583:56280:20:20:72:540:480:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of-school time may lead to better and more-focused instruction in school.  Indeed, Coleman et al.  (1966),
19:584:56386:20:21:72:540:460:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in their famous report on the equality of educational opportunity, argue that schools alone cannot treat the
19:585:56494:21:20:72:315:439:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:problem of chronic underachievement in urban schools.
19:586:56547:20:20:88:539:419:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In this subsection, we describe several attempts to provide households with more resources and to com-
19:587:56649:20:21:72:540:399:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:bat poverty,  in an effort to increase student achievement.   We organize this strand of literature in rough
19:588:56757:21:20:72:540:378:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:approximation to the “intensity” of treatment received – which ranges from providing parents with infor-
19:589:56861:20:20:72:540:358:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mation to poverty reduction though welfare-to-work programs and tax reform to moving families to better
19:590:56964:20:36:72:363:338:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:neighborhoods. The literature is summarized in Appendix Table 2.
19:591:57028:36:28:72:205:302:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.2.1    Parental Involvement
19:592:57057:28:20:72:540:274:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Parents matter. Using data from a national, cross-sectional study of children aged 8-12, Davis-Kean (2005)
19:593:57163:20:21:72:540:254:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:found significant correlations between parents’ characteristics and parenting practices and students’ math
19:594:57269:21:20:72:540:233:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and reading achievement.   Specifically,  Davis-Kean (2005) found that strong correlations with students’
19:595:57374:20:20:72:540:213:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement existed for parents’ education levels, income, parental expectations, number of books owned,
19:596:57478:20:21:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and many parental behaviors such as being warm and affectionate, responding positively, and giving praise.
19:597:57584:21:20:72:540:172:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Jeynes (2005) conducts a meta-analysis of 41 studies that investigate the impact of parental involvement on
19:598:57691:20:20:72:540:152:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the academic achievement of elementary students.  He found that increases in parental involvement have
19:599:57793:20:21:72:540:132:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:an effect size on elementary students’ academic outcomes of about 0.7 standard deviations.  Jeynes (2007)
19:600:57898:21:20:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conducts a similar meta-analysis using 52 studies that focus on secondary school students and finds the
19:601:58001:20:0:72:372:91:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effect size of parent involvement to be about 0.5 standard deviations.
20:602:58073:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Although these results are interesting, they are are not causal estimates of the impact of parental involve-
20:603:58181:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment on students’ outcomes. Levels of parental involvement are most likely correlated with many observable
20:604:58287:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and unobservable characteristics of the parents and it is exceedingly difficult to rid these estimates of thorny
20:605:58399:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:issues of selection.  Moreover, even if these estimates were causal, it is not obvious that it is possible for
20:606:58509:20:21:72:499:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:interventions to change parents’ involvement to achieve these positive impacts on child outcomes.
20:607:58606:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In what follows,  we summarize the literature on experiments to increase parental involvement using
20:608:58705:20:32:72:283:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:information treatments and incentive treatments.
20:609:58753:32:21:72:152:557:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:A. INFORMATION
20:610:58767:21:20:88:539:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To better understand the impact of parental attitudes and school involvement on student achievement,
20:611:58867:20:20:72:540:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Avvisati et al. (2014) conducted an experimental study on middle school students and parents in the educa-
20:612:58973:20:21:72:540:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tional district of Creteil, an eastern suburb of Paris, France. Classrooms randomly selected from 34 middle
20:613:59080:21:20:72:540:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools were offered a parental education program that taught parents how they can assist in their child’s
20:614:59186:20:20:72:160:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:educational process.
20:615:59206:20:21:88:539:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:This paper was motivated by a strong perception that disadvantaged parents have inadequate knowledge
20:616:59306:21:20:72:540:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and  confidence  to  be  effective  advocates  for  their  children.   The  experiment  sought  to  test  if  this  could
20:617:59427:20:20:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:be improved by a simple intervention.  The experimental program consisted of three afterschool meetings
20:618:59530:20:20:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with parents, conducted by the school head.  The first two sessions focused on how parents can help their
20:619:59635:20:21:72:540:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children’s education by participating at home and at school.  The final session, which took place after the
20:620:59742:21:20:72:540:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:end-of-term report card, focused on how parents can adapt to their children’s first term results.  Of the 352
20:621:59851:20:20:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:state-run middle schools in the Creteil district, 34 schools volunteered to participate in the program. Around
20:622:59961:20:21:72:540:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:two-thirds of schools in the study were “priority education”, a label indicating a historically disadvantaged
20:623:60070:21:20:72:93:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:area.
20:624:60075:20:20:88:539:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Parents of 6th graders in the participating middle schools were asked,  over a 6-week period,  if they
20:625:60177:20:21:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:would like to sign up for the informational meetings.  After the sign-up period closed, the list of registered
20:626:60287:21:20:72:540:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:families constituted the “volunteer families,” creating two populations within each class in each school.
20:627:60392:20:20:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:There were no strong observable pre-treatment differences between volunteer and non-volunteer families.
20:628:60495:20:21:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:After registration closed, randomization began at the class-level of each school (meaning that roughly half
20:629:60602:21:20:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of all classes were treated within each school).  The randomization process defined four basic groups of
20:630:60706:20:20:72:540:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:families within each school: volunteers in treatment classes, non-volunteers in treatment classes, volunteers
20:631:60815:20:21:72:317:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in control classes, and non-volunteers in control classes.
20:632:60873:21:0:88:539:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The study was interested in addressing three outcomes:  (1) parental involvement attitudes and behav-
21:633:60976:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ior; (2) children’s behavior as reflected by truancy, disciplinary record and work effort; and (3) children’s
21:634:61085:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:academic results.   To measure parental involvement attitudes and behavior,  all families received a ques-
21:635:61191:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tionnaire on school-based involvement,  home-based involvement,  and parents’ perception of the school.
21:636:61294:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Student outcomes were reported by teachers and academic reports. Main subject teachers were also given a
21:637:61398:20:21:72:458:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:questionnaire regarding both parental attitudes and child’s behavior/school performance.
21:638:61486:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The evidence found that the program was successful in significantly improving volunteer parent atti-
21:639:61586:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tudes.  Based on parents’ and teachers’ questionnaires, parental involvement by volunteer parents in treat-
21:640:61693:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment classes increased. Children of volunteer parents in treatment classes saw a vast improvement in school
21:641:61800:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attitudes and discipline compared to control classes: truancy was lower by 1.1 half-days, treatment students
21:642:61908:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were 4.6 percentage points less likely to be punished for disciplinary reasons (6.4% versus 11.0%), more
21:643:62012:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:likely to earn top marks for conduct, and, according to teacher questionnaire answers, were more likely to
21:644:62118:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:be agreeable in class and work diligently.  In addition to having a direct impact on the students whose par-
21:645:62226:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ents volunteered to participate, there were also spillover effects on students in treatment classrooms whose
21:646:62334:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:parents did not participate.  Treatment had a statistically significant impact on non-volunteer students’ ab-
21:647:62443:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:senteeism, probability of disciplinary sanctions, and marks for conduct.  For students of volunteer parents,
21:648:62551:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment increased average grades across all subjects by 0.08 standard deviations and increased academic
21:649:62656:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:performance as measured by the teacher survey.  However, the intervention had no impact on grades for
21:650:62757:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students whose parents did not volunteer and the intervention had no impacts on standardized test scores for
21:651:62865:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:any students. The findings overall suggested that parental involvement can be a significant input in student
21:652:62973:20:20:72:359:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement—mostly through an impact on behavioral outcomes.
21:653:63033:20:21:88:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Evidence from Avvisati et al.  (2014) and other studies suggest that it may be difficult to increase stu-
21:654:63138:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dents’ academic outcomes using parental interventions. Other parental experiments that focus on improving
21:655:63243:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students’ academic outcomes through parental tutoring also tend to have insignificant impacts on academic
21:656:63348:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:standardized measures (Warren 2009; Powell-Smith et al.  2000; Fantuzzo et al.  1995; Hirst 1972; Ryan
21:657:63450:21:20:72:100:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:1964).
21:658:63456:20:20:88:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:On  average,  parental  information  experiments  increased  student  achievement  by  -0.001σ(0.021)  on
21:659:63561:20:21:72:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math scores and 0.034σ(0.050) on reading scores. Note that our search did not return any parental incentive
21:660:63668:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments that focused solely on parents of K-12 students. Therefore, the estimates from our meta-analysis
21:661:63776:20:32:72:349:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for parental involvement and parental information are identical.
21:662:63840:32:21:72:143:110:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:B. INCENTIVES
21:663:63853:21:0:88:539:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The most well-known and well-analyzed incentive program for parents is PROGRESA. PROGRESA
22:664:63944:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:was an experiment conducted in Mexico in 1998, which provided cash incentives linked to health, nutrition
22:665:64049:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and education. The largest component of PROGRESA was linked to school attendance and enrollment. The
22:666:64149:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program provided cash payments to mothers in targeted households to keep their children in school (Skoufias
22:667:64256:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2005).  Programs based on the PROGRESA model have been replicated in New York City, Nicaragua, and
22:668:64354:20:21:72:118:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Columbia.
22:669:64363:21:20:88:542:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Beginning in 1997, the Mexican government identified 506 rural communities on the basis of a “marginal-
22:670:64466:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ity  index” gleaned from census  data.   Socio-economic data was collected from  households within these
22:671:64570:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:communities to target households living in extreme poverty.  In 1998, about two thirds of the identified lo-
22:672:64678:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:calities were randomly selected to receive financial incentives under PROGRESA; the remaining localities
22:673:64782:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:served as controls.  As a part of the program, households could receive up to $62.50 per month if children
22:674:64888:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attended school regularly. The amount of incentive was higher for older children who had to attend 85% of
22:675:64993:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:all school days. The average amount of incentives received by any treatment household in the first two years
22:676:65101:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of treatment was $34.80, which was 21% of an average household’s income.  Besides school attendance,
22:677:65201:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:PROGRESA also emphasized actual student achievement by making a child ineligible for the program if
22:678:65300:21:20:72:351:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:she failed a grade more than once (Skoufias 2005; Slavin 2010).
22:679:65363:20:20:88:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Schultz (2000) reports that PROGRESA had a positive impact on school enrollment for both boys and
22:680:65460:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:girls in primary and secondary school.  For primary school children, PROGRESA increased school enroll-
22:681:65562:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment for boys by 1.1 percentage points and 1.5 percentage points for girls from a baseline level of approxi-
22:682:65670:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mately 90 percent. For secondary school students, enrollment increased by 7.2 to 9.3 percentage points for
22:683:65776:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:boys and 3.5 to 5.8 percentage points for girls, from a baseline level of approximately 70%. The author also
22:684:65884:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reports that PROGRESA had an accumulated effect of 0.66 years additional schooling for a student from
22:685:65985:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the average poor household. Taking the baseline level of schooling at face value, PROGRESA’s 0.66 years
22:686:66088:20:20:72:395:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:accumulated effect translates into a 10% increase in schooling attainment.
22:687:66162:20:21:88:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Behrman, Sengupta, and Todd (2001) also analyze the data and report that PROGRESA children entered
22:688:66260:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school at an earlier age, had less grade repetition and better grade progression. Treatment children also had
22:689:66369:20:20:72:492:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:lower dropout rates and once dropped out, they had a higher chance of re-entry into high school.
22:690:66465:20:21:88:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Opportunity NYC – based on PROGRESA – was an experimental conditional cash transfer program that
22:691:66561:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:was conducted in New York City. The program had three components: the Family Rewards component that
22:692:66660:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:gave incentives for to parents to fulfill responsibilities towards their children; the Work Rewards component
22:693:66769:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that  gave  incentives  for  families  to  work;  and  the  Spark  component  that  gave  incentives  to  students  to
22:694:66887:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increase achievement scores in classes. The program began in August 2007 and ended in August 2010 (see
22:695:66989:20:0:72:192:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Morais de S ́a e Silva 2008).
23:696:67020:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Riccio et al., 2013 analyze data from the Family Rewards component of the program during the first two
23:697:67122:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years of treatment.  Their analysis is based on 4,800 families with 11,000 children out of which half were
23:698:67228:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assigned to treatment and the other half to control.  Opportunity NYC spent $8,700 per family in treatment
23:699:67334:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:over three years. The experiment had an insignificant impact on every school outcome measured (Riccio et
23:700:67438:20:37:72:114:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:al. 2013).
23:701:67448:37:27:72:241:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.2.2    Home Educational Resources
23:702:67483:27:21:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Education,  like  other  industries,  has  evolved  over  the  past  few  decades  –  due,  in  part,  to  technological
23:703:67603:21:20:72:540:545:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:change. With the introduction of computers, the internet, mobile wifi, and smart phones, teaching strategies
23:704:67711:20:20:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have changed to utilize these technologies in the classroom.  However, many children still lack access to
23:705:67816:20:21:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:these resources in their homes.  One could imagine that the returns to household computers are quite high.
23:706:67922:21:20:72:540:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Students  can  use  them  as  a  tool  to  efficiently  complete  assignments,  learn  new  information,  study,  and
23:707:68039:20:20:72:540:464:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:use for other educational purposes.  Despite these potential returns, it is also possible that households face
23:708:68149:20:21:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:constraints (e.g.  credit or information) that prevent them from investing in household technology.  This is
23:709:68257:21:20:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:supported by the fact that ownership of household computers and access to household internet is correlated
23:710:68363:20:20:72:540:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with income (National Telecommunication and Information Administration 2011).  Studies examining the
23:711:68463:20:21:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impact of home computers on poor families using observational or quasi-experimental data have generated
23:712:68566:21:20:72:540:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mixed results.  Some studies find large positive effects (Attewell and Battle 1999;  Fiorini 2010;  Schmitt
23:713:68673:20:20:72:540:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Wadsworth 2006; Fairlie 2005; Fairlie, Beltran and Das 2010; Malamud and Pop-Eleches 2011) and
23:714:68771:20:20:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:some find evidence of small or even negative impacts (Fuchs and Woessmann 2004; Vigdor and Ladd 2010;
23:715:68872:20:21:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Malamud and Pop-Eleches 2011).  Fairlie and Robinson (2013) present causal estimates from the first ever
23:716:68976:21:20:72:420:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomized control experiment that investigates the impact of home computers.
23:717:69053:20:20:88:539:261:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In their experiment, Fairlie and Robinson investigate the educational impacts of randomly giving home
23:718:69154:20:21:72:540:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:computers to 1,123 students in grades 6 through 10 in California over the 2008-2009 and 2009-2010 school
23:719:69258:21:20:72:540:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years.  No students who participated in the study had home computers at baseline.  Half of these students
23:720:69363:20:20:72:540:200:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were randomly selected to receive free computers without any training or technological assistance.  Fairlie
23:721:69470:20:21:72:540:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Robinson collected administrative data on student academic outcomes and demographics pretreatment
23:722:69571:21:20:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and at the end of the school year (posttreatment).  In addition, they conducted baseline and posttreatment
23:723:69677:20:20:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:surveys that included questions about computer usage,  knowledge,  homework time,  and other important
23:724:69779:20:21:72:540:119:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes.  Using this data, Fairlie and Robinson found that the experiment had large first-stage impacts.
23:725:69884:21:20:72:540:98:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:They found that treatment students were 55 percentage points more likely to have a computer at follow-up,
23:726:69989:20:0:72:540:78:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:25 percentage points more likely to have Internet service, they reported using a computer 2.5 hours more
24:727:70095:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:per week than control students’ average of 4.2 hours, and almost all of this additional usage came from a
24:728:70200:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:computer at home. However, not all of the computer usage was for educational purposes. Relative to control
24:729:70306:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students, treatment students used computers 0.80 hours more per week for schoolwork (control mean (CM)
24:730:70408:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:was 1.89 hours), 0.42 hours more for e-mail (CM = 0.25 hours), 0.80 hours more for games (CM = 0.84
24:731:70507:20:21:72:378:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:hours), and 0.57 hours more for social networking (CM = 0.57 hours).
24:732:70575:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Despite these large first-stage impacts, Fairlie and Robinson find minimal evidence for impacts on ed-
24:733:70677:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ucational outcomes.  ITT estimates for the impact of home computers on grades in math, English/reading,
24:734:70780:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:social studies, and science classes are all close to zero and precisely estimated. With standard errors of ap-
24:735:70890:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:proximately 0.04, they can rule out effect sizes on the scale of one-fourth of the difference between a “B+”
24:736:70998:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:or “B” with 95 percent confidence. Using quantile regressions, they show that these null effects exist across
24:737:71107:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the entire posttreatment achievement distribution.  Similarly, they find no evidence of impact on students’
24:738:71214:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:test scores or proficiency statuses from the California Standardized Testing and Reporting (STAR) program,
24:739:71320:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:total credits taken in the third quarter of the school year, total credits in the fourth quarter, unexcused ab-
24:740:71431:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sences,  number of tardies,  and if a student was still enrolled at the end of the school year.   These zero
24:741:71539:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effects are consistent with survey results that show treatment students did not change intermediate inputs
24:742:71645:20:20:72:523:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and outcomes such as school effort, computer knowledge, and usage of important educational software.
24:743:71745:20:21:88:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:There are other randomized field experiments that investigate the impact of providing additional re-
24:744:71845:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sources to families – such as giving students books to read during the summer.  Numerous studies suggest
24:745:71949:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that summer vacation is a critical time for forming and widening achievement gaps in reading, particularly
24:746:72055:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for the income-achievement gap.16Kim (2005) conducted an experimental study to examine the causal ef-
24:747:72156:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fects of a voluntary summer reading intervention on the reading skills of fourth-grade students in the Lake
24:748:72263:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:County Public School District, a large multi-ethnic school district located in a mid-Atlantic state.  The dis-
24:749:72373:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:trict contains more than 100 elementary schools and is therefore organized into small subdistricts, each with
24:750:72482:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:its own superintendent. To be included in the sample, the subdistrict needed to contain high-poverty schools
24:751:72590:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that administered Title I school-wide programs and contain multi-racial schools in which reading scores
24:752:72693:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for black and Latino students contributed to the federal adequate yearly progress rating.  The final sample
24:753:72800:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:included four Title I schools and the six non-Title I schools with the largest percentage of minority students.
24:754:72911:21:20:88:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:This paper was motivated by inefficiencies in current voluntary reading policies and the little evidence
24:755:73015:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in support of these programs.  Additionally, finding a cost-effective reading intervention was important for
24:756:73123:20:23:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:policymakers and practitioners given the goals of federal education policy and mandates under the No Child
24:757:73229:23:14:84:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:16See Heyns (1978), Cooper et al.  (1996), Alexander et al.  (2001), Broh (2004), Heyns (1987), Klibanoff & Haggart (1981),
24:758:73352:14:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:Murnane (1975), and Phillips et al. (1998). Fryer and Levitt (2004) is a notable example of a nationally representative sample that
24:759:73483:11:0:72:189:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:does not find “summer setback”.
25:760:73516:0:20:72:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Left  Behind  Act.17The  intervention  addressed  three  main  factors  –  access  to  books,  students’  reading
25:761:73629:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:levels, and students’ reading preferences – that are likely to shape opportunities to read in the summer and
25:762:73737:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:affect reading outcomes.  To increase access to books, each student in the treatment group received eight
25:763:73842:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:free books to read during the summer.  Students’ reading levels were based on performance on the reading
25:764:73946:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:section of the Iowa Test of Basic Skills and preferences were obtained through a survey distributed before
25:765:74052:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the summer.  A text-leveling system, the Lexile Framework, was used to provide books that were within
25:766:74153:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:each student’s independent reading level using information about each student’s reading level and reading
25:767:74258:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:preferences. With each book, students also received a postcard that asked students to check comprehension
25:768:74363:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:strategies used while reading the book and to obtain a signature from a parent or family member after reading
25:769:74472:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a portion of the book aloud to the adult.  Parents were instructed to mail each postcard back to the schools,
25:770:74581:20:21:72:314:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:regardless of if their student completed the book or not.
25:771:74638:21:20:88:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:A total of 552 students received consent to participate in the study and took pretests in June 2005. These
25:772:74744:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students were randomly assigned to treatment and control groups (282 treatment and 270 control) within
25:773:74846:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their English Language Arts (ELA) classroom, and the author reports no statistically significant differences
25:774:74954:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:between the two groups at the beginning of the experiment on numerous demographic and achievement
25:775:75051:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:characteristics. Because of attrition, the final sample included 486 students (252 treatment and 234 control)
25:776:75160:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:at the beginning of the Fall in 2005.   The intervention attempts to improve reading skills by increasing
25:777:75265:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children’s access to books, matching books to children’s reading levels and preferences, and encouraging
25:778:75369:20:20:72:349:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children to read orally with a parent/family member to practice.
25:779:75433:20:20:88:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To investigate if the intervention increased children’s access to books at home and literacy-related activ-
25:780:75540:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ities during summer vacation, the author used a two-way ANOVA on both self-reported measures of book
25:781:75640:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ownership and on literacy habits gathered from a survey conducted at the end of the summer.  The results
25:782:75744:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:suggest that the intervention did not increase children’s access to books nor the amount of silent reading.
25:783:75851:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:However,  children  in  the  treatment  group  reported  significantly  more  oral-reading  at  home  with  family
25:784:75965:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:members than the control group children.  For fall reading outcomes, ITT regressions showed no signifi-
25:785:76068:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cant differences between the treatment and control groups on a grade level measure of oral-reading fluency.
25:786:76175:20:21:72:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:However, treatment had a 0.08σ(0.04) impact on students’ standardized reading test scores and there were
25:787:76279:21:20:72:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:differential effects by race. Treatment increased test scores by 0.22σ(0.09) for black students, 0.14σ(0.08)
25:788:76387:20:20:72:539:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for Latino students, and 0.17σ(0.11) for Asian students. Further, the magnitude of the treatment effect was
25:789:76494:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:largest among lower performing students, and there were no significant interactions between the treatment
25:790:76599:21:24:72:309:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and measures of reading ability or ownership of books
25:791:76652:24:0:84:490:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:17Note that the No Child Left Behind Act was superseded by the Every Student Succeeds Act in December 2015.
26:792:76761:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Similarly, Allington et al.  (2010) conducted a randomized trial in 17 high-poverty schools in Florida
26:793:76863:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:where treatment students selected 12 books from a book fair to receive for summer reading. Allington et al.
26:794:76970:21:32:72:439:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(2010) found a 0.046σ(0.033) annual impact over the three years of the experiment.
26:795:77052:32:20:88:540:638:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The meta-coefficients for home educational resource experiment were -0.060σ(0.050) for math scores
26:796:77150:20:37:72:239:618:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and 0.015σ(0.014) for reading scores.
26:797:77187:37:27:72:253:581:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.2.3    Poverty Reduction Experiments
26:798:77225:27:21:72:540:554:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:One of the most often articulated explanations for the racial and ethnic achievement gaps that exist across
26:799:77332:21:20:72:540:533:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:developed countries is poverty.  For families with higher income, it is easier to provide their children with
26:800:77441:20:20:72:540:513:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:resources and raise them in environments that are conducive for learning. Poverty places constraints on key
26:801:77548:20:21:72:540:493:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:factors of achievement such as health care, nutrition, child care, in-home educational resources, safe neigh-
26:802:77657:21:20:72:540:472:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:borhoods, good schools, and college education (Brooks-Gunn and Duncan 1997; Evans 2004; Magnuson
26:803:77753:20:20:72:540:452:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Duncan 2002; McLoyd 1998).  In America, 42 percent of black children and 37 percent of Hispanic
26:804:77852:20:20:72:540:432:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children experience poverty while only 10 percent of white children are exposed to these hardships (Duncan
26:805:77958:20:21:72:540:412:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Magnuson 2005).  Studies suggest that this racial income gap is an important source of variation that
26:806:78063:21:20:72:540:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:can account for large proportions of raw racial achievement gaps (Duncan and Magnuson 2005; Fryer and
26:807:78164:20:20:72:331:371:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Levitt 2004; Phillips et al. 1998; Brooks-Gunn et al. 2003).
26:808:78224:20:21:88:539:351:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:This subsection discusses the impact on student achievement of experiments that attempted to reduce
26:809:78323:21:32:72:280:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:poverty through tax reform and work programs.
26:810:78368:32:20:72:149:298:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:A. TAXREFORM
26:811:78380:20:21:88:539:278:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Maynard and Murnane (1979) discuss two mechanisms by which welfare reform could affect children’s
26:812:78477:21:20:72:540:257:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:educational achievement by altering home environment: product inputs and time inputs. Product inputs are
26:813:78581:20:20:72:540:237:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:things such as food, health care, and books.  Examples of time inputs are time parents spend talking to,
26:814:78685:20:21:72:540:217:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:playing with, and reading to their children. They assume that product inputs are positively related to family
26:815:78794:21:20:72:540:196:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:income and that time inputs are positively related to time not working.  Maynard and Murnane investigate
26:816:78898:20:20:72:540:176:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the educational impacts of a program that affects both of these mechanisms in unison by increasing families’
26:817:79006:20:21:72:262:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:income and incentivizing them not to work.
26:818:79048:21:20:88:539:135:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In the early 1970s, the Gary Income Maintenance Experiment was conducted by Indiana University un-
26:819:79146:20:20:72:540:115:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:der contracts with the U.S. Department of Health, Education, and Welfare and the Indiana State Department
26:820:79251:20:21:72:540:95:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of Public Welfare.  Families who voluntarily enrolled and had at least one child under the age of 18 were
26:821:79356:21:0:72:540:74:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomly assigned to negative income tax conditions or control.  Of the 1,799 eligible families, 57 percent
27:822:79465:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were assigned to one of four negative income tax plans for three years. These tax plans were a combination
27:823:79571:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of two tax rates (40 or 60 percent) and two guaranteed income levels (about three fourths of the poverty level
27:824:79681:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:or equal to the poverty level). The lower guarantee level was about $1,000 a year more than the support level
27:825:79790:20:20:72:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of the Indiana Aid to Families with Dependent Children program.18The tax rate is the amount by which the
27:826:79894:20:21:71:445:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:negative income tax payment is reduced for each dollar of income that a family earns.
27:827:79979:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The sample for the Gary Income Maintenance Experiment was not nationally representative.  All chil-
27:828:80078:20:20:71:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dren were black and three-fifths of them lived in female-headed households. In addition, the average family
27:829:80185:20:21:71:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had a much lower income compared to the national average (the average annual income of families in the
27:830:80287:21:20:71:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Gary experiment was only $5,200 and the national average at that time was $9,433) and over 40 percent of
27:831:80391:20:20:71:301:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the Gary families were living below the poverty line.
27:832:80444:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Maynard and Murnane investigate the impact of a Gary family’s assignment to any one of the treatment
27:833:80544:21:20:71:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:arms on educational outcomes of students in grades 4-10 at the end of the experiments (three years after
27:834:80648:20:20:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomization).   They  found  that treatment increased  students’ standardized reading  test  scores  by 0.23
27:835:80758:20:21:71:539:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:standard deviations on the Iowa Test of Basic Skills in grades 4-6 but had no significant impact for students
27:836:80867:21:20:71:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in grades 7 -10. They found no evidence that treatment had an effect on grade point average of the younger
27:837:80973:20:20:71:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students, but found that it significantly decreased grade point average for the older students. They also found
27:838:81084:20:21:71:505:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:no evidence that treatment had an impact on the number of days absent for either group of students.
27:839:81183:21:20:88:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To better understand these results, Maynard and Murnane also investigate the mechanisms by which the
27:840:81283:20:20:71:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiment might have affected school performance.  They found that the Gary experiment had a signifi-
27:841:81385:20:20:71:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cant first stage impact on total family income, but caused minimal change in the number of hours worked.
27:842:81489:20:21:71:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Treatment families on average had their incomes increased by $2,000 per year (approximately a 50 percent
27:843:81593:21:20:71:539:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increase).  For married mothers, there was no change in hours worked per week.  For female family heads,
27:844:81697:20:20:71:539:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:there was a decrease of about two hours per week.  Additionally, experimental families that lived in public
27:845:81804:20:21:71:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:housing before randomization were more likely to move to private dwellings than control families that lived
27:846:81911:21:20:71:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in public housing prior to randomization.  However, there was no statistical difference in mobility in the
27:847:82017:20:29:71:137:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:pooled sample.
27:848:82031:29:20:72:172:174:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:B. WORKPROGRAMS
27:849:82046:20:21:88:539:154:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Michalopoulos et al.  (2002) evaluated another poverty reduction program, called the Self-Sufficiency
27:850:82147:21:20:71:539:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Project (SSP), that attempted to make work more appealing than welfare to long-time welfare recipients in
27:851:82252:20:20:71:539:113:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the Canadian provinces of British Columbia and New Brunswick by providing them with wage subsidies.
27:852:82351:20:16:71:539:93:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:New Brunswick is located in eastern Canada and is bordered by the U.S. state of Maine on it’s western
27:853:82452:16:0:84:379:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:18In 1972, the official poverty level for a four-person non-farm family was $4,275.
28:854:82537:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:boundary. New Brunswick has a population of 750,000, a majority of its inhabitants speak English as their
28:855:82642:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:first language, and has a per capita GDP of 42,600 Canadian dollars. British Columbia is located in western
28:856:82749:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Canada and is bordered by the U.S. states of Alaska, Washington, Idaho, and Montana.  British Columbia
28:857:82851:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:has a population of 4,400,000, an official language of English, and a per capita GDP of 47,500 Canadian
28:858:82954:20:21:72:112:630:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:dollars.19
28:859:82964:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The study randomly assigned 6,000 single parents from British Columbia and New Brunswick,  who
28:860:83058:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had been on income assistance for at least one year, to a treatment and control group.  Treatment parents
28:861:83163:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were eligible to participate in SSP and control parents were not. Parents enrolled in SSP received a monthly
28:862:83271:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:earnings supplement conditional on starting a full-time job and leaving income assistance.  The earnings
28:863:83375:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:supplement was in addition to earnings from employment for up three years, as long as the parent continued
28:864:83481:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to be employed full-time and remained off of income assistance. After random assignment, treatment parents
28:865:83587:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had one year to find full-time employment (at least 30 hours per week) and leave income assistance to enroll
28:866:83695:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in  SSP.  After  enrollment,  the  supplement  participants  received  was  half  of  the  difference  between  their
28:867:83812:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:earnings and an earnings benchmark (the benchmark varied by location and year, but was $30,000 in New
28:868:83913:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Brunswick and $37,000 in British Columbia for the first year of the experiment). This supplement was not
28:869:84017:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:affected by unearned income, earnings of other family members, and number of children. This supplement
28:870:84119:20:21:72:346:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:would essentially double the wage of many low-wage workers.
28:871:84178:21:20:88:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Michalopoulos et al.  (2002) found significant first-stage impacts.  Thirty-six percent of single parents
28:872:84283:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that were offered participation found full-time employment and took-up the supplement during the year
28:873:84384:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:long eligibility window. Of those that participated in SSP, the average parent received the supplement for 22
28:874:84493:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:months over the three years of the program and received more than $18,000 in supplements over that that
28:875:84596:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:time.  SSP increased treatment parents’ probability of employment throughout the duration of the program
28:876:84700:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and reduced income assistance payments received by these families.  As a result, treatment parents earned
28:877:84805:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:nearly $3,400 more than control members.  Total income (supplements, earnings, and income assistance)
28:878:84906:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increased by $6,300 for the average treatment family.  These impacts reduced the proportion of treatment
28:879:85010:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:parents below Canada’s low income cut-offs by 10 percentage points.  Although these large impacts were
28:880:85112:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:observed during the program, these impacts did not persist after the completion of SSP. By six years af-
28:881:85216:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ter random assignment (two years after all treatment parents would have stopped receiving supplements),
28:882:85319:20:20:72:504:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment and control parents were equally likely to be employed and had similar average earnings.
28:883:85417:20:21:88:539:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Michalopoulos et al. (2002) also investigated the impact of SSP on the outcomes of the parents’ children.
28:884:85522:21:24:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:They found differential treatment effects by the age of the child at the beginning of treatment. For children
28:885:85631:24:0:84:352:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:19Statistics come from the 2011 Canadian census (Statistics Canada 2013).
29:886:85706:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:who were 1 or 2 years old at the time of random assignment, SSP had no effects on their performance on
29:887:85808:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a standardized test of vocabulary skills (Peabody Picture Vocabulary Test) and achievement as reported by
29:888:85913:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:parents.  For children who were 3 or 4, SSP increased students’ scores on a math skills test and parental-
29:889:86019:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reported achievement. Treatment children who were 13, 14, or 15 at the time of random assignment reported
29:890:86124:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:doing worse in school and committing more minor acts of delinquency during the program, but these effects
29:891:86229:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:faded away after parents were no longer eligible for the supplement.  Finally, for older adolescents, SSP
29:892:86334:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had no impacts on educational, crime, or work related outcomes, but these students were significantly more
29:893:86440:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:likely to have babies.  Other than the effects stated above for the young adolescents, there was no evidence
29:894:86548:21:20:72:514:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of SSP having any impacts on health, behavior, and the emotional well-being of students in the study.
29:895:86649:20:20:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In a large analysis of welfare-to-work programs in the U.S., Hamilton et al.  (2001) conduct a national
29:896:86752:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:evaluation of the long-term effects of 11 welfare-to-work programs on the recipients and their children. The
29:897:86860:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:evaluation investigates the effectiveness of two different types of pre-employment strategies, Labor Force
29:898:86966:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Attachment (LFA) and Human Capital Development (HCD). LFA welfare-to-work programs typically con-
29:899:87063:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sist of short-term job search and encourage welfare participants to find employment quickly. HCD programs
29:900:87168:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:emphasize investment in longer-term skills and typically encourage participants to enroll in training or basic
29:901:87278:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:education programs. Hamilton et al. (2001) use data on over 40,000 single parents (mostly female) and their
29:902:87385:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children who were randomly assigned to these programs in sites across the nation to investigate the impact
29:903:87491:21:20:72:192:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of LFA and HCD programs
29:904:87514:20:20:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Over the course of the five-year follow-up period, a majority of control group members worked at some
29:905:87615:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:point.  For example, 88 percent of the control parents from the Grand Rapids site were employed at some
29:906:87718:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:point.   In  Oklahoma  City,  79  percent  worked  at  some  point  during  that  time  and  66  percent  worked  in
29:907:87834:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Riverside. Although there was a high percentage of control parents that ever worked, treatment parents still
29:908:87942:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:worked during more calendar quarters on average than control parents in 9 of 11 programs. Similarly, in 9 of
29:909:88050:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:11 programs, treatment parents on average had higher total earnings. Typically, Hamilton et al. (2001) found
29:910:88158:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that employment-focused programs produced employment and earnings effects almost immediately while
29:911:88256:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:education focused programs did not have effects until a year or more after randomization.  However, when
29:912:88360:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:directly comparing the LFA and HCD programs in the sites where they were run side by side, employment
29:913:88461:21:20:72:318:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and earnings levels over the five years were very similar.
29:914:88519:20:20:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:By the end of the follow-up period,  almost all control families were off of welfare and the average
29:915:88619:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control group member remained on assistance for only 2 to 3 years.  However, both treatment types still
29:916:88722:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reduced months on welfare relative to the control averages and there is some evidence that LFA treatment
29:917:88826:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:members left welfare assistance at a faster pace than HCD participants.  These reductions in welfare usage
30:918:88934:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:appear to directly offset the increase in salary. Despite increasing earnings, treatment largely had no impact
30:919:89044:20:21:72:535:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on total combined income (earnings, welfare and Food Stamp payments, and Earned Income Tax Credits).
30:920:89144:21:20:88:539:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Hamilton et al.  (2001) also investigate if the welfare-to-work programs had effects on family circum-
30:921:89246:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:stances and children’s well-being.  They found that there was no evidence of impacts on health care cover-
30:922:89352:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:age, marriage rates, and few impacts on household composition and living arrangements.  However, adults
30:923:89455:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assigned to a welfare-to-work program were less likely to report recent physical abuse at the end of the
30:924:89559:20:20:72:124:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiment.
30:925:89570:20:21:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To investigate impacts on children,  the researchers conducted a Child Outcomes Study in six of the
30:926:89669:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:programs (three different sites that each offered LFA and HCD programs).  These studies included almost
30:927:89772:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:50 measures of children’s academic functioning, health, social skills, and behavior for children who were
30:928:89877:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:preschool  age  at  randomization.   The  authors  report  that  15  percent  of  these  tests  produced  statistically
30:929:89996:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:significant differences, but the sign and magnitudes were rarely consistent across sites.  For example, the
30:930:90103:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:estimates from the Atlanta LFA and HCD programs suggested favorable impacts on social skills and be-
30:931:90203:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:havior for young children, but the Grand Rapids programs revealed negative effects. For older children, the
30:932:90310:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:programs led to few significant results. However, whenever results for these students were significant, they
30:933:90418:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tended to be unfavorable.  For example, a HCD program at one site increased the likelihood of dropping
30:934:90520:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:out, increased percentage of adolescents who had a physical, emotional, or mental condition that impeded
30:935:90624:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their mother’s ability to go to work, and increased teenage pregnancies among families with lower levels of
30:936:90731:20:32:72:514:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:education. Note again that no effects varied consistently by program approach or site for adolescents.
30:937:90833:32:20:88:539:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Summarizing the literature on poverty reduction attempts to increase student achievement, the meta-
30:938:90932:20:21:72:540:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:coefficients for this strand of literature are 0.008σ(0.029) and 0.016σ(0.024).  And, perhaps more telling,
30:939:91039:21:36:72:543:272:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:there is not one experiment that generates statistically significant positive effects on standardized test scores.20
30:940:91155:36:28:71:208:236:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.2.4    Neighborhood Quality
30:941:91184:28:20:71:539:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:A more nuanced version of the “poverty is first-order” argument is that the mechanism by which disad-
30:942:91285:20:20:71:539:188:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:vantage affects achievement is not directly through income – hence, addressing the income problem has no
30:943:91389:20:21:71:539:168:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:real impact – but through what sociologists refer to as “a culture of poverty.” This theory argues that the
30:944:91496:21:20:71:539:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:poor are not simply lacking resources, but are also immersed in a culture that develops mechanisms or has
30:945:91601:20:20:71:539:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:social institutions that perpetuate poverty (Moynihan 1969; Harrignton 1982). Taking the culture of poverty
30:946:91708:20:30:71:539:107:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:paradigm at face value, the randomized field experiment that one would ideally conduct would be to move
30:947:91811:30:0:84:527:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:20However, note that some of these studies found impacts for sub samples of the participants or on non-cognitive outcomes.
31:948:91935:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:families from high-poverty to low-poverty neighborhoods – particularly when children are young.  This is
31:949:92039:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:precisely what the Moving to Opportunity (MTO) randomized housing mobility experiment did – one of the
31:950:92141:21:20:72:289:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:most pathbreaking experiments of our generation.
31:951:92189:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:From 1994 to 1998, MTO enrolled 4,604 poor families with children residing in public housing in high-
31:952:92290:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:poverty neighborhoods of Baltimore, Boston, Chicago, Los Angeles, and New York City.  Families were
31:953:92389:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomly assigned to three groups: (1) the experimental voucher group, which received a restricted housing
31:954:92495:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:voucher that could be used to pay for private rental housing initially restricted to be in a low-poverty area
31:955:92604:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(a census tract with under a 10 percent poverty rate in 1990) and some housing-mobility counseling; (2) the
31:956:92711:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Section-8 only voucher group, which received regular Section 8 housing vouchers with no MTO relocation
31:957:92813:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:constraint; and (3) a control group, which received no assistance through MTO. Across the MTO treatment
31:958:92916:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sites, 61 percent of household heads were non-Hispanic blacks, 31 percent were Hispanic, and nearly all
31:959:93019:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:households were female-headed at baseline. About half of the experimental voucher group and 63 percent of
31:960:93124:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the Section 8-only voucher group were able to obtain leases and move with an MTO voucher (the compliance
31:961:93228:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:rate).  The MTO families were tracked for 15 years using administrative data as well as major interim (4
31:962:93332:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to 7 years after random assignment) and long-term (10 to 15 years after random assignment) follow-up
31:963:93432:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:surveys and analyses (Kling, Liebman, and Katz 2007; Sanbonmatsu et al. 2011). MTO generated large and
31:964:93534:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:persistent improvements in residential neighborhoods for the treatment groups (especially the experimental
31:965:93640:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:voucher group) relative to the control group but only modest changes in school quality.  The average MTO
31:966:93744:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:family lived at baseline in a neighborhood with a 53 percent poverty rate. MTO led to a 9 percentage point
31:967:93850:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:decline in the duration-weighted average tract poverty rate over the 10-15 year follow-up period for the
31:968:93954:20:21:72:321:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experimental voucher group relative to the control group.
31:969:94011:21:20:88:539:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In stark contrast, MTO only modestly improved school quality for the MTO treatment groups.  From
31:970:94107:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the time of random assignment until the long-term follow-up, the experimental voucher group children at-
31:971:94211:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tended schools that outperformed their control group peers by only 3 percentile points on state exams, and
31:972:94317:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the Section-8 only voucher group children attended schools that performed just 1 percentile point higher.
31:973:94422:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:MTO treatment group students also typically remained in schools where the majority of the students were
31:974:94525:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:low-income and minority.  MTO reduced the share of students eligible for free or reduced-price lunch by
31:975:94628:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:4 percentage points for the experimental voucher group.  Although it is difficult to compare the size of the
31:976:94736:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:neighborhood quality change to that of the school quality change, MTO appears to have a larger improve-
31:977:94839:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment on neighborhood quality. The MTO treatment groups experienced more than twice as large a reduction
31:978:94942:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the share of poor residential peers as compared to poor school peers and more than three times as large an
31:979:95051:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:improvement in percentile rank in the national Census-tract poverty distribution for their neighborhoods than
32:980:95162:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the state test score distribution for their schools. Many of the MTO movers remained in the same school
32:981:95268:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:districts and very similar schools. MTO also had no significant impact on adult economic self-sufficiency or
32:982:95376:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:family income at the interim or long-run follow-ups. Thus, an analysis of the impacts of MTO treatments on
32:983:95482:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:child outcomes comes close to getting at the pure effects of changes in home and neighborhood conditions
32:984:95586:20:21:72:535:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for disadvantaged kids (with little change in schools or family economic resources):∂Y∂Hin our framework.
32:985:95691:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The MTO voucher treatments did not detectably impact parent’s economic outcomes, but they did sig-
32:986:95789:20:20:71:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:nificantly and persistently improve key aspects of mother’s (adult female’s) mental and physical health in-
32:987:95896:20:21:71:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cluding substantial reductions in psychological distress, extreme obesity, and diabetes (Ludwig et al. 2011;
32:988:96004:21:20:71:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Sanbonmatsu et al.  2011).  MTO movers also experienced significant increases in adult subjective well-
32:989:96107:20:20:71:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:being with larger gains for adults from sites where treatment induced larger reductions in neighborhood
32:990:96210:20:21:71:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:poverty (Ludwig et al. 2012). For female youth, MTO treatments similarly led to persistent and significant
32:991:96316:21:20:71:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:improvements in mental health (including substantial reductions in psychological distress) and marginally
32:992:96421:20:20:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:significant improvements in physical health, but there were no long-term detectable health impacts for male
32:993:96528:20:21:71:539:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:youth (Kling, Liebman and Katz 2007; Sanbonmatsu et al. 2011). Analyses 4 to 7 and 10 to 15 years after
32:994:96631:21:20:71:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomization found that MTO produced no sustained improvements in academic achievement, educational
32:995:96731:20:20:71:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attainment, risky behaviors, or labor market outcomes for either female or male children, including those
32:996:96836:20:21:71:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:who were below school age at the time of random assignment.  Interestingly though, using administrative
32:997:96939:21:20:71:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:data from tax returns through 2012, Chetty et al. (2016) show that the Moving to Opportunity experiment has
32:998:97046:20:20:71:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had large impacts on early-adulthood outcomes for children who were younger than 13 years old at random-
32:999:97150:20:20:71:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ization.  In their mid-twenties, these individuals have 31% higher incomes, have higher college attendance
32:1000:97256:20:21:71:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:rates, are less likely to be single parents, and live in better neighborhoods relative to similar individuals in
32:1001:97368:21:20:71:539:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the control group.  For children who were older than 13 years old at randomization, MTO had no positive
32:1002:97471:20:20:71:153:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:long-term impacts.
32:1003:97489:20:21:88:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The MTO findings imply that large improvements in neighborhood conditions for poor families (at least
32:1004:97590:21:20:71:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the range feasible with Section 8 housing vouchers) alone do not produce noticeable gains in children’s
32:1005:97696:20:20:71:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:short-term socioeconomic and educational outcomes but can have substantial impacts on important long-
32:1006:97797:20:21:71:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:term outcomes for children who were exposed to these environment changes before the age of 13.   The
32:1007:97897:21:20:71:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:lack of school quality changes induced by treatment are suggestive of a key role for schools in children’s
32:1008:98003:20:0:71:305:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:short-term educational outcomes and risky behaviors.
33:1009:98057:0:28:72:172:711:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.2.5    Meta-Analysis
33:1010:98079:28:20:72:540:683:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:B:Combining all the randomized studies for home environment, the random effects coefficients are -0.004σ
33:1011:98181:20:20:72:539:663:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(0.008) for math interventions and 0.010σ(0.007) for reading. Astonishingly, the only study that had a sta-
33:1012:98288:20:21:72:540:643:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tistically positive pooled impact was an unpublished dissertation. These results show that interventions that
33:1013:98397:21:20:72:540:622:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:directly impact parents and households have struggled to have immediate effects on students’ achievement
33:1014:98501:20:37:72:117:602:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes.
33:1015:98510:37:28:72:343:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:C:3.3    Randomized Field Experiments in K-12 Schools
33:1016:98561:28:20:72:540:537:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Thus far, the literature suggests that early childhood experiments yield strong effects, but policies designed
33:1017:98671:20:20:72:540:517:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to reduce poverty, increase work opportunities, or increase neighborhood quality do little to effect the pro-
33:1018:98780:20:21:72:540:497:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:duction of human capital of school children.  In this section, we explore 105 randomized field experiments
33:1019:98886:21:20:72:414:476:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conducted in K-12 schools. The literature is summarized in Appendix Table 3.
33:1020:98962:20:20:88:539:456:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:We categorize experiments into four buckets:  student-based interventions, teacher-based interventions,
33:1021:99065:20:36:72:296:436:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:management reforms, and “market-based” reforms.
33:1022:99112:36:40:72:238:400:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.3.1    Student-Based Interventions
33:1023:99148:40:20:72:199:360:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:A. FINANCIALINCENTIVES
33:1024:99170:20:21:88:539:340:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Perhaps the most natural way to increase human capital production – at least to an economist – is to
33:1025:99270:21:20:72:540:319:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:change  the  incentives  of  school  children  to  exert  effort.   Of  course,  rational  agents  –  even  little  ones  –
33:1026:99393:20:20:72:540:299:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:internalize the returns to education that accrue in the labor market.  Yet, if agents discount the future or are
33:1027:99505:20:21:72:540:279:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:otherwise “boundedly rational”, individual effort may be below the optimum.  Financial incentives offer a
33:1028:99610:21:20:72:300:258:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:chance to bridge the gap and thereby increase effort.
33:1029:99663:20:20:88:539:238:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:There is a nascent but growing body of scholarship on the role of incentives in primary, secondary, and
33:1030:99766:20:21:72:540:218:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:post-secondary education around the globe (Angrist et al.  2002; Angrist and Lavy 2009; Kremer, Miguel,
33:1031:99869:21:20:72:540:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Thornton 2009;  Behrman, Sengupta, and Todd 2005;  Angrist, Bettinger, and Kremer 2006;  Angrist,
33:1032:99970:20:20:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Lang, and Oreopoulos 2009;  Fryer 2011;  Fryer and Holden 2013;  Barrera-Osorio et al.  2011;  Bettinger
33:1033:100074:20:33:72:502:157:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2012; Hahn, Leavitt, and Aaron 1994; Jackson 2010). We describe a subset of the literature below.
33:1034:100171:33:20:72:203:124:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Incentives in Primary Schools
33:1035:100200:20:20:88:539:104:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Psychologists argue that children understand the concept of money as a medium of exchange at a very
33:1036:100299:20:0:72:540:84:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:young age (Marshall and MacGruder 1960), but the use of financial incentives to motivate primary school
34:1037:100404:0:20:72:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students is exceedingly rare.21Bettinger (2012), who evaluates a pay-for-performance program for students
34:1038:100509:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in grades three through six in Coshocton, Ohio, is one notable exception. Coshocton is ninety-four percent
34:1039:100615:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:white and fifty-five percent free/reduced-price lunch. Students in grades three through six took achievement
34:1040:100723:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tests in five different subjects: math, reading, writing, science, and social studies.  Bettinger (2012) reports
34:1041:100835:20:21:72:539:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a 0.13σincrease in math scores and no significant effects on reading, social science, or science.  Pooling
34:1042:100941:21:20:72:249:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:subjects produces an insignificant effect.
34:1043:100983:20:20:88:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Fryer (2011) and Fryer and Holden (2013) also describe student financial incentive experiments that
34:1044:101082:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:target primary students that were conducted during the 2007-2008 and 2010-2011 school year in Dallas and
34:1045:101186:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Houston, respectively.  In Dallas, Fryer (2011) paid second graders $2 per book to read and pass a short
34:1046:101290:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:computer-based comprehension quiz on the book in Accelerated Reader (AR), a software program that has
34:1047:101391:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:quizzes for 80,000 trade books, all major reading textbooks, and leading children’s magazines.  Students
34:1048:101495:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were allowed to select and read books of their choice at the appropriate reading level and at their leisure,
34:1049:101603:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:not as a classroom assignment.  The books came from the existing stock available at their school (in the
34:1050:101707:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:library or in the classroom).  To reduce the possibility of cheating, quizzes were taken in the library on a
34:1051:101815:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:computer and students were only allowed one chance to take a quiz.  Data on the number of books read
34:1052:101915:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for students in control schools in Dallas was not available because control schools did not have consistent
34:1053:102022:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:access to (AR). In total, the experiment distributed $42,800 (21,400 quizzes passed) to 1,777 children across
34:1054:102131:21:20:72:181:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the 21 treatment schools.
34:1055:102156:20:20:88:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Paying students to read books yielded a treatment effect of 0.012σ(0.069) in reading and 0.079σ(0.086)
34:1056:102258:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in math.  The key result from this analysis emerges when one partitions students in Dallas into two groups
34:1057:102364:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:based on whether they took the exam administered to students in bilingual classes (Logramos) or the exam
34:1058:102468:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:administered to students in regular classes (Iowa Test of Basic Skills). Splitting the data in this way reveals
34:1059:102579:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:B:that there is a 0.173σ(0.069) increase in reading achievement among English speaking students and a 0.118σ
34:1060:102685:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(0.104) decrease in reading achievement among students in bilingual classes. When we aggregate the results
34:1061:102791:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in our main analysis this heterogeneity cancels itself out.  Similarly, the treatment effect for students who
34:1062:102900:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:are not English Language Learners is 0.221σ(0.068) and -0.164σ(0.095) for students who are English
34:1063:102998:20:21:72:159:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Language Learners.
34:1064:103016:21:20:88:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Fryer and Holden (2013) conducted a randomized field experiment in fifty traditionally low-performing
34:1065:103117:20:32:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:public schools in Houston, Texas – providing financial incentives to fifth grade students, their parents, and
34:1066:103226:32:14:84:539:110:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:21The use of non-financial incentives – gold stars,  aromatic stickers,  certificates,  and so on – are a more common form of
34:1067:103351:14:11:72:540:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:incentive for young children.   Perhaps the most famous national incentive program is the Pizza Hut Book It!   Program which
34:1068:103475:11:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:provides one-topping personal pan pizzas for student readers.  This program has been in existence for 25 years, but never credibly
34:1069:103605:11:0:72:108:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:evaluated.
35:1070:103617:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their teachers in twenty-five treatment schools. Students received $2 per math objective mastered in Accel-
35:1071:103724:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:erated Math (AM), a software program that provides practice and assessment of leveled math objectives to
35:1072:103828:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:complement a primary math curriculum. Students practice AM objectives independently or with assistance
35:1073:103930:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on paper worksheets that are scored electronically and verify mastery by taking a computerized test indepen-
35:1074:104038:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dently at school. Parents also received $2 for each objective their child mastered and $20 per parent-teacher
35:1075:104147:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conference attended to discuss their student’s math performance. Teachers earned $6 for each parent-teacher
35:1076:104254:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conference held and up to $10,100 in performance bonuses for student achievement on standardized tests. In
