35:1077:104360:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:total, the experiment distributed $51,358 to 46 teachers, $430,986 to 1,821 parents, and $393,038 to 1,734
35:1078:104466:21:20:72:250:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students across the 25 treatment schools.
35:1079:104507:20:20:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The experimental results raise a number of questions.  On outcomes for which direct incentives were
35:1080:104606:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:provided, there were very large and statistically significant treatment effects. Students in treatment schools
35:1081:104716:21:20:72:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mastered 1.087σ(0.031) more math objectives than control students.  On average, treatment parents at-
35:1082:104817:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tended almost twice as many parent-teacher conferences as control group parents.  And, perhaps most im-
35:1083:104920:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:portant, these behaviors translated into a 0.081σ(0.025) increase in math achievement on Texas’s statewide
35:1084:105026:21:20:71:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student assessment.  The impact of our incentive scheme on reading achievement (which was not incen-
35:1085:105126:20:20:71:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tivized) is -0.077σ(0.027), however, offsetting the positive math effect.  These results are consistent with
35:1086:105234:20:21:71:424:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the classic multitasking and job design work of Holmstrom and Milgrom (1991).
35:1087:105311:21:20:88:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Interestingly,  there is significant heterogeneity in treatment effects as a function of pretreatment test
35:1088:105417:20:20:71:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores.  Higher-achieving students (measured from pretreatment test scores) master 1.66σmore objectives,
35:1089:105521:20:20:71:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have parents who attend two more parent-teacher conferences, have 0.228σhigher standardized math test
35:1090:105622:20:21:71:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores and equal reading scores relative to high-achieving students in control schools.  Conversely, lower-
35:1091:105729:21:20:71:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achieving students master 0.686σmore objectives, have parents who attend 1.5 more parent-teacher con-
35:1092:105830:20:20:71:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ferences, have equal math test scores and 0.165σlowerreading scores.  Put differently, higher-achieving
35:1093:105933:20:21:71:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students put in significant effort and were rewarded for that effort in math without a deleterious impact in
35:1094:106041:21:20:71:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading.  Lower-achieving students also increased effort on the incentivized task, but did not increase their
35:1095:106150:20:20:71:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math scores and their reading scores decreased significantly. These data suggest that the classic “substitution
35:1096:106261:20:21:71:241:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effect” may depend on baseline ability.
35:1097:106300:21:20:88:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Two years after removing the incentives, the treatment effect for high-achieving students is large and
35:1098:106402:20:20:71:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:statistically significant in math [0.271σ(0.110)] and is small and statistically insignificant in reading.  In
35:1099:106512:20:21:71:539:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:stark contrast, low-achieving students have no treatment effect in math but a large, negative, and statistically
35:1100:106624:21:20:71:539:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:significant treatment effect on reading [-0.219σ(0.084)].  These data suggests that there may be long-run
35:1101:106729:20:0:71:415:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts of multitasking through learning, dynamic complementarities, or both.
36:1102:106808:0:20:72:213:711:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Incentives in Secondary Schools
36:1103:106839:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Fryer (2011) and Fryer (2010) describe the results of a series of randomized field experiments on fi-
36:1104:106940:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:nancial incentives and secondary student achievement.  In NYC, seventh grade students were paid for per-
36:1105:107044:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:formance on a series of ten interim assessments administered by the NYC Department of Education to all
36:1106:107146:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students. In Chicago, ninth graders were paid every five weeks for grades in their core courses. In Washing-
36:1107:107254:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ton, DC, sixth, seventh, and eighth grade students were paid for their performance on a metric that included
36:1108:107362:20:20:72:511:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attendance, behavior, and three inputs to the production function chosen by each school individually.
36:1109:107463:20:21:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The results reported in Fryer (2011) and Fryer (2010) are surprising. The impact of financial incentives
36:1110:107567:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on state test scores is statistically zero in each city. In NYC, paying students for performance on standardized
36:1111:107679:20:20:72:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tests yielded treatment effects of 0.004σ(0.017) in reading and -0.031σ(0.037) in mathematics in seventh
36:1112:107783:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grade and similar results for fourth graders.  In Chicago, rewarding ninth graders for their grades had no
36:1113:107889:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effect on achievement test scores in math or reading.  In Washington, DC, where students were paid for
36:1114:107991:20:20:72:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:various inputs to the educational production function, we observed an impact of 0.152σ(0.092) in reading
36:1115:108095:20:21:72:228:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and 0.114σ(0.106) in mathematics.
36:1116:108128:21:20:88:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Overall,  these estimates suggest that incentives are not a panacea – but we cannot rule out small to
36:1117:108229:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:modest effects (e.g., 0.10σ) which, given the relatively low cost of providing financial incentives to students,
36:1118:108341:20:21:72:232:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have a positive return on investment.
36:1119:108378:21:20:88:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Perhaps even more surprisingly, financial incentives had little or no effect on the outcomes for which
36:1120:108480:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students received direct incentives, self-reported effort, or intrinsic motivation. In NYC, the effect of student
36:1121:108593:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:incentives on the interim assessments is, if anything, negative. In Chicago, where we rewarded students for
36:1122:108700:20:21:72:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grades in five core subjects, the grade point average in these subjects increased 0.093σ(0.057) and treatment
36:1123:108809:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students earned 1.979 (1.169) more credits (half a class) than control students.  Both of these impacts are
36:1124:108916:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:marginally significant. Incentives in Washington D.C. had no significant impacts on attendance rates, report
36:1125:109024:20:21:72:230:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:card grades, or behavioral incidents.
36:1126:109061:21:20:88:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Treatment effects on an index of “effort,” which aggregates responses to survey questions such as how
36:1127:109162:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:often students complete their homework or asks their teacher for help, are small and statistically insignif-
36:1128:109270:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:icant across all cities, though there may have been substitution between tasks.  Finally, using the Intrinsic
36:1129:109379:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Motivation Inventory developed in Ryan (1982), Fryer (2011), Fryer (2010), and Fryer and Holden (2013)
36:1130:109481:20:32:72:350:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:find little evidence that incentives decrease intrinsic motivation.
36:1131:109548:32:21:88:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Taken together, the randomized field experiments involving financial incentives for students have gener-
36:1132:109652:21:0:72:540:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ated a rich set of facts. Paying second grade students to read books significantly increases reading achieve-
37:1133:109763:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment for students who take the English tests or those who are not English Language Learners, and is detri-
37:1134:109869:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mental to non-English speakers. Paying fifth graders for completing math homework significantly increases
37:1135:109974:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their math achievement and significantly decreases their reading achievement.  All other incentive schemes
37:1136:110080:20:32:72:428:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had, at best, small to modest effects – none of which were statistically significant.
37:1137:110165:32:21:72:369:618:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:B. NON-FINANCIALINCENTIVES ANDRETURNS TOSCHOOLING
37:1138:110214:21:20:88:539:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Fryer (2013) describes a large and innovative randomized field experiment which grew out of a part-
37:1139:110313:20:20:71:539:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:nership between three large organizations:  Tracphone – the largest pre-paid mobile phone provider in the
37:1140:110418:20:21:71:539:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:US, Droga5 – an internationally recognized advertising firm, and the Oklahoma City Public Schools.  The
37:1141:110521:21:20:71:539:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiment, entitled “The Million”, was designed to provide accurate information to students about the im-
37:1142:110627:20:20:71:539:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:portance of education on future outcomes such as unemployment, incarceration, and wages and to provide
37:1143:110729:20:21:71:411:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:incentives to read books through free cell phones and minutes to talk and text.
37:1144:110808:21:20:88:539:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Students in three treatment groups were given cellular phones free of charge, which came pre-loaded
37:1145:110907:20:20:71:539:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with 300 credits that could be used to make calls or send text messages.  Students in the main treatment
37:1146:111011:20:21:71:539:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:arm received 200 credits per month to use as they wanted and received one text message per day on the link
37:1147:111117:21:20:71:539:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:between human capital and future outcomes delivered at approximately 6:00 P.M. A second treatment arm
37:1148:111218:20:20:71:539:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:provided the same text messages as well as non-financial incentives – credits to talk and text were earned by
37:1149:111327:20:20:71:539:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading books outside of school.  A third treatment arm allowed students to earn credits by reading books
37:1150:111432:20:21:71:539:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and included no information. There was also a pure control group that received neither free cellular phones,
37:1151:111540:21:20:71:192:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:information, nor incentives.
37:1152:111568:20:20:88:539:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:On direct outcomes for students in the informational treatments, Fryer (2013) reports students’ ability
37:1153:111671:20:21:71:539:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to answer specific questions about the information provided in the text messages.  Treatment effects were
37:1154:111776:21:20:71:539:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:uniformly positive. Pooling across both informational treatments, treatment students were 4.9 (2.7) percent-
37:1155:111884:20:20:71:539:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:age points more likely to correctly identify the wage gap between college graduates and college dropouts,
37:1156:111989:20:21:71:539:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:17.9 (3.8) percentage points more likely to correctly identify the relationship between schooling and incar-
37:1157:112097:21:20:71:539:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ceration, and 17.8 (3.8) percentage points more likely to answer both questions correctly.  As a robustness
37:1158:112204:20:20:71:539:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:test, we included a “placebo” question on the unemployment rate of college graduates, about which students
37:1159:112310:20:21:71:539:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:never received information.  The difference in the probability of answering this question correctly between
37:1160:112417:21:20:71:539:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:informational treatments and the control group was trivial and statistically insignificant. Moreover, 54 per-
37:1161:112526:20:20:71:539:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cent of control students believe that incarceration rates for high school graduates and dropouts are “no[t]
37:1162:112633:20:21:71:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:differen[t]” or “really close”, suggesting that students in Oklahoma Public Schools do not have accurate
37:1163:112737:21:0:71:239:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:knowledge of the returns to schooling.
38:1164:112777:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Results are mixed for indirect outcomes such as self-reported effort, state test scores, and attendance.
38:1165:112881:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Across the treatment arms, ITT estimates of the effect of treatment on self-reported effort are positive and
38:1166:112989:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:statistically significant for both incentives and information arms.  For instance, students in the information
38:1167:113099:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment were 15.1 (3.7) percentage points more likely to report feeling more focused or excited about doing
38:1168:113208:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:well in school and 7.0 (3.7) percentage points more likely to believe that students were working harder in
38:1169:113314:21:20:72:103:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school.
38:1170:113321:20:20:88:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In  stark  contrast,  on  all  administrative  outcomes  –  math  or  ELA  test  scores,  student  attendance,  or
38:1171:113435:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:behavioral incidence – there was no evidence that any treatment had a statistically significant impact, though
38:1172:113545:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:due to imprecise estimates one cannot rule out small to moderate effects which might have a positive return
38:1173:113652:20:20:72:136:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on investment.
38:1174:113666:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another potentially powerful incentive is offering students a chance to earn college credit or college
38:1175:113768:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:degrees while still in high school.  The idea is that offering college credit will increase student incentives
38:1176:113878:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to exert effort and increase access to college for some students.  Over 240 schools nationwide, called Early
38:1177:113986:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Colleges, have already adopted this model. Early Colleges combine a rigorous high school curriculum along
38:1178:114091:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with the potential to earn two years of college credit or a two-year degree during high school.  Most Early
38:1179:114198:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Colleges target underserved students and team up with colleges to offer this opportunity at no or low cost
38:1180:114304:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to the students. Berger et al. (2013) utilize the random lottery admission process of some Early Colleges to
38:1181:114412:21:20:72:379:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:investigate the causal impact of Early Colleges on students’ outcomes.
38:1182:114482:20:20:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In their study, Berger et al.  (2013) used administrative and survey data from ten Early Colleges that
38:1183:114584:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conducted random admission lotteries for the 2005-06, 2006-07, or 2007-08 school years. Comparing lottery
38:1184:114689:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:winners  to  lottery  losers,  they  were  able  to  estimate  causal  impacts  on  high  school  completion,  college
38:1185:114807:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:enrollment, college degrees earned, standardized test scores, and high school and college experiences. High
38:1186:114914:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school outcome and student demographic data were obtained directly from the administrative records of the
38:1187:115019:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools involved in the study; for college outcomes, students were matched to records in National Student
38:1188:115124:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Clearinghouse;  data on high school and college experiences as well as college credits obtained while in
38:1189:115228:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:high school came from a student survey that the researchers administered to students in eight of the Early
38:1190:115334:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Colleges.  The final sample included 2,458 students for the administrative outcomes and 1,294 students for
38:1191:115440:21:20:72:164:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the survey outcomes.
38:1192:115460:20:20:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Using  this  data,  Berger  et  al.   (2013)  found  that  students  offered  admission  to  Early  Colleges  were
38:1193:115574:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:significantly more likely to graduate high school and ever attend college than students who lost the lottery.
38:1194:115683:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Eighty-six percent of Early College students graduated high school compared to 81 percent of lottery losers
38:1195:115790:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and 80 percent of Early College students ever enrolled in college whereas only 71 percent of comparison
39:1196:115895:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students did. Note that these numbers only reflect enrollment observed during the study period, 2005-2011,
39:1197:116001:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and that the gap in enrollment rates between lottery winners and lottery losers was decreasing as time went
39:1198:116108:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on.  For example, for cohorts with six years of data available, the gap four years after 9th grade was 39.2
39:1199:116215:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:percentage points and this gap had decreased to 9.8 percentage points six years out. Further, when restricting
39:1200:116325:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the sample to only students that enrolled in college after high school graduation, lottery students were only
39:1201:116434:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:5.7 percentage points more likely to attend a four-year college and they find no significant differences for
39:1202:116542:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:any college or two-year college enrollment. Similarly, during the study period, Early College students were
39:1203:116649:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:20 percentage points more likely to obtain a college degree (control mean was 2 percent).  These degrees
39:1204:116753:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were typically associate’s degrees and approximately 20 percent of Early College students earned a degree
39:1205:116858:20:20:72:200:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:before the end of high school
39:1206:116887:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Berger et al.  (2013) found no impact on GPA and math standardized test scores.  However, they found
39:1207:116987:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that Early College students scored 0.14 standard deviations higher than lottery losers on standardized ELA
39:1208:117093:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tests. The survey results showed that Early College students were 45.1 percentage points more likely to earn
39:1209:117201:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:college credit in high school than comparison students and that comparison students were 33.7 percentage
39:1210:117305:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:points more likely to take at least one advanced placement exam in high school. In addition, Early College
39:1211:117411:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students reported engaging in rigorous learning activities in school more frequently, being exposed to higher
39:1212:117520:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:expectations of college attendance from teachers, principals, and their peers, and reported receiving more
39:1213:117626:21:20:72:353:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:help for completing college applications and financial aid forms.
39:1214:117691:20:20:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The findings overall suggest that Early Colleges can successfully impact students’ college enrollment
39:1215:117792:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and  attainment  during  the  four  years  that  the  students  are  enrolled  in  an  Early  College  –  but  that  these
39:1216:117914:20:33:72:395:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts might not spillover to the years following high school graduation.
39:1217:117988:33:20:88:540:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The meta-analysis coefficients for student incentives experiments are 0.024σ(0.018) for math achieve-
39:1218:118089:20:32:72:233:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment and 0.021σ(0.017) for reading.
39:1219:118124:32:21:72:135:220:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:C. TUTORING
39:1220:118135:21:20:88:539:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Throughout  recorded  history,  the  children  of  the  elites  were  taught  in  a  manner  that  would  now  be
39:1221:118248:20:20:72:540:179:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:referred to as tutoring.  In ancient Greece, children from wealthy families received their primary education
39:1222:118356:20:21:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:individually or in small groups from masters or tutors (Dunstan 2010). This practice continued for children
39:1223:118463:21:20:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of  the  rich  and  nobles  throughout  the  Middle  Ages  (Nelson-Royes  2015).   As  late  as  the  17th  century,
39:1224:118579:20:20:72:540:118:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schooling was thought to be a social, not academic, activity with primary human capital produced in small
39:1225:118684:20:21:72:540:98:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:groups at home. Yet, the term, “tutoring”, has in more recent history become synonymous with remediation
39:1226:118788:21:0:72:171:77:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and fallen out of favor.
40:1227:118814:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:There is substantial heterogeneity in how schools implement various programs that fall under the general
40:1228:118918:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:umbrella of “tutoring.” Some schools place students in one-on-one settings with a trained tutor, other schools
40:1229:119028:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:place  eight  students  with  a  volunteer.   Some  students  receive  tutoring  30  minutes  per  week,  others  are
40:1230:119145:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:provided 5 hours of intense instruction in the same time period. This heterogeneity leads, naturally, to large
40:1231:119255:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:differences in treatment effects.  Dobbie and Fryer (2013), define “high-dosage” tutoring as being tutored
40:1232:119361:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in groups of 6 or fewer for 4 or more days per week.  Moreover, they demonstrate that tutoring itself is
40:1233:119465:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:not correlated with charter school effectiveness.  However, schools who implement “high-dosage” tutoring
40:1234:119569:20:21:72:239:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:demonstrate marked treatment effects.
40:1235:119606:21:20:88:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Following Dobbie and Fryer (2013), we divide the randomized field experiments in tutoring into these
40:1236:119706:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:two groups:  low-dosage and high-dosage tutoring.  They are discussed in turn.  In this exposition, high-
40:1237:119811:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dosage tutoring is defined as being tutored in groups of 6 or fewer for more than three days per week or
40:1238:119915:21:29:72:447:487:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:being tutored at a rate that would equate to 50 hours or more over a 36-week period.22
40:1239:120001:29:20:72:171:458:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:High-Dosage Tutoring
40:1240:120021:20:20:88:539:438:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Blachman  et  al.   (2004)  report  results  from  a  study  of  a  high-dosage  tutoring  program  that  targeted
40:1241:120135:20:21:72:540:418:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:struggling second and third grade readers.  Their study specifically focused on these young readers in an
40:1242:120240:21:20:72:540:397:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attempt to increase the growth trajectories of these students and possibly combat the negative adolescent
40:1243:120345:20:20:72:540:377:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and adult outcomes that have been associated with poor early reading skills.   The study uses data from
40:1244:120448:20:20:72:540:357:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:two  cohorts  of  students  drawn  from  eleven  schools  in  the  spring  of  1997  and  the  spring  of  1998.   The
40:1245:120566:20:21:72:540:337:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:researchers sent letters home to the parents of 723 students that teachers identified as being in the lowest
40:1246:120674:21:20:72:540:316:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:20% of readers in their classroom. Of these, 295 students were screened using standardized reading and IQ
40:1247:120779:20:20:72:540:296:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tests.  In order to be eligible for the study, students had to obtain a standard score below 90 on either the
40:1248:120888:20:21:72:540:276:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Word Identification or the Word Attack subtest of the Woodcock Reading Mastery Tests, obtain a standard
40:1249:120991:21:20:72:540:255:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:score below 90 on a composite of these two subtests, and have a Verbal IQ of at least 80. After screening and
40:1250:121100:20:20:72:540:235:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:balancing for gender, 89 students were randomly assigned to treatment or control (48 to treatment and 41 to
40:1251:121207:20:21:72:540:215:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control).  The study also contained a neuroimaging component that required an additional health screening
40:1252:121312:21:20:72:540:194:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:post-randomization, thus, the researchers contacted parents again to gain consent for both the neuroimaging
40:1253:121419:20:20:72:540:174:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and tutoring aspects of the experiment.  This resulted in a final sample of 37 students in treatment and 32
40:1254:121526:20:21:72:540:154:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students in control. Balance tests revealed no significant differences on observables between the final set of
40:1255:121636:21:20:72:260:133:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment and controls students at baseline.
40:1256:121680:20:20:88:539:113:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Treatment students received one-on-one tutoring instruction for 50 minutes a day,  five days a week,
40:1257:121780:20:16:72:540:93:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from September to June. This resulted in the average treatment student attending 126 sessions or 105 hours
40:1258:121886:16:0:84:450:77:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:A:22We add to the Dobbie and Fryer (2013) definition because not all studies report days and group size.
41:1259:121990:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of tutoring.  This instruction replaced the typical remedial instruction that the schools offered and that the
41:1260:122100:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control students participated in.  The instruction was carried out by 12 tutors who were certified in reading
41:1261:122209:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:or special education.  Prior to the intervention, each tutor received 45 hours of training on early childhood
41:1262:122318:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:interventions,  early reading acquisition,  and teaching strategies.  Additionally, tutors received 2 hours of
41:1263:122428:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:training each month for the duration of the experiment. The instruction focused on developing fluency and
41:1264:122533:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:comprehension strategies, and teaching students to read for pleasure. To do this, tutors incorporated a five-
41:1265:122642:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:step plan that was featured in previous published studies into each session (Blachman 1987; Blachman et al.
41:1266:122749:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:1999).  In over 90% of classroom observations and audiotapes of the tutor sessions, tutors included all five
41:1267:122857:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:steps of the instruction.  Control students continued business-as-usual – nine control students received no
41:1268:122964:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:remedial instruction outside of their reading class and the rest participated in small group tutoring that met
41:1269:123074:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for 3-5 times a week. On average, control students that received remedial instruction attended 104 sessions
41:1270:123181:21:20:72:278:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and received 77 hours of additional instruction.
41:1271:123229:20:20:88:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To test the impact of treatment, Blachman et al.  (2004) administered a battery of tests pretreatment,
41:1272:123331:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:immediately following treatment,  and one year after treatment.  The test battery included the Woodcock
41:1273:123434:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Reading Mastery Tests—Revised (WRMT), Gray Oral Reading Tests—Third Edition (GORT), Wide Range
41:1274:123528:20:20:72:559:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Achievement Test 3—Spelling (WRAT), and the Calculation and Applied Problems subtests from the Woodcock-
41:1275:123632:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Johnson Psycho-Educational Battery—Revised (WJ-R). In addition, the researchers administered subtests
41:1276:123733:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of the non-normed Comprehensive Test of Phonological Processes (CTOPP) four times during the treat-
41:1277:123832:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment year and four times during the follow-up year. At posttest, the researchers found large and statistically
41:1278:123942:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:significant impacts on all standardized reading measures.  These impacts ranged from 0.55σon the com-
41:1279:124043:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:prehension subtest of the GORT to 1.69σon the WRMT basic skills cluster.   Furthermore,  6 of these 8
41:1280:124144:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts were still large and significant a year after the completion of the experiment (the two insignificant
41:1281:124253:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts were 0.30σand 0.24σon the GORT accuracy and GORT comprehension subtests, respectively).
41:1282:124348:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The authors saw similar reading results for the non-standardized subtests from the CTOPP. As expected,
41:1283:124450:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment had no significant impacts on standardized measures of mathematics. If anything, at posttest, the
41:1284:124557:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math results suggest negative impacts with effect sizes of -0.33σand -0.37σon the WJ-R calculations and
41:1285:124660:20:21:72:244:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:applied problems subtests, respectively.
41:1286:124700:21:20:88:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The findings overall suggest that one-on-one high dosage tutoring with research-proven instruction can
41:1287:124802:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increase the growth rates of low-ability students. Although treatment and control students have statistically
41:1288:124911:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:indistinguishable growth rates in the follow-up year, the large impact on reading scores from one year of
41:1289:125016:21:20:72:153:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment remains.
41:1290:125034:20:0:88:539:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another randomized study that investigates the impacts of high-dosage tutoring on low-ability students
42:1291:125138:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:is Cook et al. (2014). In this study, we implemented an academic and behavioral intervention for 106 male
42:1292:125243:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:9th and 10th grade students from a public school in the south side of Chicago. Over 90% of the sample were
42:1293:125349:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:both black and eligible for free or reduced-price lunch. The intervention consisted of providing students with
42:1294:125459:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:non-academic supports that teach the students social cognitive skills through the “Becoming a Man” (BAM)
42:1295:125563:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program while also providing students intensive individualized tutoring. The BAM program used principles
42:1296:125667:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of  cognitive  behavioral  therapy  to  deliver  a  curriculum  that  focused  on  values  education.   The  program
42:1297:125783:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sought to develop specific social or social cognitive skills such as generating new solutions to problems,
42:1298:125889:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:learning new ways to behave, and identifying consequences ahead of time.  BAM was conducted in small
42:1299:125989:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:groups that met once a week for one hour each time. Over the course of the year, students had the chance to
42:1300:126096:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:participate in 27 different group sessions and typically had to skip an academic class in order to participate.
42:1301:126207:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:For the academic portion of the intervention, students met in groups of two with a math tutor one hour a
42:1302:126311:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:day, every day.  The tutors were hired following the methodology of Match Corps and were paid $16,000
42:1303:126412:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:plus benefits for the nine-month academic year.23Control students were not eligible to participate in BAM
42:1304:126517:20:21:72:513:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:or the intensive tutoring but could participate in other academic supports available at the high school.
42:1305:126621:21:20:88:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Students were selected to participate in the study based on an academic risk index that was a function of
42:1306:126726:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the number of prior-year course failures, unexcused absences, and being previously held back. The 106 male
42:1307:126832:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:9th and 10th grade students with the highest risk index score were then randomly assigned to three groups:
42:1308:126938:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Control (N=34), BAM only (N=24), and BAM plus high-dosage tutoring (N=48). In order to investigate the
42:1309:127040:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impact of assignment to one of these two treatment arms, we obtained student-level records from Chicago
42:1310:127143:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Public Schools that contained demographic information and scores from the EXPLORE and PLAN tests for
42:1311:127243:20:21:72:268:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the year prior to and year of the intervention.
42:1312:127290:21:20:88:539:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:We found that the ITT effect of assigning students to either one of the treatment arms was large and
42:1313:127390:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:statistically significant for math achievement and math GPA. Assignment to either treatment arm increased
42:1314:127495:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math achievement by 0.51σand increased math GPA by 0.425 grade points on a four-point scale. We found
42:1315:127596:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:no spillovers to reading achievement and no significant impacts on discipline incidents or number of days
42:1316:127701:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:suspended. However, treatment students were absent 10.272 fewer days throughout the school year. Mostly
42:1317:127804:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:due to the relatively modest size of our sample, when separated by treatment arm, we found no significant
42:1318:127909:21:41:72:290:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:difference between the impacts of the two groups.
42:1319:127958:41:14:84:539:121:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:23Match Corps is an AmeriCorps program in which members spend a year attempting to close the achievement gap by tutoring
42:1320:128078:14:11:72:540:107:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:small groups of students in the various Match Charter Schools in Boston. Match Corps seeks to employ tutors who are dedicated to
42:1321:128206:11:11:72:540:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:constant improvement, who possess strong communication and writing skills, and who are committed to spending a year working
42:1322:128329:11:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:with children.  Adopting their hiring best practices, tutors in Chicago were required to pass a math assessment, conduct a mock
42:1323:128456:11:0:72:448:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:tutorial session with actual high school students, and interview with the principal or principal’s designee.
43:1324:128566:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Summarizing, the meta-coefficient on high-dosage tutoring is 0.309σ(0.106) for math achievement and
43:1325:128665:20:21:71:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.229σ(0.033) for reading achievement.  Indeed, 54.3% of coefficients demonstrate statistically significant
43:1326:128772:21:20:71:539:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:positive treatment effects;  0% yield statistically significant negative effects.  Surprisingly, the fraction of
43:1327:128884:20:32:71:398:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:statistically positive treatments is larger than early childhood interventions.
43:1328:128963:32:21:71:167:618:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Low-Dosage Tutoring
43:1329:128982:21:20:88:539:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The Early Start to Emancipation Preparation (ESTEP)-Tutoring program of Los Angeles County was
43:1330:129076:20:20:71:539:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:created in 1998.  The program targets foster children aged 14 to 15 who are three or more years behind in
43:1331:129181:20:21:71:539:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math or reading ability. ESTEP-Tutoring aims to improve the math and reading skills of these students and
43:1332:129286:21:20:71:539:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:encourage them to take advantage of educational resources of which they may have been previously unaware.
43:1333:129391:20:20:71:539:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Tutoring is provided in the home of the students by college student tutors drawn from the surrounding twelve
43:1334:129499:20:21:71:539:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:community colleges. Tutors are trained to teach the students in math, reading, and spelling and are provided
43:1335:129607:21:20:71:539:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with curriculum materials that fit a student’s skill level. In addition to tutoring, the program hopes to foster
43:1336:129719:20:20:71:539:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a mentorship relationship between the tutor and the student. Once assigned to the program, each student is
43:1337:129825:20:21:71:539:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:eligible for 50 hours of tutoring and tutors are allotted additional time for preparation, mentoring, or other
43:1338:129935:21:20:71:539:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:activities.  Courtney et al.  (2008) take advantage of the high demand of ESTEP-Tutoring and conduct an
43:1339:130038:20:20:71:367:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:evaluation of the program using its oversubscribed application pool.
43:1340:130106:20:20:88:539:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:For the study, all students referred to the program were screened to ensure their math or reading ability
43:1341:130211:20:21:71:539:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:was indeed three years behind grade level.  Eligible students were then randomly assigned to a group that
43:1342:130316:21:20:71:539:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:could participate in ESTEP-Tutoring or a control group that could not.  This resulted in a study sample of
43:1343:130422:20:20:71:539:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:445 students, 246 assigned to treatment and 219 assigned to control. On average, approximately four months
43:1344:130528:20:21:71:539:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:passed between assignment and a student’s first meeting with a tutor. Throughout the two years of the study
43:1345:130635:21:20:71:539:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:researchers found that 61.8 percent of treatment students eventually participated in ESTEP-Tutoring and
43:1346:130738:20:20:71:539:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the average treatment student received 18 hours of math tutoring and 17 hours of reading tutoring.  The
43:1347:130841:20:21:71:539:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:relatively low take-up rate is attributed to the high mobility of foster children and the length of time that
43:1348:130950:21:20:71:539:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:passed between assignment and receipt of tutoring. By the time tutors attempted to deliver the first tutoring
43:1349:131059:20:20:71:539:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:session,  a majority of the non-participants were no longer in the foster home listed on their application.
43:1350:131166:20:21:71:539:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Once the tutoring program was initiated, students were eligible for 50 hours of tutoring delivered through 2
43:1351:131274:21:20:71:192:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:hour sessions twice a week.
43:1352:131301:20:20:88:539:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In order to investigate the impact of ESTEP-Tutoring on these students, Courtney et al.  (2008) con-
43:1353:131401:20:21:71:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ducted three interviews over the two years after randomization (baseline, one year out, and two years out).
43:1354:131508:21:0:71:539:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:At  each  of  these  interviews,  the  researchers  administered  the  letter-word  identification,  calculation,  and
44:1355:131628:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:passage comprehension subtests of the Woodcock-Johnson Tests of Achievement III as well as a student
44:1356:131728:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:survey. The survey combined questions from The Midwest Evaluation of Adult Functioning of Former Fos-
44:1357:131829:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ter Youth, The National Survey of Child Adolescent Well-Being, the National Longitudinal Survey of Youth,
44:1358:131934:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and the National Longitudinal Survey of Adolescent Health.  The survey collected data on demographics,
44:1359:132036:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:prior experiences in care, prior victimization, relationships, social support, employment, education, health
44:1360:132144:21:20:72:207:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:behaviors, and physical health.
44:1361:132175:20:20:88:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Courtney et al. (2008) found evidence of a first-stage impact in that treatment students were more likely
44:1362:132280:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to report having been tutored at home.  However, control students were more likely to report that they had
44:1363:132386:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:received tutoring at school and the total number of tutoring hours reported by treatment and control students
44:1364:132495:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were not statistically different.  The authors limit their impact analysis to the second follow-up interview
44:1365:132603:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(two years after random assignment) due to the fact that participation in ESTEP was still ongoing for many
44:1366:132709:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students one year after random assignment and they find no evidence of impacts on any outcome measure.
44:1367:132811:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The difference between control and treatment groups on Woodcock-Johnson achievement scores,  school
44:1368:132910:20:33:72:506:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grades, educational attainment, and school behavior are all statistically indistinguishable from zero.
44:1369:133012:33:20:88:539:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Putting  all  low-dosage  tutoring  experiments  together,  the  meta-coefficient  on  low-dosage  tutoring  is
44:1370:133123:20:36:72:433:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.015σ(0.013) for math achievement and 0.015σ(0.015) for reading achievement.
44:1371:133200:36:28:71:237:358:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.3.2    Teacher-Based Interventions
44:1372:133236:28:20:71:539:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Great teachers matter.  A one-standard deviation improvement in teacher quality translates into annual stu-
44:1373:133343:20:20:71:540:310:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dent achievement gains of 0.15σto 0.24σin math and 0.15σto 0.20σin reading (Rockoff 2004; Rivkin et
44:1374:133442:20:21:72:540:290:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:al. 2005; Aaronson et al. 2007; Kane and Staiger 2008). These effects are comparable to reducing class size
44:1375:133549:21:20:72:540:269:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:by about one-third (Krueger, 1999). Using quasi-experimental methods, Chetty et al. (2011) estimate that a
44:1376:133655:20:20:72:540:249:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:one-standard deviation increase in teacher quality in a single grade increases earnings by about 1% per year;
44:1377:133764:20:21:72:540:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students assigned to these better teachers are also more likely to attend college and save for retirement, and
44:1378:133874:21:20:72:261:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:less likely to have children when teenagers.
44:1379:133918:20:20:88:539:188:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:How to select or produce great teachers is one of the most important open questions in human capital
44:1380:134018:20:21:72:540:168:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:research.  Observable characteristics such as college-entrance test scores,  grade point averages,  or major
44:1381:134126:21:20:72:540:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:choice are not highly correlated with teacher value-added on standardized test scores (Aaronson et al. 2007;
44:1382:134234:20:20:72:540:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Rivkin et al.  2005; Kane and Staiger 2008; Rockoff et al.  2008).  And, many programs that aim to make
44:1383:134337:20:21:72:540:107:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers more effective have shown little impact on teacher quality (see e.g., Boyd et al. 2007 for a review).
44:1384:134447:21:0:72:540:86:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Some argue that these two facts, coupled with the inherent costs of removing low performing teachers due
45:1385:134553:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to collective bargaining agreements along with increased job market opportunities for women, contributes
45:1386:134657:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to the fact that teacher quality and aptitude has declined significantly in the past 40 years (Corcoran et al.
45:1387:134767:21:20:72:207:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2004; Hoxby and Leigh 2004).
45:1388:134795:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:We  group  the  set  of  teacher-based  random  assignment  studies  into  three  subcategories:   increasing
45:1389:134904:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher supply,  providing teachers incentives,  or increasing human capital through professional develop-
45:1390:135010:21:32:72:97:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment.
45:1391:135015:32:20:72:231:577:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:A. INCREASINGTEACHERSUPPLY
45:1392:135041:20:21:88:539:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Perhaps the most obvious way to increase teacher supply is to lower the barriers into the teaching pro-
45:1393:135144:21:20:71:539:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fession by allowing alternative routes for teachers to obtain necessary certifications.   Due to the teacher
45:1394:135252:20:20:71:539:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:shortages and the No Child Left Behind Act, which required every classroom to be staffed with a certified
45:1395:135357:20:21:71:539:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher or a teacher actively pursuing a certification through an approved program, there has been an in-
45:1396:135462:21:20:71:539:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:crease in teachers who enter teaching through alternative paths.Traditionally, teachers have completed all of
45:1397:135571:20:20:71:539:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their certification requirements at an accredited university or program before starting to teach in a classroom.
45:1398:135683:20:21:71:539:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In comparison, alternatively certified (AC) teachers start teaching before completing their requirements and
45:1399:135791:21:20:71:539:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:earn their certification while teaching.  Well-known examples of AC programs include Teach for America
45:1400:135893:20:20:71:539:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(TFA) and the New York City Teaching Fellows (NYCTF) program.  Both of these programs attract ex-
45:1401:135990:20:20:71:539:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tremely qualified uncertified individuals and place them in schools that are in dire need of good teachers.
45:1402:136097:20:21:71:539:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The potential benefits and advantages of these different routes to certification have been debated by many.
45:1403:136204:21:20:71:539:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:For example, some argue that the coursework required for traditionally certified (TC) teachers is an unnec-
45:1404:136311:20:20:71:539:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:essary burden that discourages some from pursuing teaching and AC programs are a way to circumvent that.
45:1405:136415:20:21:71:539:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In contrast, others argue that without that coursework, AC teachers enter classrooms underprepared and will
45:1406:136522:21:20:71:143:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:be less effective.
45:1407:136540:20:20:88:539:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In order to better understand the effectiveness of AC teachers relative to TC teachers, Constantine et
45:1408:136642:20:21:71:539:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:al.  (2009) conducted a randomized study in elementary schools around the nation in the 2004-2005 and
45:1409:136743:21:20:71:539:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2005-2006 school years.  Their study included 63 schools from 20 districts in 7 states across the nation.
45:1410:136848:20:20:71:539:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Within these schools, 2,610 K-5 students were randomly assigned to be taught by an AC teacher or a TC
45:1411:136949:20:21:71:539:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher for one school year.  Schools were only allowed to participate if they had at least one eligible AC
45:1412:137056:21:20:71:539:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher and one eligible TC teacher in the same grade.  In order for a teacher to be eligible to participate,
45:1413:137165:20:20:71:539:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers had to be relative novices, had to teach in a regular classroom, and had to deliver both reading and
45:1414:137274:20:21:71:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math instruction to all their students.  Researchers collected data on student achievement by administering
45:1415:137381:21:0:71:539:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the  math  and  reading  sections  of  the  California  Achievement  Test,  5th  Edition  (CAT).  The  researchers
46:1416:137497:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:also collected data on the classroom practices of teachers through classroom observations and principals’
46:1417:137602:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ratings.  In addition, all teachers completed a survey in the spring that collected information on teachers’
46:1418:137710:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:professional and personal backgrounds, experience in the school as a full-time teacher, and SAT/ACT scores.
46:1419:137817:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Finally, they also collected data on the details of each program a teacher attended for certification/alternative
46:1420:137930:20:21:72:120:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:placement.
46:1421:137940:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Constantine et al. (2009) found that students of AC teachers did not perform statistically different than
46:1422:138045:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students of TC teachers. Furthermore, there were no statistically significant differences when comparing low
46:1423:138153:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grade-level (K-1) teachers to high grade-level (2-5) teachers or low-experience teachers to high-experience
46:1424:138260:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers.  When exploring heterogeneous effect sizes across amount of coursework teachers were required
46:1425:138363:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to do while teaching, there is some evidence that AC teachers who had high-levels of course work had neg-
46:1426:138468:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ative impacts on student achievement. Similarly, there is no statistically significant difference in classroom
46:1427:138578:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:observation scores between AC and TC teachers.  However,  when restricting the sample to teachers that
46:1428:138680:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had high-levels of coursework, there is evidence that AC teachers’ classroom practices were worse than TC
46:1429:138785:20:21:72:156:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers’ practices.
46:1430:138805:21:20:88:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In addition to the experimental results, Constantine et al.  (2009) also present non-experimental results
46:1431:138910:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that explore the relationship between teacher characteristics and program details with the impacts on stu-
46:1432:139016:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dents’ achievement. Overall, they found that teacher characteristics and training experiences only explained
46:1433:139124:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:5 percent of the variation in effects on math test scores and 1 percent of the variation in effects on reading test
46:1434:139239:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores.  The only significant correlations they found were that AC teachers with master’s degrees were less
46:1435:139346:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effective in improving student achievement in reading than TC teachers without a master’s degree and that
46:1436:139451:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students in classrooms taught by AC teachers who were taking coursework towards a degree or certification
46:1437:139556:21:20:72:463:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:did worse in reading than students taught by TC teachers who weren’t taking coursework.
46:1438:139643:20:20:88:539:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Some argue that schools don’t just need access to more teachers, but specifically need access to different
46:1439:139749:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and potentially better talent pools.  Proponents of this argument often point to successful foreign education
46:1440:139858:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:systems, such as Hong Kong or Finland, that draw their teachers from the uppermost ranks of their univer-
46:1441:139963:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sities (Tucker 2011). In contrast, it is a well-documented fact that the talent pool of American teachers has
46:1442:140072:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:been declining since 1960 (see Corcoran et al. 2004). Hoxby and Leigh (2004) attribute a large part of this
46:1443:140179:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:decline to opportunities outside of teaching drawing high-aptitude women from the profession.  Over the
46:1444:140282:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:past couple decades, we have seen an increase of programs designed to combat this decline and get more
46:1445:140384:20:21:72:467:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and better college students to enter into teaching. One such program is Teach for America.
46:1446:140474:21:20:88:539:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Teach For America, a non-profit organization that recruits recent college graduates to teach for two years
46:1447:140580:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in low-income communities, is one of the nation’s most prominent service programs.  Based on founder
47:1448:140682:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Wendy Kopp’s undergraduate thesis at Princeton University, TFA’s mission is to create a movement that will
47:1449:140788:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:eliminate educational inequity by enlisting our nation’s most promising future leaders as teachers. In 1990,
47:1450:140896:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:TFA’s first year in operation, Kopp raised $2.5 million and attracted 2,500 applicants for 500 teaching slots
47:1451:141005:20:20:72:369:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in New York, North Carolina, Louisiana, Georgia, and Los Angeles.
47:1452:141070:20:21:88:539:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Since its founding, TFA corps members have taught more than three million students.  Today, there are
47:1453:141171:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:8,200 TFA corps members in 125 “high-need” districts across the country, including 13 of the 20 districts
47:1454:141276:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with the lowest graduation rates.  Roughly 80 percent of the students reached by TFA qualify for free or
47:1455:141380:20:21:72:371:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reduced-price lunch and more than 90 percent are black or Hispanic.
47:1456:141447:21:20:88:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Entry into TFA is highly competitive; in 2010, more than 46,000 individuals applied for just over 4,000
47:1457:141550:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:spots. Twelve percent of all Ivy League seniors applied. In its recruitment efforts, TFA focuses on individu-
47:1458:141659:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:als who possess strong academic records and leadership capabilities, regardless of whether or not they have
47:1459:141766:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had prior exposure to teaching. To apply, candidates complete an online application, which includes a letter
47:1460:141874:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of intent and a resume.  After a phone interview, the most promising applicants are invited to participate in
47:1461:141983:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:an in-person interview, which includes a sample teaching lesson, a group discussion, a written exercise, and
47:1462:142091:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a personal interview. Applicants who are invited to interview are also required to provide transcripts, obtain
47:1463:142201:20:20:72:367:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:two online recommendations, and provide one additional reference.
47:1464:142266:20:21:88:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Using information collected through the application and interview, TFA bases their candidate selection
47:1465:142368:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on a model that accounts for multiple criteria that they believe are linked to success in the classroom. These
47:1466:142478:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:criteria include achievement, perseverance, critical thinking, organizational ability, motivational ability, re-
47:1467:142590:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:spect for others, and commitment to the TFA mission.  TFA conducts ongoing research on their selection
47:1468:142692:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:criteria, focusing on the link between these criteria and observed single-year gains in student achievement
47:1469:142799:21:20:72:157:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in TFA classrooms.
47:1470:142817:20:20:88:539:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:TFA teachers are required to take part in a five-week TFA summer institute to prepare them for place-
47:1471:142918:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment  in  the  classroom  at  the  end  of  the  summer.   The  TFA  summer  institute  includes  courses  covering
47:1472:143033:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teaching practice, classroom management, diversity, learning theory, literacy development, and leadership.
47:1473:143139:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:During the institute, groups of participants also take full teaching responsibility for a class of summer school
47:1474:143251:20:21:72:110:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students.
47:1475:143260:21:20:88:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:At the time of their interview,  applicants submit their subject, grade,  and location preferences.  TFA
47:1476:143364:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:works to balance these preferences with the needs and requirements of districts.  With respect to location,
47:1477:143471:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:applicants rank each TFA region as highly preferred, preferred, or less preferred and indicate any special
47:1478:143577:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:considerations, such as the need to coordinate with a spouse. Over 90 percent of the TFA applicants accepted
47:1479:143685:20:0:72:417:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:are matched to one of their “highly preferred” regions (Glazerman et al. 2006).
48:1480:143766:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:TFA also attempts to match applicants to their preferred grade levels and subjects, depending on appli-
48:1481:143869:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cants’ academic backgrounds, district needs, and state and district certification requirements.  As require-
48:1482:143977:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ments vary by region,  applicants may not be qualified to teach the same subjects and grade levels in all
48:1483:144082:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:areas.  It is also difficult for school regions to predict the exact openings they will have in the fall, and late
48:1484:144196:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:changes in subject or grade-level assignments are not uncommon.  Predicted effectiveness scores are not
48:1485:144299:21:20:72:512:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:used to determine the placement region, grade, or school, and the scores are not available to districts.
48:1486:144403:20:20:88:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:TFA corps members are hired to teach in local school districts through alternative routes to certification.
48:1487:144510:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Typically, they must take and pass exams required by their districts before they begin teaching and may also
48:1488:144618:21:20:72:410:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:be required to take additional courses to meet state certification requirements.
48:1489:144698:20:20:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:TFA corps members are employed and paid directly by the school districts for which they work, and
48:1490:144795:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:generally receive the same salaries and health benefits as other first year teachers.   Most districts pay a
48:1491:144903:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:$1,500 per corps member fee to TFA to offset screening and recruiting costs.  TFA gives corps members
48:1492:145004:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:various additional financial benefits, including “education awards” of $4,725 for each year of service that
48:1493:145111:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:can be used for past or future educational expenses, and transitional grants and no-interest loans to help
48:1494:145217:21:20:72:274:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:corps members make it to their first paycheck.
48:1495:145263:20:20:88:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To date, there have been a couple randomized evaluations of the impact of TFA teachers. Glazerman et
48:1496:145363:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:al.  (2006) report findings from a national evaluation of TFA. The experiment involved approximately 100
48:1497:145467:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:elementary classrooms from 17 schools drawn from Baltimore, Chicago, Compton, Houston, New Orleans,
48:1498:145566:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and the Mississippi Delta.  Students were stratified by grade and school and assigned randomly to either a
48:1499:145672:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:TFA or a non-TFA teacher. At the end of school year, Glazerman et al. (2006) found that students assigned to
48:1500:145780:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:TFA teachers score about 0.12σhigher in math and 0.03σhigher in reading than students assigned to tradi-
48:1501:145884:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tionally certified teachers.They found no impacts on other student outcomes such as attendance, promotion,
48:1502:145990:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:or disciplinary incidents, but TFA teachers were more likely to report problems with student behavior than
48:1503:146096:20:21:72:144:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were their peers.
48:1504:146113:21:20:88:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:An even bigger study analyzed by Clark et al.  (2013) uses a sample drawn from almost 100 schools
48:1505:146210:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:across eight states to investigate the effectiveness of middle school math teachers from TFA and a similar
48:1506:146316:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program called The New Teacher Project (TNTP). In each participating school,  students were randomly
48:1507:146416:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assigned to math classrooms taught by a program teacher (TFA or TNTP) or a teacher that did not enter
48:1508:146517:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher through either of these programs.  Similar to Glazerman et al.  (2006), Clark et al.  (2013) find a
48:1509:146624:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:B:significant impact of TFA on students’ math test scores.  Students assigned to TFA teachers scored 0.07σ
48:1510:146728:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:higher on state standardized testing whereas students assigned to TNTP teachers had test scores that were
48:1511:146833:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:indistinguishable from students in control classrooms.  Note that this study was not designed to investigate
49:1512:146943:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the difference between TFA and TNTP teachers.  Students were not randomly assigned between TFA and
49:1513:147041:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:TNTP teachers, so differences between the effectiveness of the teachers could be due to differences in the
49:1514:147147:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students they taught, the comparison teachers, or the schools they were in. Indeed, TFA and TNTP teachers
49:1515:147252:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:included in the study largely taught in different schools and districts. With this in mind, there are still some
49:1516:147364:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:major differences between the two programs worth noting. TFA requires its teachers to commit to two years
49:1517:147469:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of teacher whereas TNTP expects their recruits to teach for many years.  Also, TFA recruits heavily from
49:1518:147573:20:20:72:423:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:college campuses while TNTP recruits professionals that want to switch careers.
49:1519:147652:20:21:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Several other programs similar – in spirit – to TFA are Boston Teaching Residency, Match Teaching
49:1520:147749:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Residency, NYC Teaching Fellowships, Inner-City Teaching Corps of Chicago, and Harvard Teaching Fel-
49:1521:147849:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:lows.  Although these programs all differ in length, training procedures, and credentials earned through the
49:1522:147957:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program, they all recruit college graduates with strong academic backgrounds and place them in struggling
49:1523:148062:21:32:72:520:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school districts. To the best of our knowledge, no randomized evaluations exist yet for these programs.
49:1524:148165:32:20:72:190:455:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:B. TEACHERINCENTIVES
49:1525:148185:20:21:88:539:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To increase teacher productivity, there is growing enthusiasm among policy makers for initiatives that tie
49:1526:148291:21:20:72:540:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher incentives to the achievement of their students.  Since 2006, the U.S. Department of Education has
49:1527:148397:20:20:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:provided over $1 billion to incentive programs through the Teacher Incentive Fund – a program designed
49:1528:148499:20:20:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:specifically to support efforts developing and implementing performance-based compensation systems in
49:1529:148600:20:21:72:540:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools. At least seven states and many more school districts have implemented teacher incentive programs
49:1530:148705:21:20:72:322:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in an effort to increase student achievement (Fryer 2013).
49:1531:148763:20:20:88:539:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Yet, the empirical evidence on the effectiveness of teacher incentive programs is mixed.  In developing
49:1532:148866:20:21:72:540:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:countries where the degree of teacher professionalism is extremely low and absenteeism is rampant, field
49:1533:148970:21:20:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments that link pay to teacher performance are associated with substantial improvements in student
49:1534:149074:20:20:72:540:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:test scores (Duflo et al. 2012; Glewwe et al. 2010; Muralidharan and Sundararaman 2011). Conversely, the
49:1535:149178:20:21:72:444:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:few field experiments conducted in the United States have had, at best, mixed results.
49:1536:149264:21:20:88:539:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Theoretically, it is unclear how to design optimal teacher incentives when the objective is to improve
49:1537:149366:20:20:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student achievement.   Much depends on the characteristics of the education production function.   If,  for
49:1538:149473:20:21:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:instance,  the production function is additively separable,  then individual incentives may dominate group
49:1539:149579:21:20:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:incentives, as the latter encourages free-riding.  If, however, the production function has important com-
49:1540:149685:20:20:72:540:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:plementarities between teachers in the production of student achievement, group incentives may be more
49:1541:149787:20:33:72:288:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effective at increasing achievement (Baker 2002).
49:1542:149836:33:0:72:147:77:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Group Incentives
50:1543:149854:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In the 2007-2008 through the 2009-2010 school year, the United Federation of Teachers (UFT) and the
50:1544:149953:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:New York City Department of Education (DOE) implemented a teacher incentive program in over 200 high-
50:1545:150054:21:20:72:539:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:need schools, distributing a total of roughly $75 million to over 20,000 teachers.24The experiment was
50:1546:150156:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a randomized school-based trial.  Each participating school could earn $3,000 for every UFT-represented
50:1547:150259:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:staff member if the school met the annual performance target set by the DOE based on school report cards,
50:1548:150364:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:which the school could distribute at its own discretion. Each participating school was given $1,500 per UFT
50:1549:150471:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:staff member if it met at least 75% of the target but not the full target.  Note that the average New York
50:1550:150577:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:City public school has roughly sixty teachers; this implies a transfer of $180,000 to schools on average if
50:1551:150684:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:they met their annual targets and a transfer of $90,000 if they met at least 75% of, but not the full target.
50:1552:150793:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In elementary and middle schools, school report card scores hinge on student performance and progress on
50:1553:150897:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:state assessments, student attendance, and learning environment survey results. High schools are evaluated
50:1554:151003:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:similarly,  with graduation rates,  Regents exams,  and credits earned replacing state assessment results as
50:1555:151111:20:20:72:238:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:proxies for performance and progress.
50:1556:151148:20:21:88:539:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:An important feature of the experiment is that schools had discretion over their incentive plans.   As
50:1557:151250:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mentioned above, if a participating school met all of the annual targets, it received a lump sum equivalent
50:1558:151357:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to $3,000 per full-time unionized teacher.  Each school had the power to decide whether all of the rewards
50:1559:151463:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:would  be  given  to  a  small  subset  of  teachers  with  the  highest  value-added,  whether  the  winners  of  the
50:1560:151581:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:rewards would be decided by lottery, or virtually anything in-between. The only restriction was that schools
50:1561:151689:20:20:72:323:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were not allowed to distribute rewards based on seniority.
50:1562:151747:20:20:88:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:An overwhelming majority of the schools decided on a group incentive scheme that varied the individ-
50:1563:151847:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ual bonus amount only by the position held in the school.  This could be because teachers have superior
50:1564:151950:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:knowledge of education production and believe the production function to have important complementar-
50:1565:152051:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ities, because they feared retribution from other teachers if they supported individual rewards, or simply
50:1566:152157:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:because this was as close to pay based on seniority (the UFT’s official view as to why schools typically
50:1567:152261:21:20:72:248:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:settled on this scheme) as they could do.
50:1568:152302:20:20:88:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The results from this incentive experiment are informative. Providing incentives to teachers based on a
50:1569:152405:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school’s performance on metrics involving student achievement, improvement, and the learning environment
50:1570:152509:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:did not increase student achievement in any statistically meaningful way.  If anything, student achievement
50:1571:152616:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:declined.  ITT estimates yield treatment effects of -0.018σ(0.024) in mathematics and -0.014σ(0.020) in
50:1572:152719:20:23:71:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading for elementary schools,  and -0.046σ(0.018) in math and -0.030σ(0.011) in reading for middle
50:1573:152819:23:14:84:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:24The details of the program were negotiated by Chancellor Joel Klein and Randi Weingarten, along with their staffs.  At the
50:1574:152943:14:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:time of the negotiation, I was serving as an advisor to Chancellor Klein and convinced both parties to agree to include random
50:1575:153069:11:0:72:220:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:assignment to ensure a proper evaluation.
51:1576:153112:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools,per year.   Thus,  if an elementary school student attended schools that implemented the teacher
51:1577:153216:20:21:72:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:incentive  program  for  three  years,  her  test  scores  would  decline  by  -0.054σin  math  and  by  -0.042σin
51:1578:153330:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading,  neither  of  which  is  statistically  significant.   For  middle  school  students,  however,  the  negative
51:1579:153449:20:20:72:474:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts are more sizeable: -0.138σin math and -0.090σin reading over a three-year period.
51:1580:153538:20:21:88:539:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Consistent with Fryer (2013), Springer et al.  (2012) evaluated another group incentive experiment that
51:1581:153641:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:took place in the Round Rock Independent School District in Texas.  The study used random assignment
51:1582:153741:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to investigate the impacts of a program that awarded teams of middle school teachers bonuses based on
51:1583:153842:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their collective contribution to students’ test score gains. Two years after the initial randomization, Springer
51:1584:153954:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al.   (2012) found no significant impacts on the attitudes and practices of teachers or on the academic
51:1585:154060:20:32:72:180:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement of students.
51:1586:154084:32:21:72:164:496:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Individual Incentives
51:1587:154105:21:20:88:539:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Springer et al.  (2010) evaluated Tennessee’s POINT program – a three-year pilot initiative on teacher
51:1588:154207:20:20:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:incentives conducted in the Metropolitan Nashville School System from the 2006-07 school year through
51:1589:154308:20:21:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the 2008-09 school year.  296 middle school mathematics teachers who volunteered to participate in the
51:1590:154410:21:20:72:540:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program were randomly assigned to the treatment or the control group, and those assigned to the treatment
51:1591:154515:20:20:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:group could earn up to $15,000 as a bonus if their students made gains in state mathematics test scores
51:1592:154618:20:20:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:equivalent to the 95th percentile in the district.  They were awarded $5,000 and $10,000 if their students
51:1593:154724:20:21:72:540:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:made gains equivalent to the 80th and the 90th percentiles, respectively.  Springer et al.  (2010) found there
51:1594:154834:21:20:72:540:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:was no significant treatment effect on student achievement and on measures of teachers’ response such as
