51:1595:154938:20:20:72:153:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teaching practices.
51:1596:154957:20:21:88:539:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In an important observation, Neal (2011) discusses how group incentives (e.g.  Fryer 2013;  Springer
51:1597:155057:21:20:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al.  2012) or sufficiently obtuse (e.g.  Springer et al.  2010) pay schemes lead to problems when trying
51:1598:155164:20:20:72:540:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to calculate the incentive effect at the individual teacher level and could be the reason these experiments
51:1599:155271:20:21:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:observed little to no incentive effects. For instance, calculating the expected value of a one standard deviation
51:1600:155384:21:20:72:540:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increase in teacher effort when the incentive scheme depends on where a teacher lies in the overall district
51:1601:155492:20:20:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:distribution is a non-trivial calculation for an econometrician with loads of data and sophisticated techniques.
51:1602:155604:20:21:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:It would be exceedingly difficult for a teacher to perform this calculation and understand how their efforts
51:1603:155712:21:20:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:could translate into rewards. To circumvent this and competition issues between teachers, Barlevy and Neal
51:1604:155818:20:20:72:540:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(2012) develop a “pay for percentile” method that rewards teachers according to how highly their students’
51:1605:155924:20:21:72:540:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:test score improvement ranks among other students from other schools with similar baseline achievement
51:1606:156026:21:0:72:215:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and demographic characteristics.
52:1607:156060:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Although not fully using the method recommended by Barlevy and Neal (2012), Glazerman et al. (2009)
52:1608:156159:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:present results from a randomized experiment that ties individual teacher incentives to value-added mea-
52:1609:156263:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sures. This incentive scheme is more in line with the insights in Neal (2011) than Fryer (2013) or Springer
52:1610:156370:20:20:72:152:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al (2010, 2012).
52:1611:156389:20:21:88:539:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In 2007, Chicago Public Schools implemented its own version of the national Teacher Advancement
52:1612:156484:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Program (TAP). The national version of TAP was developed in the late 1990s by the Milken Family Foun-
52:1613:156585:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dation as an incentive program to increase teacher quality. Teachers could earn extra pay by being promoted
52:1614:156692:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to Mentor or Lead Teacher and receive annual performance bonuses based on their value-added and class-
52:1615:156794:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:room observations.  Chicago adopted this model with some minor alterations.  For example, the Chicago
52:1616:156895:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:TAP added principal bonuses tied to implementation benchmarks and school-wide value-added.  Teacher
52:1617:156994:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:incentives had an expected payout of $2,000 per teacher and teachers could earn an additional $7,000 by
52:1618:157097:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:becoming a Mentor or an additional $15,000 by becoming a Lead Teacher.   As Mentors,  teachers were
52:1619:157196:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:expected to provide ongoing classroom support to other teachers in the school.  Lead Teachers served on
52:1620:157299:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the leadership team responsible for implementing TAP, analyzing student data, and developing achievement
52:1621:157403:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:plans.  In addition, Mentors and Lead Teachers conducted weekly group meetings to foster collaboration
52:1622:157505:20:20:72:365:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:between teachers and provide additional professional development.
52:1623:157570:20:21:88:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Glazerman et al.  (2009) conducted a randomized evaluation of the first year of Chicago TAP. Of the
52:1624:157669:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sixteen K-8 schools that volunteered to participate in the program, eight were randomly assigned to start
52:1625:157774:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment in the 2007-2008 school year and the other eight would delay the start of the program until the
52:1626:157879:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2008-2009 school year. Glazerman et al. (2009) compared the outcomes for teachers and students in schools
52:1627:157984:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomly assigned to the two groups for the 2007-2008 school year to determine causal impacts of exposure
52:1628:158089:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to  one  year  of  Chicago  TAP.  For  their  analysis,  the  researchers  collected  student  achievement  data  and
52:1629:158206:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers’ classroom assignments from Chicago Public Schools as well as administered surveys to teachers
52:1630:158309:20:21:72:481:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and principals to collect important information that was not present in the administrative data.
52:1631:158405:21:20:88:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The evaluation suggests that TAP increased retention in treatment schools.  Teachers in TAP schools
52:1632:158504:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had a retention rate of 87.9 percent while teachers in control schools had a retention rate of 82.8 percent, a
52:1633:158614:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:statistically significant difference. However, teacher satisfaction and teachers’ positive attitudes toward their
52:1634:158727:21:20:72:400:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:principals were not statistically different between TAP and control schools.
52:1635:158803:20:20:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:More importantly, the introduction of TAP did not produce any measurable impacts on student stan-
52:1636:158900:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:B:dardized test scores.  The effect size for reading was -0.04σ(0.05) and the effect size for math was -0.04σ
52:1637:159007:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(0.06). The test sore impacts were insignificant across all grade levels and were robust to various sensitivity
52:1638:159118:20:0:72:112:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:analyses.
53:1639:159129:0:20:72:348:711:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Enhancing the Efficacy of Teacher Incentives Through Framing
53:1640:159189:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:During the 2010-2011 and the 2011-2012 school years, Fryer et al. (2015) conducted an experiment in
53:1641:159288:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:nine schools in Chicago Heights, IL. At the beginning of each school year, teachers were randomly selected
53:1642:159394:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to participate in a pay-for-performance program.  Among those who were selected, the timing and framing
53:1643:159497:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of the reward payment varied.  One set of teachers – whom we label the “Gain” treatment – received “tra-
53:1644:159601:21:20:72:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:ditional” financial incentives in the form of bonuses at the end of the year linked to student achievement.25
53:1645:159710:20:20:71:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Other teachers – the “Loss” treatment – were given a lump sum payment at the beginning of the school year
53:1646:159815:20:21:71:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and informed that they would have to return some or all of it if their students did not meet performance tar-
53:1647:159924:21:20:71:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:gets.  Teachers in the “Gain” and “Loss” groups with the same performance received the same final bonus.
53:1648:160028:20:20:71:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Within the “Loss” and “Gain” groups, we additionally tested whether there are heterogeneous effects for
53:1649:160131:20:21:71:425:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:individual teacher rewards compared to awarding incentives to teams of teachers.
53:1650:160211:21:20:88:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In all groups, performance was incentivized according to the “pay for percentile” method developed by
53:1651:160312:20:20:71:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Barlevy and Neal (2011), in which teachers are rewarded according to how highly their students’ test score
53:1652:160418:20:21:71:539:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:improvement ranks among peers from other schools with similar baseline achievement and demographic
53:1653:160516:21:20:71:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:characteristics.  As Neal (2011) describes, pay for percentile schemes separate incentives and performance
53:1654:160622:20:20:71:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:measurements for teachers since this method only uses information on relative ranks of the students. Thus,
53:1655:160728:20:21:71:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:motivation for teachers to engage in behaviors (e.g.  coaching or cheating) that would contaminate perfor-
53:1656:160834:21:20:71:277:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mance measures of the students are minimized.
53:1657:160879:20:20:88:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The first year ITT results of our experiment are consistent with over three decades of psychological and
53:1658:160983:20:20:71:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:economic research on the power of framing to motivate individual behavior, though other models may also
53:1659:161086:20:21:71:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:be consistent with the data.  Students who were assigned to teachers in the “Loss” treatment show large
53:1660:161189:21:20:71:539:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and statistically significant gains in year one math test scores (0.455σ(0.097)).  Teacher incentives that are
53:1661:161299:20:20:71:539:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:framed as gains demonstrate less success. In the first year of the experiment, students in the “Gain” treatment
53:1662:161410:20:21:71:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increased their math test scores 0.245σ(0.094). Importantly, the difference between the “Loss” and “Gain”
53:1663:161515:21:20:71:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatments in math improvement is statistically significant at conventional levels.   More generally,  these
53:1664:161623:20:20:71:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:results support the view in Barlevy and Neal (2011) and Neal (2011) that properly designed incentives can
53:1665:161728:20:21:71:174:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have significant effects.
53:1666:161753:21:20:88:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Interestingly,  when looking at the sample of all students,  we find little evidence of treatment effects
53:1667:161858:20:20:71:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the second year of the experiment.   The ITT estimates for “Loss” are 0.087σ(0.088) and for “Gain”
53:1668:161959:20:23:71:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:B:are 0.115σ(0.109).  The pooled estimates for both years of the experiment are 0.210σ(0.069) and 0.116σ
53:1669:162061:23:14:84:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:25Note that although math, reading, and science test scores were incentivized (the latter only for fourth and seventh grade science
53:1670:162192:14:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:teachers), the main analysis of the paper focuses on math achievement due to most students having multiple reading teachers and
53:1671:162319:11:0:72:196:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:the science sample being so small.
54:1672:162355:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(0.075) for “Loss” and “Gain”, respectively.  The difference between the “Loss” and “Gain” treatments for
54:1673:162460:20:21:72:263:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the pooled estimates has a p-value of 0.099.
54:1674:162504:21:20:88:539:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Although incentivizing teachers had differential impacts across both years when looking at the entire
54:1675:162605:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sample, we found that kindergartners had large gains in both years of the experiment regardless of whether
54:1676:162711:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their teachers were in the “Loss” or “Gain” group. In the first year of the experiment, the ITT estimates for
54:1677:162820:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:kindergarten students were 0.796σ(0.209) for “Loss” and 0.376σ(0.168) for “Gain”.  In the second year,
54:1678:162922:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the estimates were 0.574σ(0.176) and 0.714σ(0.144) for “Loss” and “Gain” respectively.  Therefore, the
54:1679:163024:20:33:72:518:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:pooled effect size for both years and both treatments was 0.568σ(0.121) for kindergarten math scores.
54:1680:163125:33:20:72:143:536:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Talent Transfers
54:1681:163141:20:20:88:539:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In America, inexperienced teachers are more likely to be assigned to high-minority and high-poverty
54:1682:163240:20:21:72:540:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:classrooms  (Feng 2010).   As  a result,  novice teachers are  taking on tougher school assignments,  teach-
54:1683:163348:21:20:72:540:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ing multiple grades, and teaching out-of-field classes (Donaldson and Johnson 2010).  To counteract this
54:1684:163452:20:20:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:trend, several school districts – such as Houston ISD – provide effective teachers incentives to teach in the
54:1685:163561:20:21:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:most troubled schools.  The theory is that the marginal return for an additional effective teacher in a well-
54:1686:163670:21:20:72:540:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:functioning school is less than the marginal return of that teacher in a less well-functioning school.  Good
54:1687:163778:20:20:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers have the potential to change the culture of a school and provide effective pedagogical tools and
54:1688:163883:20:20:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mentorship to struggling colleagues.  If true, providing incentives for talented teachers to teach in troubled
54:1689:163993:20:21:72:243:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools will increase total productivity.
54:1690:164034:21:20:88:539:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Glazerman et al. (2013) used a randomized experiment in 10 districts across the nation to investigate the
54:1691:164139:20:20:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impact of filling vacancies with high-achieving teachers through the Talent Transfer Initiative (TTI). In each
54:1692:164249:20:21:72:540:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:district, the TTI offered teachers with consistently high value-added (ranking in the top 20 percent within
54:1693:164356:21:20:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their subject and grade) $20,000, paid over two years, to teach at low-achieving schools selected through
54:1694:164461:20:20:72:540:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a random process.  Principals of schools with low average test scores volunteered to fill vacancies at their
54:1695:164569:20:21:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school using the TTI. Schools that volunteered were matched based on the grade-level and subject of the
54:1696:164672:21:20:72:540:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:vacancy as well as school demographics. Teacher teams (teachers grouped by grade and subject) within each
54:1697:164777:20:20:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:block of schools that had at least one vacancy were then randomly assigned to treatment or control. Teacher
54:1698:164884:20:21:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teams assigned to treatment status were eligible to fill their vacancy with a TTI teacher and vacancies in
54:1699:164990:21:20:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control teacher teams were filled using the typical process of the given school.  Note that high-performing
54:1700:165097:20:20:72:540:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers were not randomly assigned to these vacancies. After a teacher team is assigned to treatment, TTI
54:1701:165203:20:21:72:540:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers must interview for the position, principals must extend an offer to a TTI teacher, and then a TTI
54:1702:165309:21:0:72:540:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher must accept and voluntarily move to fill this vacancy. In order to receive the full financial incentive,
55:1703:165423:0:20:72:451:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:high-performing teachers must remain in the low-achieving school for a full two years.
55:1704:165509:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Glazerman et al. (2013) investigated the impact of teacher teams being eligible to fill their vacancies us-
55:1705:165616:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ing the TTI. Across the 10 districts included in the study, 165 teacher teams from 114 schools were randomly
55:1706:165724:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assigned to treatment (N= 85) or control (N=80). The transfer incentive was able to successfully attract high-
55:1707:165834:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achieving teachers. Eighty-eight percent of treatment vacancies were filled with teachers through the TTI. In
55:1708:165943:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:order to achieve this high rate of transfer, over 1,500 high-achieving teachers were invited to participate in
55:1709:166053:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:TTI. The teachers hired to fill treatment vacancies were significantly more experienced than teachers hired
55:1710:166160:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for control spots.  Treatment teachers had on average four years more experience and were 11 percentage
55:1711:166263:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:points more likely to have a National Board Certification than control teachers (CM = 9 percent).  Interest-
55:1712:166371:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ingly, there was evidence that principals reacted to the hiring of a TTI teacher by reallocating weak teachers
55:1713:166481:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to be in the same team as the incoming TTI teacher.  Teachers from elsewhere in the school that joined a
55:1714:166585:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment teacher team after the hiring of a TTI teacher had five years less experience than teachers that
55:1715:166691:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:moved into a control teacher team. In addition, treatment teachers were more likely to provide mentoring to
55:1716:166798:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their peers (15 compared to 5 percent of the control teachers) and were less likely to receive mentoring (39
55:1717:166906:21:20:72:265:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:compared to 59 percent of control teachers).
55:1718:166950:20:20:88:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Glazerman et al.  (2013) found that the above first-stage and intermediate impacts translated into large
55:1719:167054:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effects on student achievement tests for elementary schools but that there were no significant impacts on the
55:1720:167163:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement of middle school students. TTI eligible elementary classrooms increased students’ math scores
55:1721:167268:20:20:72:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:by 0.18σand students’ reading scores by 0.10σin the first year after randomization. In the second year, the
55:1722:167375:20:20:71:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cumulative impacts for treatment students were 0.22σand 0.25σfor math and reading test scores, respec-
55:1723:167477:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tively. Although treatment elementary teachers had large impacts on their students, there were no spillover
55:1724:167584:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effects for other teachers in their team.  Elementary student achievement outcomes were not significantly
55:1725:167689:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:different between students assigned to other teachers in the treatment team and students assigned to other
55:1726:167795:20:21:72:195:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers in the control team.
55:1727:167824:21:20:88:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, there was evidence that the TTI was effective at keeping these high-performing teachers in the
55:1728:167927:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:low-performing schools.  At the halfway point of the program, retention rates were higher for teachers that
55:1729:168034:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:filled TTI vacancies.  Treatment teachers were 23 percentage points more likely to remain in a school after
55:1730:168141:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the first year than their control counterparts (93 percent compared to 70 percent). In addition, retention rates
55:1731:168253:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:after the completion of the second year of the experiment were not statistically significant.  Approximately
55:1732:168361:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:60 percent of treatment teachers returned to the low-achieving school for a third, non-incentivized school
55:1733:168467:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:year.  In comparison, a statistically indistinguishable 51 percent of control teachers remained in the fall of
55:1734:168577:20:0:72:164:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the third school year.
56:1735:168601:0:20:88:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The meta-coefficient on teacher incentives is 0.022σ(0.022) for math achievement and -0.006σ(0.012)
56:1736:168700:20:21:71:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for reading achievement.   Yet,  that number seems particularly misleading in this context as many of the
56:1737:168805:21:20:71:539:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schemes were quite ad hoc and inconsistent with economic theory. More experiments are needed before one
56:1738:168908:20:20:71:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:can better hazard a guess on the efficacy of teacher incentives.  Future randomized trials ought to take the
56:1739:169016:20:33:71:533:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:insights in Barlevy and Neal (2011) and Neal (2011) seriously when designing teacher incentive schemes.
56:1740:169119:33:32:72:279:597:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:C. TEACHERPROFESSIONALDEVELOPMENT
56:1741:169152:32:20:71:224:565:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:General Professional Development
56:1742:169184:20:21:88:539:545:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The Gates Foundation states that the American education system spends $18 billion annually on pro-
56:1743:169282:21:20:71:539:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fessional development (Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation 2014).   For 2014,  Title II of the Elementary
56:1744:169385:20:20:71:539:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Secondary Education Act, a program mostly devoted to professional development, was appropriated
56:1745:169484:20:20:71:539:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:$2.3 billion (U.S. Department of Education 2014).   More than $450 million (approximately half) of the
56:1746:169586:20:21:71:539:464:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Department of Education’s Investing in Innovation (i3) grant money funded professional development pro-
56:1747:169689:21:20:71:539:443:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grams from 2010-2012 (U.S. Government Accountability Office 2014).  A new report released by TNTP
56:1748:169786:20:20:71:539:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:estimates that three large public districts included in their study spent nearly $18,000 per teacher per year
56:1749:169895:20:21:71:263:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for professional development (TNTP 2015).
56:1750:169936:21:20:88:539:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Professional development (PD) is viewed as a vital tool to increase teachers’ human capital and improve
56:1751:170039:20:20:71:539:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school effectiveness (Hill 2007).  However, experts have expressed concern that teachers are not receiving
56:1752:170145:20:21:71:539:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:enough professional development to have meaningful impacts on teachers’ practices and that the little pro-
56:1753:170251:21:20:71:539:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fessional development they receive does not focus enough on subject-matter knowledge (Cohen and Hill
56:1754:170351:20:20:71:540:301:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2001; Fletcher and Lyon 1998; Foorman and Moats 2004; Garet et al.  2001).26Another often articulated
56:1755:170452:20:21:71:539:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:concern is that professional development tends to be one-time workshops scheduled on “professional devel-
56:1756:170557:21:20:71:539:260:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:opment days” or in the summer months with little relevant follow-up (Joyce and Showers 1988; Parsad et
56:1757:170659:20:20:71:238:240:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:al. 2001; Loucks-Horsley et al. 1998).
56:1758:170697:20:21:88:539:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The U.S. Department of Education commissioned two PD interventions to provide states and districts
56:1759:170795:21:20:71:539:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with further information of the potential of PD programs to improve reading instruction (Garet et al. 2008).
56:1760:170903:20:20:71:539:179:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The first intervention provided second grade teachers with a year-long research-based institute series and the
56:1761:171013:20:21:71:539:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:second intervention provided the same institute series plus in-school coaching. Garet et al. (2008) presented
56:1762:171122:21:20:71:539:138:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:results from the randomized evaluation of these two interventions.   In their study,  90 schools across six
56:1763:171229:20:30:71:539:118:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:districts from four states were randomly assigned to one of the two treatment groups or a control group
56:1764:171332:30:14:84:539:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:26A national study revealed that over 80% of elementary and secondary teachers reported participating in 24 hours or less of
56:1765:171456:14:0:72:495:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:professional development over the 2005-2006 school year and summer of 2006 (U.S. Department of Education 2009).
57:1766:171569:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:such that each district had an equal number of elementary schools allocated to the three groups. Garet et al.
57:1767:171678:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(2008) collected data on teacher knowledge, teacher practices, and student achievement at the completion
57:1768:171782:21:20:72:372:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of the intervention and two years after randomization as a follow-up.
57:1769:171851:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:On average, teachers in the first intervention reported attending 39 hours of PD and teachers in the second
57:1770:171958:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:intervention reported attending 47 hours of PD. In comparison, control teachers only reported attending 13
57:1771:172064:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:hours of PD. Garet et al.  (2008) found that this exposure to PD lead to significant impacts on teachers’
57:1772:172169:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:knowledge and practices for both groups. Both interventions had positive impacts on second grade teachers’
57:1773:172275:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:knowledge of early reading content and instructional knowledge at posttest and a year after the PD programs
57:1774:172382:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:had completed.  For both years, teachers in both interventions used explicit instruction to a much greater
57:1775:172488:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:extent than teachers assigned to control.   However,  there was no significant difference in the amount of
57:1776:172594:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:independent student activity incorporated into the classroom and the use of differential instruction between
57:1777:172702:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:either  of  the  two  treatment  groups  and  control  teachers.   Although  there  were  large  impacts  on  teacher
57:1778:172819:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:knowledge and practices, there was no evidence that these changes had an impact on students’ test scores.
57:1779:172924:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Test scores from the implementation year and the follow-up year revealed no statistically significant impacts
57:1780:173033:21:20:72:267:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on standardized math and reading outcomes.
57:1781:173075:20:20:88:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another widely used PD program is Classroom Assessment of Student Learning (CASL). The program
57:1782:173169:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:set consists of a primary text, DVDs, ancillary books, and an implementation handbook. CASL is designed
57:1783:173272:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to  be  a  self-executing  PD  program  where  teachers  learn  from  the  textbook  and  use  CASL  assessments
57:1784:173384:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to  better  understand  their  own  and  their  students’  progress.   The  program  mostly  emphasizes  formative
57:1785:173498:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assessments,  but  also  includes  lessons  on  how  to  utilize  other  forms  of  classroom  assessments  such  as
57:1786:173614:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:standardized test scores. The program is typically implemented via teacher learning teams, in which teachers
57:1787:173722:21:20:72:446:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:can discuss and receive feedback from other teachers who are also using the program.
57:1788:173806:20:20:88:539:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In order to better understand the effects of CASL on students’ achievement, motivation to learn, and
57:1789:173906:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers’ classroom assessment practices, Randel et al.  (2011) conducted a large randomized experiment.
57:1790:174010:21:20:72:431:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Due to regional needs, they decided to focus the study in mathematics classrooms.
57:1791:174091:20:20:88:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Almost 70 schools from 32 districts from across Colorado participated in the study. Schools volunteered
57:1792:174194:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to participate and were eligible if they were large enough to have at least one fourth grade and one fifth
57:1793:174300:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grade teacher.  The 67 eligible schools were then randomly assigned to a treatment group (N = 33) and a
57:1794:174403:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control group (N= 34).  In November of 2007, treatment schools received one set of CASL PD materials
57:1795:174503:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for each math teacher in fourth or fifth grade.  In total, there were 178 such teachers in treatment schools
57:1796:174611:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and 231 teachers in control schools.  Treatment teachers participated in an introductory video conference
57:1797:174716:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with the author of CASL and had access to a facilitator who had received training in the CASL program,
58:1798:174820:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:but  other  than  this,  the  experiment  was  completely  hands  off.   The  teachers  were  asked  to  use  the  PD
58:1799:174937:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:naturally without any input or requirements from the research team. The 2007-2008 school year was used as
58:1800:175042:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a training year during which teachers studied the CASL material and started integrating CASL practices into
58:1801:175149:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:their classrooms.  The 2008-2009 year was the actual intervention year.  Fidelity of treatment was assessed
58:1802:175256:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:using self-reported logs that 90 percent of teachers returned to the research team.  In order to combat the
58:1803:175363:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:alternative hypothesis that any impact was just the result of the intervention schools having more resources,
58:1804:175472:20:20:72:224:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:control schools were given $1,000.
58:1805:175506:20:21:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In order to assess the impact of the intervention on student and teacher outcomes, Randel et al.  (2011)
58:1806:175610:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:collected administrative and survey data from both the training and implementation year. The administrative
58:1807:175717:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:data came directly from the Colorado Department of Education and contained state achievement test scores
58:1808:175821:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and student demographics.  In order to quantify students’ motivation to learn, researchers administered a
58:1809:175926:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student survey.  Further, teachers’ knowledge of classroom assessments, their classroom assessment prac-
58:1810:176030:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tices, and teachers’ involvement of students in assessments were all measured through self-reported teacher
58:1811:176137:20:21:72:108:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:surveys.
58:1812:176145:21:20:88:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Randel et al.  (2011) found evidence that treatment had a significant impact on teacher knowledge of
58:1813:176245:20:20:72:539:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:class assessments.  Intervention teachers on average answered 2.78 questions more (0.42σ) correctly on a
58:1814:176349:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:60-item test about teachers’ knowledge of classroom assessments. However, there was no evidence that this
58:1815:176454:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:knowledge influenced their classroom practices. There were no significant differences in classroom practices
58:1816:176562:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and the extent to which they involved their students in formative assessments.  Intervention teachers were
58:1817:176668:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:given an average rating of 1.61 for classroom assessment and control teachers had an average rating of
58:1818:176770:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:1.60 (where 1 represents low quality and 4 represents high quality).  For student involvement, intervention
58:1819:176877:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers  self-reported  average  score  was  a  0.39  and  control  teachers’  average  score  was  0.34  (where  1
58:1820:176993:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:indicates that all students were involved in formative assessments everyday and 0 represents no students
58:1821:177097:20:21:72:140:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were involved).
58:1822:177112:21:20:88:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:As  one  would  suspect  from  the  similar  practices  of  control  and  treatment  teachers,  average  student
58:1823:177224:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mathematics achievement was not statistically different between treatment and control students.  The ad-
58:1824:177328:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:justed mean scale score for students in a treatment classroom was 502.49(2.52) and the mean scale score
58:1825:177431:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for students in control classrooms was 501.91(2.44).  The impacts remain statistically insignificant when
58:1826:177536:20:32:72:234:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:looking at effect sizes by grade level.
58:1827:177575:32:21:88:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The meta-coefficient for general PD is 0.019σ(0.024) for math achievement and 0.022σ(0.023) for
58:1828:177670:21:0:71:539:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading achievement. In fact, there is not a single study with significant annual pooled impacts. Ironically –
59:1829:177782:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and perhaps sadly – Erik Hanushek argues school districts are overspending on ineffective and unmanaged
59:1830:177885:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:professional development and these districts refuse to veer away from practices that fail time and time again
59:1831:177994:21:32:72:137:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(Layton 2015).
59:1832:178008:32:20:72:238:638:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:‘Managed’ Professional Development
59:1833:178042:20:21:88:539:618:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another form of PD is one that has precise training and curriculum materials that schools and districts
59:1834:178145:21:20:72:540:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:can implement to increase teacher effectiveness.  These programs are significantly more prescriptive.  They
59:1835:178252:20:20:72:540:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:don’t abstractly discuss issues such as “classroom management” or endeavor to increase “rigor.” Consider
59:1836:178356:20:21:72:540:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:two well known examples of this approach to professional development:  Success for All and Reading Re-
59:1837:178458:21:20:72:103:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:covery.
59:1838:178465:20:20:88:539:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Success for All is a school-level elementary school intervention that focuses on improving literacy out-
59:1839:178569:20:21:72:540:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:comes for all students in order to improve overall student achievement and is currently used in 1,200 schools
59:1840:178678:21:20:72:540:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:across the country (Borman et al.  2007).  The program is designed to identify and address deficiencies in
59:1841:178784:20:20:72:540:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading skills at a young age using a variety of specific instruction strategies,  ranging from cooperative
59:1842:178891:20:21:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:learning to data-driven instruction.  Success for All is purchased as a comprehensive package, which in-
59:1843:178995:21:20:72:540:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cludes materials, training, ongoing PD, and a well-specified “blueprint” for delivering and sustaining the
59:1844:179101:20:20:72:540:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:model. Schools that elect to adopt Success for All implement a program that organizes resources to attempt
59:1845:179207:20:20:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to ensure that every child will reach the third grade on time with adequate basic skills and will continue to
59:1846:179316:20:21:72:333:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:build on those skills throughout the later elementary grades.
59:1847:179377:21:20:88:539:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Borman et al.  (2007) use a cluster randomized trial design to evaluate the impacts of the Success for
59:1848:179479:20:20:72:540:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:All model on student achievement.  Forty-one schools from eleven states volunteered and were randomly
59:1849:179580:20:21:72:540:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assigned to either the treatment or control groups. Treatment schools implemented Success for All in grades
59:1850:179687:21:20:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:K-2 and control schools implemented the program in grades 3-5. Borman et al. (2007) present results three
59:1851:179792:20:20:72:540:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years after randomization for the baseline cohort of kindergarten students. Although forty-one schools were
59:1852:179899:20:21:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:initially randomized, only thirty-five schools were included in the analysis due to six schools dropping out
59:1853:180007:21:20:72:540:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:over the years for various reasons. The authors conclude that these thirty-five schools are still balanced and
59:1854:180117:20:20:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attrition is not a threat to their results.  Using standardized test scores from three subtests of the Woodcock
59:1855:180228:20:21:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Reading Mastery Test—Revised, Borman et al.  (2007) find that Success for All increased student achieve-
59:1856:180332:21:20:72:539:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment by 0.36σ(0.11) on phonemic awareness, 0.24σ(0.11) on word identification, and 0.21σ(0.09) on
59:1857:180429:20:20:72:178:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:passage comprehension.
59:1858:180451:20:21:88:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another similar professional development program is Reading Recovery (RR). RR is a short-term in-
59:1859:180548:21:0:72:540:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tervention designed to help struggling readers in first grade catch up to their peers.  The program consists
60:1860:180658:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of students meeting one-on-one with a specially trained teacher every day for a 30-minute lesson over 12
60:1861:180762:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to 20 weeks.  The lessons are individualized by the RR teacher to fit to a student’s strengths and needs and
60:1862:180870:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:follow the RR model—focusing on phonemic awareness, phonics, vocabulary, fluency, and comprehension.
60:1863:180970:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:RR teachers undergo a year-long training procedure that takes place at designated training facilities and the
60:1864:181079:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools where they are assigned.  Through this training, they learn how to design and deliver daily lesson
60:1865:181185:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:plans,  document lessons,  and to collect and effectively use different types of student progress data.   All
60:1866:181294:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:RR teachers are overseen by a teacher leader who has attended an intensive post-graduate program where
60:1867:181396:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:they are expected to emerge as literary experts.  Literature on RR reports that approximately 75 percent of
60:1868:181503:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students enrolled in RR typically reach grade-level proficiency after participating in RR for the program’s in-
60:1869:181614:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tended length of 12-20 weeks and that these students go on to maintain their progress through the remainder
60:1870:181721:20:21:72:245:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of elementary school (May et al. 2013).
60:1871:181760:21:20:88:539:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Schwartz (2005) conducted the first randomized evaluation of RR in the United States.  In his study,
60:1872:181860:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:thirty-seven first-grade teachers from across the nation identified two at-risk students in their classroom.
60:1873:181968:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:One student from each pair was randomly assigned to a treatment condition that received RR in the fall
60:1874:182070:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and the other student was assigned to a control condition that received RR in the spring.  The participating
60:1875:182178:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers were all certified RR teachers and the program was active in their schools. The teachers gave up one
60:1876:182287:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of their four 30-minute RR slots to whichever student was randomly assigned to treatment. At the end of the
60:1877:182394:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:first semester, Schwartz (2005) found that treatment students had large and significant impacts on various
60:1878:182500:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:observation survey and standardized reading measures.  Effect sizes on the text level, letter identification,
60:1879:182609:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:concepts about print, and hearing and recording sounds in words tasks on the observation survey ranged from
60:1880:182716:20:21:72:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.9σto 2.02σand treatment had an impact of 0.94σon scores from the Slosson Oral Reading Test—Revised.
60:1881:182817:21:20:88:539:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In 2010, the U.S. Department of Education awarded RR a $45 million i3 grant along with $10.1 million
60:1882:182917:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from private sources to fund a scale-up of RR across the nation.  The scale-up intends to reach over 2,000
60:1883:183023:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools and provide literary assistance to over 88,000 students.  May et al.  (2013) report the findings from
60:1884:183132:21:20:72:222:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the first two years of this scale-up.
60:1885:183169:20:20:88:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:628 schools from across the nation were enrolled in the i3 scale-up of Reading Recovery. These schools
60:1886:183271:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were randomly assigned to three blocks and one of these blocks was randomly chosen to participate in a
60:1887:183373:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:RCT of Reading Recovery during the 2011-2012 school year.  Of the 209 schools in this block, only 156
60:1888:183474:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools actually carried out the randomization process described below and were included in the evaluation.
60:1889:183581:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Each school that participated in the RCT identified the eight lowest scoring students in their school using
60:1890:183688:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the Observation Survey of Early Literacy. These eight students were matched according to their scores and
60:1891:183793:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ELL status and then one student from each pair was randomly assigned to treatment and the other to control.
61:1892:183902:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:This process resulted in 628 students in the treatment group and 625 students in the control group (when
61:1893:184006:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:there were less than eight eligible students, odd number students were automatically assigned to treatment.
61:1894:184113:21:20:72:313:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:These students were omitted from the impact analysis).
61:1895:184167:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Using standardized test scores from the Iowa Test of Basic Skills and baseline demographics, May et
61:1896:184266:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:al.  (2013) investigate the causal impact of being assigned to the RR program.  They find that RR increased
61:1897:184373:21:32:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student achievement by 0.60σon the reading words subtest and 0.61σon the reading comprehension subtest.
61:1898:184476:32:20:88:539:577:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The effects of these ‘managed’ PD experiments for both subjects are statistically significant and for
61:1899:184577:20:21:72:540:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading, quite large.  The meta-coefficient is 0.052σ(0.016) for math achievement and 0.403σ(0.120) for
61:1900:184680:21:32:72:165:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading achievement.
61:1901:184700:32:20:72:151:504:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Teacher Feedback
61:1902:184716:20:20:88:539:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The modernization of teacher evaluation systems, an increasingly common component of teacher pro-
61:1903:184813:20:21:72:540:464:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fessional development, promises to reveal new, systematic information about the performance of individual
61:1904:184918:21:20:72:540:443:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:classroom teachers.  Yet while states and districts race to design new systems, most discussion of how the
61:1905:185024:20:20:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:information might be used has focused on traditional human resource–management tasks, namely, hiring,
61:1906:185125:20:21:72:540:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:firing, and compensation. By contrast, very little is known about how the availability of new information, or
61:1907:185234:21:20:72:540:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the experience of being evaluated, might change teacher effort and effectiveness.  Dobbie and Fryer (2013)
61:1908:185340:20:20:72:486:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:report that teacher feedback is one of the variables most correlated with charter school success.
61:1909:185437:20:21:88:539:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In the research reported here, we study one approach to teacher feedback:  practice-based assessment
61:1910:185537:21:20:72:540:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that relies on multiple, highly structured classroom observations conducted by experienced peer teachers
61:1911:185641:20:20:72:540:301:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and administrators.  While this approach contrasts with principal walk-through styles of class observation,
61:1912:185748:20:21:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:its use is on the rise in new and proposed evaluation systems in which rigorous classroom observation is
61:1913:185852:21:20:72:484:260:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:often combined with other measures, such as teacher value-added based on student test scores.
61:1914:185945:20:20:88:539:240:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Proponents of evaluation systems that include high-quality classroom observations point to their poten-
61:1915:186048:20:21:72:540:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tial value for improving instruction (see “Capturing the Dimensions of Effective Teaching,” Features, Fall
61:1916:186154:21:20:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:2012).  Individualized, specific information about performance is especially scarce in the teaching profes-
61:1917:186261:20:20:72:540:179:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sion, suggesting that a lack of information on how to improve could be a substantial barrier to individual
61:1918:186367:20:21:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:improvement among teachers.  Well-designed evaluations might fill that knowledge gap in several ways.
61:1919:186468:21:20:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:First, teachers could gain information through the formal scoring and feedback routines of an evaluation
61:1920:186572:20:20:72:540:118:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:program.  Second, evaluation could encourage teachers to be generally more self-reflective, regardless of
61:1921:186677:20:21:72:540:98:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the evaluative criteria. Third, the evaluation process could create more opportunities for conversations with
61:1922:186786:21:0:72:328:77:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:other teachers and administrators about effective practices.
62:1923:186848:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Taylor  and  Tyler  (2012),  using  a  quasi-experimental  design,  find  that  teachers  are  more  effective  at
62:1924:186962:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:raising student achievement during the school year when they are being evaluated as opposed to previous
62:1925:187065:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years,  and even more effective in the years after evaluation.  A student instructed by a teacher after that
62:1926:187173:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher has been through an evaluation scored about eleven percent of a standard deviation (4.5 percentile
62:1927:187279:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:points for a median student) higher in math than a similar student taught by the same teacher before the
62:1928:187383:21:36:72:170:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teacher was evaluated.
62:1929:187405:36:28:72:200:573:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.3.3    School Management
62:1930:187431:28:20:72:540:545:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Bloom et al. (2015) identify an interesting relationship between management quality of 1,800 high schools
62:1931:187536:20:20:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from  eight  countries  and  student  achievement  in  those  schools.   They  find  a  strong  correlation  between
62:1932:187652:20:21:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:higher management quality and better educational outcomes.  Dobbie and Fryer (2013) use variation in the
62:1933:187756:21:20:72:540:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:management practices of New York City charter schools to investigate the characteristics that differentiate
62:1934:187863:20:20:72:540:464:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:those that increase student achievement (as measured by standardized test scores) and those that do not
62:1935:187966:20:21:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increase achievement.  Using survey and administrative data from 39 New York City charter schools, they
62:1936:188069:21:20:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:correlated the policies of each school with the school’s individual impact on math and reading achievement.
62:1937:188176:20:20:72:540:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Dobbie and Fryer (2013) report that traditional inputs (i.e.  class size, per pupil expenditure, the fraction of
62:1938:188288:20:21:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers with no certification, and the fraction of teachers with an advanced degree) are not correlated with
62:1939:188397:21:20:72:540:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school effectiveness. Instead, they found that frequent teacher feedback, the use of data to guide instruction,
62:1940:188508:20:20:72:540:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:high-dosage tutoring, increased instructional time, and high expectations are highly correlated with schools’
62:1941:188617:20:20:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts on math and reading. In this section, we present studies that explore causal impacts of some of the
62:1942:188724:20:33:72:447:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:management practices discussed in Bloom et al. (2015) and Dobbie and Fryer (2013).
62:1943:188806:33:20:72:262:269:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:A. USINGDATA  TODRIVEINSTRUCTION
62:1944:188838:20:20:88:539:249:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Carlson et al. (2011) present results from a large randomized study that investigates the impacts of data-
62:1945:188944:20:21:71:539:229:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:driven reform on student achievement in mathematics and reading.  The study included over 500 schools
62:1946:189045:21:20:71:539:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from 59 school districts across seven states.   Districts randomly assigned to treatment implemented a 3-
62:1947:189150:20:20:71:539:188:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:year data-driven reform initiative with the support of consultants from the Johns Hopkins Center for Data-
62:1948:189256:20:21:71:539:168:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Driven Reform in Education (CDDRE). Control districts implemented the same initiative, but one year after
62:1949:189361:21:20:71:539:147:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:random assignment.  Carlson et al.  (2011) utilize the delayed start to investigate the causal impacts of the
62:1950:189470:20:20:71:539:127:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:first year of the CDDRE initiative on student achievement outcomes. The first year of the CDDRE initiative
62:1951:189576:20:21:71:539:107:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:focuses on developing and evaluating quarterly benchmark assessments, reviewing all available data to better
62:1952:189684:21:0:71:539:86:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:understand the needs of the district, and conducting leadership and data interpretation training for district
63:1953:189795:0:20:72:155:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and school leaders.
63:1954:189814:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The participating districts were selected through an extensive recruitment process.  The Department of
63:1955:189916:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Education of each state nominated districts with a large number of low performing schools to participate
63:1956:190020:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the study. District officials of the nominated districts were contacted and those that agreed to participate
63:1957:190131:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were included in the randomization procedure.  Further, for each participating district, the district officials
63:1958:190242:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:specified which schools in their district they wanted to participate in the experiment.  Generally, low per-
63:1959:190350:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:forming schools were selected.  Following the selection of schools, districts were stratified by recruitment
63:1960:190458:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:wave and state and randomly assigned to treatment or control.  Treatment schools implemented CDDRE
63:1961:190556:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:data-driven initiative and control schools continued business-as-usual for one year and then implemented
63:1962:190660:20:20:72:154:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the same initiative.
63:1963:190680:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In order to assess the impact of the intervention, results from state-administered achievement tests were
63:1964:190785:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:collected for each participating school.  Carlson et al.  (2011) found treatment had a significant impact on
63:1965:190893:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student math scores but found no significant effect for reading scores – treatment schools increased students’
63:1966:191003:20:21:72:460:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math scores by 0.059σ(0.029) and increased students’ reading scores by 0.033σ(0.020).
63:1967:191088:21:20:88:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In addition to providing constructive feedback for teachers, collecting teacher data could also be a useful
63:1968:191195:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tool for leaders in managing their schools.  Rockoff et al.  (2012) investigate the impact of giving over 200
63:1969:191304:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:New York City principals objective performance evaluations of the teachers in their schools.  All schools
63:1970:191409:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in NYC that contained any grades four through eight were eligible to participate (over 1,000 schools); 223
63:1971:191515:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:signed up and completed the necessary survey to be included in the experiment.  Participating principals
63:1972:191619:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:were stratified by grade configuration and assigned randomly to treatment or control.  Treatment principals
63:1973:191726:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:received reports detailing the value-added of the teachers in their school relative to similar teachers in NYC
63:1974:191836:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and  training  on  how  to  use  and  interpret  this  data.   Rockoff  et  al.   (2012)  find  evidence  that  principals
63:1975:191958:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:do  use  this  information  to  update  their  beliefs  of  the  teachers  in  the  school.   Using  baseline  and  post-
63:1976:192079:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:intervention surveys that solicited principals’ evaluation of their teachers, they find that treatment principals
63:1977:192192:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:update their beliefs in the direction of the teacher value-added detailed in the report.  Moreover, consistent
63:1978:192302:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:with a Bayesian learning model, principals put more weight on the teacher value-added information when
63:1979:192404:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that information is more precise than their prior beliefs and they put more weight on their prior beliefs when
63:1980:192514:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the relative precision is reversed.   Providing this information to principals led to an increase in turnover
63:1981:192623:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for teachers with low performance estimates and had a positive impact on students’ math achievement for
63:1982:192726:20:33:72:444:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students assigned to teachers that remained in the intervention throughout its entirety.
63:1983:192814:33:0:72:141:89:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:B. CLASSSIZE
64:1984:192828:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Project STAR was an experiment carried out in 79 Tennessee schools from 1985 to 1989 where 11,600
64:1985:192925:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students in grades K to 3 were randomly assigned to small classes (13-17 students), regular classes (22-
64:1986:193029:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:25 students), or regular classes with a full-time aide.  At the time, the statewide pupil-to-teacher ratio was
64:1987:193139:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:22.3,  so regular classes represented close to the average classroom size in the state.   At the time of the
64:1988:193247:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiment, kindergarten was not compulsory in Tennessee, so many new students entered schools in first
64:1989:193350:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grade. Students who entered a participating school after the 1985-1986 school year were randomly assigned
64:1990:193455:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to one of the three types of classes.  Additionally, students in regular classes and in regular classes with
64:1991:193563:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:an aide were randomly reassigned between these two types of classes at the end of kindergarten. However,
64:1992:193667:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:kindergartners initially assigned to small classes remained in small classes throughout the entire experiment.
64:1993:193777:20:20:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Using a student’s initial assignment to one of the three groups, Krueger (1999) estimated the impact of
64:1994:193880:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reduced class size and teacher aides on an index of scores from the math, reading, and word subtests of
64:1995:193983:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the Stanford Achievement Test.  Krueger (1999) found that for grades K-3, students scored about five to
64:1996:194086:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:seven percentile points higher on the index than students assigned to a regular class without an aide. These
64:1997:194194:20:21:72:539:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:results correspond to effect sizes in the range of 0.19σ-0.28σand represent 64 to 82 percent of the white-
64:1998:194300:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:black test score gap in the data.  Additionally, there was some evidence that regular classrooms with aides
64:1999:194407:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outperformed regular classrooms without aides—the estimates for aide classrooms tended to be small and
64:2000:194509:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:positive, but only the first grade results were statistically significant with an impact of 1.48 percentile points.
64:2001:194624:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:When exploring heterogeneous treatment effects, Krueger (1999) found that smaller class sizes were more
64:2002:194727:20:32:72:310:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effective for students on free lunch and black students.
64:2003:194783:32:20:72:165:313:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:C. EXTENDEDTIME
64:2004:194798:20:21:88:539:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:There are very few randomized trials that expose students to higher quantities of schooling. Zvoch and
64:2005:194900:21:20:72:540:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Stevens (2012) show that a summer literacy program has enormous impacts on kindergarten and first grade
64:2006:195003:20:20:72:540:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:reading test scores. In this study, the researchers invited students to a five-week summer program that lasted
64:2007:195113:20:21:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for 3.5 hours a day, four days a week.  In the program, students received classroom instruction on funda-
64:2008:195218:21:20:72:540:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mental literacy topics, were assigned homework, completed in-class work packets, and practiced literacy
64:2009:195321:20:20:72:540:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:skills in small groups with students of a similar skill level.  The summer program was typically reserved
64:2010:195426:20:21:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for struggling students that scored below a cutoff point on the spring standardized tests.  However, for this
64:2011:195535:21:20:72:540:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:study, the district established upper bounds so that approximately 50 kindergartners and 50 first graders fell
64:2012:195645:20:20:72:540:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the range between the cutoff scores and the upper bound scores.  These students were considered the
64:2013:195747:20:21:72:540:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experimental sample and half were randomly invited to participate in the program.  At posttest, Zvoch and
64:2014:195852:21:0:72:539:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Stevens (2012) found that the summer program on average increased reading test scores by 0.69σfor the
65:2015:195955:0:20:72:233:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:kindergarten and first grade students.
65:2016:195993:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:However, Holmes and McConnell (1990) utilized a larger sample of students to investigate the impact of
65:2017:196095:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:full-day versus half-day kindergarten instruction and found no significantly positive impacts.  In fact, their
65:2018:196205:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:study provided evidence that half-day kindergarten students perform better on math achievement tests than
65:2019:196310:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:full-day kindergartners.  The experiment randomly assigned twenty elementary schools to either a full or
65:2020:196414:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:half-day schedule.  Holmes and McConnell found that full-day kindergartners had math scores that were
65:2021:196515:20:20:72:429:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.29σlower and reading scores that were 0.11σhigher than the half-day students.
65:2022:196594:20:21:88:539:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:An experiment that investigated extended day impacts in a slightly older sample was Meyer and Van
65:2023:196691:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Klaveren (2013).  This experiment randomly invited Dutch 5th, 6th, and 7th grade students to participate
65:2024:196795:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in an extended school day program.  The program consisted of a classroom of approximately ten students
65:2025:196897:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:receiving an additional two hours of language instruction, two hours of math instruction, and one hour of
65:2026:197002:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:excursions per week. Meyer and Van Klaveren found that assignment to treatment increased math scores by
65:2027:197105:20:20:72:521:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.087σ(0.067) and increased reading scores by 0.005σ(0.081). Neither of these effects are significant.
65:2028:197207:20:21:88:539:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Taking the treatment effects at face value, one potential explanation for the patterns in the experimental
65:2029:197313:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:data is that increasing the amount of time students spend in class per day is not as effective as extending the
65:2030:197424:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school year.  Put differently, if there are concavities in human capital production as a function of time and
65:2031:197533:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students are at the point of diminishing marginal returns for a given day but not for a given year, this can
65:2032:197641:21:36:72:175:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:rationalize the findings.
65:2033:197666:36:27:72:229:329:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:3.3.4    Market-Based Approaches
65:2034:197698:27:21:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In recent years,  developed countries across the globe have increased the scope of schooling alternatives
65:2035:197803:21:20:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:available to students—an approach long advocated by leading economists (Friedman 1955; Becker 1995;
65:2036:197902:20:20:72:540:261:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Hoxby 2002).  Creating a competitive and active marketplace has the potential to improve educational out-
65:2037:198007:20:21:72:540:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:comes because schools would have more incentive to improve in response to increased market pressure. To
65:2038:198110:21:20:72:540:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the extent that match quality between a school and a student is important, school choice programs may also
65:2039:198216:20:20:72:473:200:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:yield benefits simply by increasing the set of schools over which a student is able to choose.
65:2040:198310:20:21:88:539:180:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:For these approaches to be an effective means of reform, however, it is necessary that students benefit
65:2041:198413:21:20:72:540:159:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:from the opportunity to attend sought-after schools, and that these improvements are apparent to students
65:2042:198518:20:20:72:540:139:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and parents.  The goal of this subsection is to understand the measurable achievement benefits accrued to
65:2043:198623:20:33:72:322:119:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students when there is more flexibility and school choice.
65:2044:198681:33:0:72:138:86:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:A. VOUCHERS
66:2045:198694:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:There have been a series of important studies that exploit randomized voucher lotteries to estimate the
66:2046:198797:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:effect of attending a private school for youth at various ages.  The Milwaukee voucher program, offering
66:2047:198901:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:vouchers to a limited number of low-income students to attend one of three private nonsectarian schools in
66:2048:199007:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the district, is the most prominent of these. Analyses of this program obtain sharply conflicting estimates of
66:2049:199117:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the impact on achievement depending upon the assumptions made to deal with selective attrition of lottery
66:2050:199222:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:losers from the sample (Witte et al. 1995; Greene et al. 1999; Witte 1997; Rouse 1998). Although in theory
66:2051:199328:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomization provides an ideal context for evaluating the benefits of expanding parental choice sets, in the
66:2052:199437:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Milwaukee case, less than half of the unsuccessful applicants returned to the public schools and those who
66:2053:199543:21:20:72:387:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:did return were from less educated, lower income families (Witte 1997).
66:2054:199614:20:20:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Rouse (1998) used a typical ITT specification to evaluate the Milwaukee voucher program.  Compar-
66:2055:199711:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ing lottery winners to lottery losers, she found that being selected for the choice program had significant
66:2056:199818:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts on math achievement but insignificant impacts on reading. Students who won the lottery scored ap-
66:2057:199923:20:20:72:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:proximately 1.5-2.3 percentile points (0.08σ-0.12σ) more per year in math compared to lottery losers. This
66:2058:200029:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:suggests effect sizes on the order of 0.32σ-0.48σfor four years of school.  The results in Rouse (1998) are
66:2059:200136:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:robust to various methods of imputing missing data and attrition from the sample – when imputing missing
66:2060:200240:20:20:72:415:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:observations, estimates remained in the range of 1.38 to 2.31 percentile points.
66:2061:200320:20:21:88:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The DC Opportunity Scholarship Program (OSP) is another voucher program that provides up to $7,500
66:2062:200418:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to low-income families in the District of Columbia to send their children to participating private schools.
66:2063:200525:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Wolf et al. (2010) use 2,300 applicants to a series of lotteries in 2004 and 2005 to evaluate the impact of the
66:2064:200636:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:OSP. The study found that the OSP had no impact on student achievement but increased students’ chance of
66:2065:200740:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:graduation. Additionally, parents of students who were offered a scholarship had a higher satisfaction with
66:2066:200847:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools and rated schools as safer. This result is significant regardless of whether a student actually used the
66:2067:200959:20:20:72:187:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:offered scholarship or not.
66:2068:200986:20:21:88:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Mayer et al. (2002) present results from the third year of a randomized evaluation of the School Choice
66:2069:201089:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Scholarships Foundation Program in NYC. In 1997,  the program provided scholarships of up to $1,400
66:2070:201188:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:annually for up to four years via lottery to low-income families with students in grades K-4. The scholarship
66:2071:201297:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:could be used to pay tuition at a religious or secular school of the family’s choosing. Fifty-three percent of
66:2072:201407:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students who were offered scholarships used the scholarship for at least three full years.  The families that
66:2073:201516:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:did not utilize the offered scholarship claimed they were unable to do so because they were unable to afford
66:2074:201624:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the tuition and expenses that the scholarship did not cover or were unable to find a school in a convenient
66:2075:201731:21:20:72:110:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:location.
66:2076:201740:20:0:88:539:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Through parent and student surveys, Mayer et al.  (2002) found that the private schools these students
67:2077:201844:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:elected to attend were indeed different from the public schools non-participants remained in.  Parents with
67:2078:201951:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students who switched to private schools reported that the schools had smaller class sizes; were more likely
67:2079:202059:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to have computer laboratories,  after-school programs,  and tutor programs;  had less incidents of students
67:2080:202166:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:destroying property, fighting, cheating, and racial conflict; communicated more with parents; allowed par-
67:2081:202272:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ents to spend less time helping their children with homework; and this resulted in an overall higher level of
67:2082:202381:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:satisfaction with their students’ school. Students who switched reported that students in private school were
67:2083:202490:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:more likely to get along with teachers, were more proud of their school, were less likely to be put down
67:2084:202594:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:by teachers, and were asked to complete more homework.  Additinoally, students reported that the private
67:2085:202698:21:20:72:425:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools had stricter behavior rules, and there was a lower prevalence of cheating.
67:2086:202780:20:20:88:539:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Although there was evidence that students offered a scholarship switched to better school environments,
67:2087:202883:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Mayer et al.  (2002) found that three years after random assignment, there was no average treatment effect
67:2088:202989:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on students’ performance. Moreover, students who ever attended a private school and students who attended
67:2089:203094:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for all three years did no better than students who never attended a private school.  These results are robust
67:2090:203204:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:across grade levels,  but there is evidence of heterogeneous treatment effects across races – Mayer et al.
67:2091:203310:21:31:72:412:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(2002) found positive effects on the standardized test scores of black students.
67:2092:203390:31:20:88:540:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The meta-coefficient on voucher experiments is 0.024σ(0.021) for math achievement and 0.030σ(0.024)
67:2093:203489:20:20:72:540:375:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:for reading achievement.  Relative to their popularity with politicians, the lack of effectiveness of voucher
67:2094:203598:20:20:72:540:355:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:programs is surprising.  Rather than focusing on achievement, many use a revealed preference argument to
67:2095:203702:20:21:72:487:335:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conclude families who make active choices – even if achievement is unaffected – are better off.
67:2096:203797:21:20:88:539:314:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Before one dismisses them entirely, there are two key pieces of data missing on voucher experiments.
67:2097:203897:20:20:72:540:294:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:First, in the average voucher experiment a student enrolls in a private school between grades K and 8. There
67:2098:204005:20:21:72:529:274:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:is no experiment that tests the full pre-K through high school graduation treatment. This seems essential.
67:2099:204111:21:20:88:539:253:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Second, although vouchers are a market-based reform, we do not know what happens if there are enough
67:2100:204211:20:20:72:540:233:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:vouchers in a concentrated area to allow the market to respond by altering the supply (and scope) of schools
67:2101:204319:20:21:72:540:213:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:available to educate disadvantaged children.  Because all the experiments have been relatively small, one
67:2102:204424:21:16:72:318:192:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:cannot assess the potential general equilibrium effects.27
67:2103:204482:16:14:84:539:176:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:27A notable counter example is a recent experiment implemented in India.  Muralidharan and Sundararaman (2015) conducted
67:2104:204602:14:11:72:540:162:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:an experiment using 180 villages from the Indian state of Andhra Pradesh in which they randomly assigned villages to treatment
67:2105:204728:11:11:72:540:151:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:or control and then awarded private school vouchers to public school applicants through random lotteries in the treatment villages.
67:2106:204859:11:11:72:540:140:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:Two and four years after randomization,  they found that winning a voucher had no impact on Telugu (native language),  math,
67:2107:204983:11:11:72:540:129:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:English, and science/social studies achievement. However, the program had large impacts on Hindi test scores, a subject not taught
67:2108:205113:11:11:72:540:118:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:in public schools.  Since private schools are approximately a third of the cost of public schools, Muralidharan and Sundararaman
67:2109:205241:11:11:72:540:107:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:(2015) conclude that private schools are a much more cost-effective way of teaching students.  Further, they found no evidence of
67:2110:205370:11:11:72:540:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:spillovers (negative or positive) on the achievement of public school students that did not apply to the voucher program or on non-
