67:2111:205501:11:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:voucher private students.  This suggests that vouchers are a cost-effective way to potentially increase student achievement without
67:2112:205632:11:0:72:165:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:any negative externalities.
68:2113:205661:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:An ideal voucher experiment might take a large state with multiple school districts and randomly im-
68:2114:205761:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:plement voucher programs or Education Savings Accounts in half of the districts and analyze both student
68:2115:205865:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement and the market response.  The vouchers could be risk adjusted – more disadvantaged children
68:2116:205968:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:receive more school funding – or contain location preferences that would induce a more aggressive supply
68:2117:206072:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:response in blighted communities. These ideas only scratch the surface of what is possible and have not been
68:2118:206180:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:evaluated in a compelling way. Thus, whether the Friedman (1955) vision for public schools is effective at
68:2119:206286:20:32:72:255:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:producing human capital is still unknown.
68:2120:206327:32:21:72:165:557:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:B. SCHOOLCHOICE
68:2121:206342:21:20:88:539:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Cullen, Jacob, and Levitt (2006) present causal estimates of the impact of school choice on a variety
68:2122:206443:20:20:71:539:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of student outcomes.  Specifically, they utilize the random lotteries of oversubscribed schools in Chicago’s
68:2123:206551:20:21:71:539:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:open  enrollment  system.   This  system  allows  students  to  apply  to  public  magnet  schools  and  programs
68:2124:206664:21:20:71:539:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outside of their neighborhood school.28When oversubscribed, many Chicago Public Schools (CPS) use
68:2125:206761:20:20:71:539:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:random lotteries to offer admission to students.  The authors obtained the results of 194 such lotteries from
68:2126:206870:20:21:71:539:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:19  high  schools  in  CPS.  The  final  sample  consisted  of  14,434  students  who  applied  to  these  19  choice
68:2127:206987:21:20:71:243:414:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools in the spring of 2000 and 2001.
68:2128:207026:20:20:88:539:394:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The analysis in Cullen,  Jacob,  and Levitt (2006) finds little evidence that winning a lottery has any
68:2129:207129:20:20:71:539:374:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impact on traditional achievement measures such as test scores, graduation rates, attendance rates, or courses
68:2130:207239:20:21:71:539:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:taken. These results are robust to a variety of sensitivity analyses and are similar across student subgroups.
68:2131:207349:21:20:71:539:333:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In an attempt to better understand the findings, the authors explored potential mechanisms that could explain
68:2132:207458:20:20:71:539:313:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the zero-impact on academic outcomes.  They found little evidence of lottery winners and losers attending
68:2133:207563:20:21:71:539:293:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:similar  schools  (lottery  winners attended  schools with  higher  average  achievement,  lower  poverty rates,
68:2134:207675:21:20:71:539:272:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and higher graduation rates), of choice schools substituting for parental involvement, or of travel costs and
68:2135:207784:20:20:71:539:252:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:disruption of peer groups interfering with academic success.  Therefore, the results in Cullen, Jacob, and
68:2136:207890:20:21:71:539:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Levitt (2006) seem to suggest that the measurable school inputs of these choice schools have little causal
68:2137:207996:21:20:71:248:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impact on students’ academic outcomes.
68:2138:208034:20:20:88:539:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another possibility is that students and parents apply to choice schools for non-academic reasons. Using
68:2139:208138:20:21:71:539:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:survey data collected by the Consortium on Chicago School Research for CPS students in grades 6-10 in
68:2140:208239:21:20:71:539:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:spring 2001, the authors investigated this possibility. They found evidence of some positive effects on non-
68:2141:208347:20:20:71:539:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:traditional outcomes, possibly supporting the hypothesis that students and parents choose choice schools for
68:2142:208455:20:22:71:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:non-academic reasons. Cullen, Jacob, and Levitt (2006) found that lottery winners report fewer incidents of
68:2143:208562:22:14:84:539:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:28Magnet schools are different from traditional public schools in that each magnet school tends to have a specific educational
68:2144:208688:14:0:72:411:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:theme and students can choose to enroll in a school based on their interest in a school’s theme.
69:2145:208786:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:disciplinary action, fewer arrests, and lower incarceration rates. However, lottery winners are not statistically
69:2146:208899:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:different from lottery losers for other outcomes such as liking school, trusting their teachers, and having high
69:2147:209011:21:20:72:189:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:expectations for the future.
69:2148:209039:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another example of a school choice experiment is Connecticut’s interdistrict magnet school program.
69:2149:209138:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:In 1996, the Connecticut Supreme Court ruled that students in Hartford public schools were denied equal
69:2150:209241:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:educational  opportunities  due  to  racial  and  economic  isolation.   One  of  the  state’s  many  responses  was
69:2151:209357:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to foster the growth of interdistrict magnet schools.  A decade after the the Connecticut Supreme Court’s
69:2152:209462:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ruling, there were 54 magnet schools in operation in Connecticut and 41 of these served students residing
69:2153:209567:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in Hartford, New Haven, or Waterbury.  Additionally, interdistrict magnets serve two or more districts and
69:2154:209673:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:all students residing in these districts are eligible to enroll in the school. Urban students that elect to attend
69:2155:209787:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:magnet schools are typically moving to schools where there are fewer students eligible for free lunch, more
69:2156:209894:21:20:72:461:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:white students, and higher average scores on standardized mathematics and reading tests.
69:2157:209982:20:20:88:539:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Bifulco et al.  (2009) evaluated the impact of Connecticut’s interdistrict magnet schools using the ran-
69:2158:210086:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:dom admission lotteries of two oversubscribed magnets serving Hartford and four surrounding suburban
69:2159:210186:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:districts.  One of these schools served grades 6-8 and the other served grades 6-12.  The authors obtained
69:2160:210292:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:admission data for the 2003 and 2004 sixth grade lotteries at these schools as well as student-level test
69:2161:210397:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores from the Connecticut State Department of Education for the 2001-2002 to 2006-2007 school years.
69:2162:210499:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The final sample for these two schools consisted of 553 students in 12 oversubscribed lotteries (both schools
69:2163:210608:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:conducted lotteries by district for each year), 164 of which were eventually offered admission to one of the
69:2164:210716:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:two magnets. Comparing the eighth grade outcomes of lottery winners to lottery losers, Bifulco et al. (2009)
69:2165:210824:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:find that students offered admission to the magnet schools scored 0.109σhigher on math and 0.252σhigher
69:2166:210927:21:32:71:466:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on reading tests, of which only the latter was statistically significant at conventional levels.
69:2167:211023:32:20:72:178:252:11:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:B:C. CHARTERSCHOOLS
69:2168:211040:20:21:88:539:232:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:A charter school is a school that receives public funding but operates independently of the established
69:2169:211143:21:20:71:539:211:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:public school system in which it is located. They exist (and are increasing in demand) across the developed
69:2170:211250:20:20:71:539:191:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:world  –  from  Australia  to  England  and  Wales.   Figure  2  shows  the  increase  in  the  number  of  students
69:2171:211366:20:21:71:329:171:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attending charter schools in the United States and England.
69:2172:211425:21:20:88:539:150:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:When originally conceived, charter schools offered two distinct promises:  First, they were to serve as
69:2173:211528:20:20:71:539:130:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:an escape hatch for students in failing schools.  Second, they were to use their legal and financial freedoms
69:2174:211637:20:21:71:539:110:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to create and incubate new educational practices that could be used to inform traditional public schools with
69:2175:211746:21:0:71:212:89:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:new ideas and fresh approaches.
70:2176:211779:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In America, charter schools currently enroll almost four percent of all students.  Some of these schools
70:2177:211883:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have shown remarkable success in increasing test scores – closing the racial achievement gap in just a few
70:2178:211989:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years. For example, schools such as the Success Academy Charter Schools in New York City, YES Prep in
70:2179:212090:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Houston, and charter schools in the Harlem Children’s Zone have become beacons of hope, demonstrating
70:2180:212191:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the enormous potential to improve student achievement in the most blighted communities. Others, however,
70:2181:212295:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have failed to increase achievement and have actually performed substantially worse than their traditional
70:2182:212401:20:32:72:493:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:counterparts. In this scenario, students would have been better off not attending a charter school.
70:2183:212500:32:21:72:194:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:C:Evaluating Charter Schools
70:2184:212526:21:20:88:540:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The method for evaluating charter schools is remarkably consistent across the literature.29The literature
70:2185:212631:20:20:72:540:516:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:estimates two empirical models – ITT effects and Local Average Treatment Effects (LATEs) – which provide
70:2186:212735:20:21:72:540:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a set of causal estimates of the impact of attending a charter school on outcomes. The ITT estimates measure
70:2187:212843:21:20:72:540:475:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the causal effect of winning a charter lottery by comparing the average outcomes of students who ‘won’ the
70:2188:212949:20:37:72:356:455:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:lottery to the average outcomes of students who ‘lost’ the lottery:
70:2189:213016:37:11:140:272:418:11:g_d0_f4:16:g_d0_f8:?:outcomei=μ+γXi+πZi+∑
70:2190:213036:11:0:266:268:407:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:?:j
70:2191:213037:0:11:274:345:418:11:g_d0_f8:16:g_d0_f8:?:νjLotteryi j+∑
70:2192:213051:11:0:339:341:407:8:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:?:j
70:2193:213052:0:38:346:540:418:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f2:A:φjLotteryi j∗1(siblingi)+ηi(1)
70:2194:213082:38:21:72:539:380:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:whereZiis an indicator for winning an admissions lottery, andXiincludes controls for student-level demo-
70:2195:213186:21:20:72:540:359:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:graphics such as gender, race, special education status, eligibility for free or reduced-price lunch, receipt of
70:2196:213298:20:20:72:540:339:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Limited English Proficiency (LEP) services, and a quadratic in two prior years of math and ELA test scores.
70:2197:213405:20:21:72:540:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f2:B:Lotteryi jis an indicator for entering the lottery in yearj, and 1(siblingi)indicates whether studentihad a
70:2198:213512:21:20:72:539:298:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sibling enter the lottery in the same year.30Equation (1) identifies the impact ofbeing offered a chanceto
70:2199:213618:20:20:72:539:278:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:attend a charter school,π, where the lottery losers form the control group corresponding to the counterfac-
70:2200:213725:20:21:72:540:258:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tual state that would have occurred for students in the treatment group if they had not been offered a spot
70:2201:213832:21:20:72:540:237:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in the charter school.  Using this approach, the literature on charter effectiveness has quickly amassed an
70:2202:213939:20:20:72:171:217:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:interesting set of facts.
70:2203:213964:20:20:88:539:197:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:First, the typical charter school is no more effective at increasing test scores than the typical traditional
70:2204:214073:20:21:72:540:177:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:public school (Gleason et al. 2010). Evaluations that encompass the most representative samples of charter
70:2205:214179:21:20:72:540:156:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools show little impact.  Using lottery admissions data for 36 charter schools from around the nation,
70:2206:214284:20:26:72:540:136:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Gleason et al.  (2010) investigated the impact of charter schools on student outcomes.  They found that two
70:2207:214391:26:14:84:539:110:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:29The national charter school studies released by the Center for Research on Education Outcomes (CREDO) are anomalous in
70:2208:214511:14:8:72:531:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:that they use observational data instead of randomized admissions lotteries (Center for Research on Education Outcomes 2013).
70:2209:214636:8:14:84:539:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:30In typical charter lotteries, an offer is extended to all siblings when multiple siblings enter the same lottery and one sibling
70:2210:214766:14:0:72:91:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:wins.
71:2211:214773:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years after the random lotteries, students who won the lotteries scored, if anything, lower on standardized
71:2212:214880:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:test scores than students who lost the lotteries.31In addition, this national sample of charter schools had
71:2213:214987:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:no impact on students’ math and reading proficiency levels, number of days absent, and grade promotion.
71:2214:215090:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Gleason et al. (2010) found no impact of charter schools on student behavior and school disciplinary action,
71:2215:215198:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:but a higher fraction of lottery winners showed up late to school five or more days.  Although the average
71:2216:215304:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:charter school included in their study did not have any positive impacts on student outcomes, Gleason et al.
71:2217:215412:20:20:72:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(2010) found large, positive, and statistically significant impacts – ranging from 0.07σto 0.94σ– on every
71:2218:215518:20:21:72:410:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:measure of students’ and parents’ satisfaction with and perceptions of school.
71:2219:215596:21:20:88:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Second, an emerging body of research suggests that high-performing charter schools can significantly
71:2220:215696:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increase the achievement of poor urban students.  Students attending over-subscribed Boston-area charter
71:2221:215800:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools score approximately 0.4σhigher per year in math and 0.2σhigher per year in reading (Abdulka-
71:2222:215900:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:diroglu et al. 2011). Promise Academy students in the Harlem Children’s Zone (HCZ) score 0.229σhigher
71:2223:216001:20:20:71:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:per year in math and 0.047σhigher per year in reading (Dobbie and Fryer 2011). Students in the Knowledge
71:2224:216105:20:21:71:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:is Power Program (KIPP) schools – America’s largest network of charter schools – score 0.180σhigher per
71:2225:216208:21:20:71:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:year in math and 0.075σhigher per year in reading (Tuttle et al.  2013; Angrist et al.  2011).  The SEED
71:2226:216312:20:20:71:530:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:urban boarding school in Washington D.C., demonstrates similar test score gains (Curto and Fryer 2014).
71:2227:216415:20:21:88:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Third, charter schools are more effective at increasing math scores than reading scores. Abdulkadiroglu
71:2228:216518:21:20:71:539:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:et al.  (2011) and Angrist et al.  (2011) find that the treatment effect of attending an oversubscribed charter
71:2229:216629:20:20:71:539:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school is four times as large for math as reading.  Dobbie and Fryer (2011) demonstrate effects that are
71:2230:216733:20:20:71:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:almost 5 times as large in middle school and 1.6 times as large in elementary school in favor of math.  In
71:2231:216839:20:21:71:539:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:larger samples, Hoxby and Murarka (2009) report an effect size 2.5 times as large in New York City charters,
71:2232:216947:21:20:71:539:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Gleason et al.  (2010) show that an average urban charter school increases math scores by 0.16σwith
71:2233:217050:20:20:71:208:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:statistically 0 effect on reading.
71:2234:217084:20:21:88:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:According  to  the  National  Alliance  for  Public  Charter  Schools,  the  median  grade  served  by  charter
71:2235:217195:21:20:71:539:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools in the U.S. is sixth grade (usually students are 11-12 years old).  However, the achievement data
71:2236:217300:20:20:71:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:necessary to conduct evaluations of charter schools is typically not available for kindergarten through sec-
71:2237:217408:20:21:71:539:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ond grade students, so the average grade evaluated is most likely even higher.  The theory and empirical
71:2238:217512:21:20:71:539:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:findings discussed above suggest that the relatively late timing of charter school “interventions” might be an
71:2239:217622:20:32:71:348:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:important factor in the observed differential impacts by subject.
71:2240:217687:32:14:84:540:110:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:31The two-year ITT impact for the pooled sample is -0.08σ(p-value = 0.032) for reading scores and -0.06σ(p-value = 0.136)
71:2241:217808:14:11:72:540:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:for math test scores. Note that pooling results together masks heterogeneous treatment effects described in the paper. For example,
71:2242:217939:11:11:72:539:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f8:F:charter schools in large urban areas had a 0.16σimpact on math scores while schools outside of large urban areas had a -0.14σ
71:2243:218064:11:0:72:284:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:impact. Both of these impacts were statistically significant.
72:2244:218127:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another leading theory posits that reading scores are influenced by the language spoken when students
72:2245:218228:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:are outside of the classroom (Rickford 1999; Charity, Scarborough, and Griffin 2004). Charity, Scarborough,
72:2246:218335:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and  Griffin  (2004)  argue  that  if  students  speak  nonstandard  English  at  home  and  in  their  communities,
72:2247:218451:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increasing reading scores might be especially difficult.  This theory is consistent with the data and could
72:2248:218558:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:explain why students at an urban boarding school make similar progress on reading and math (Curto and
72:2249:218659:21:20:72:127:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Fryer 2014).
72:2250:218671:20:20:88:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Fourth,  there are important features of charter schools that seem to be correlated with their level of
72:2251:218774:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student achievement. It is important to note that these analyses are non-experimental. Angrist et al. (2013)
72:2252:218882:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:argue that both the urbanicity of charter schools and whether they adopt the so called “No Excuses” approach
72:2253:218990:20:20:72:399:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to culture and discipline are positive predictors of charter treatment effects.
72:2254:219069:20:21:88:539:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Dobbie and Fryer (2013) provide evidence on the determinants of charter school effectiveness by col-
72:2255:219169:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:lecting data on the inner-workings of 29 charter schools in New York City and correlating these data with
72:2256:219274:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:lottery-based estimates of each school’s effectiveness. Information on school practices were collected from
72:2257:219381:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a variety of sources.  Principal interviews asked about teacher development, instructional time, data driven
72:2258:219489:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:instruction, parent outreach, and school culture. Teacher interviews asked about professional development,
72:2259:219595:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school policies,  school culture,  and student assessment.   Student interviews asked about school environ-
72:2260:219702:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ment, school disciplinary policy, and future aspirations. Lesson plans were used to measure curricular rigor.
72:2261:219811:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Videotaped classroom observations were used to calculate the fraction of students on task throughout the
72:2262:219915:20:20:72:121:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school day.
72:2263:219926:20:20:88:539:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:School effectiveness is estimated by exploiting the fact that oversubscribed charter schools in New York
72:2264:220030:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:City are required to admit students via random lottery.  The variability inherent in the set of NYC charter
72:2265:220137:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools, combined with rich measures of school inputs and lottery-based estimates of each school’s impact
72:2266:220242:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on student achievement, provides an ideal opportunity to understand which inputs best explain school ef-
72:2267:220346:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fectiveness.   This,  coupled with some of the best practices of our meta-analysis,  provide the intellectual
72:2268:220455:21:20:72:314:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:backbone of the randomized field trial discussed below.
72:2269:220510:20:20:88:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Dobbie and Fryer (2013) find that input measures associated with a traditional resource-based model of
72:2270:220612:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:education – class size, per pupil expenditure, the fraction of teachers with no teaching certification, and the
72:2271:220723:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:fraction of teachers with an advanced degree – are not correlated with school effectiveness in our sample.
72:2272:220829:20:20:72:540:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Indeed, our data suggest that increasing resource-based inputs may marginally lower school effectiveness.
72:2273:220934:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:On the surface, this evidence may seem inconsistent with the important results reported in Krueger (1999).
72:2274:221040:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:There are a few ways to reconcile this.  First, Dobbie and Fryer (2013) analyzes charter schools in NYC,
72:2275:221144:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:whereas Krueger (1999) uses a sample of traditional public schools in Tennessee.  Second, the variation in
73:2276:221252:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Dobbie and Fryer (2013) comes from only 39 charter schools with relatively similar class sizes, whereas
73:2277:221355:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the thousands of treatment students in Krueger (1999) are placed in classrooms that are almost 40% smaller
73:2278:221461:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:than control classrooms. Third, Krueger’s analysis focused on students in grades kindergarten through third
73:2279:221568:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:whereas the correlations in Dobbie and Fryer (2013) used third through eighth grade test scores. Fourth, and
73:2280:221676:20:21:72:349:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:most important, the analysis in Krueger (1999) is experimental.
73:2281:221739:21:20:88:539:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In stark contrast, Dobbie and Fryer (2013) demonstrate that an index of five policies suggested by forty
73:2282:221843:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years of human capital research – frequent teacher feedback, data-driven instruction, high-dosage tutoring,
73:2283:221950:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increased instructional time, and a relentless focus on academic achievement – explains roughly half of the
73:2284:222057:21:44:72:326:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:variation in school effectiveness in both math and reading.
73:2285:222116:44:27:72:540:504:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:F:4    Combining What Works: Evidence from a Randomized Field Experiment
73:2286:222186:27:31:93:160:477:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:A:in Houston
73:2287:222196:31:21:72:540:446:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Improving the efficiency of the production of human capital is of great importance across the developed
73:2288:222299:21:20:72:540:425:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:world.  The United States spends $10,768 per pupil on primary and secondary education, ranking it fourth
73:2289:222403:20:20:72:540:405:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:among OECD countries (Aud et al.  2011).  Yet, among these same countries, American fifteen year-olds
73:2290:222504:20:20:72:540:385:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:rank twenty-fifth in math achievement, seventeenth in science, and fourteenth in reading (Fleischman 2010).
73:2291:222611:20:21:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:This is not a phenomenon that is unique to the United States. Other OECD countries are unable to translate
73:2292:222717:21:20:72:540:344:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:large amounts of educational spending into educational success.  For example, the two countries ranking
73:2293:222820:20:20:72:540:324:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:directly behind the United States with per pupil primary and secondary spending of $9,959 and $9,448 are,
73:2294:222925:20:21:72:540:304:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:respectively, Austria and Denmark (Aud et al.  2011).  However, Austrian fifteen year-olds rank eighteenth
73:2295:223031:21:20:72:540:283:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in math achievement, twenty-fourth in science, and thirty-first in reading and Danish fifteen year-olds rank
73:2296:223139:20:20:72:445:263:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:thirteenth in math, twentieth in science, and nineteenth in reading (Fleischman 2010).
73:2297:223225:20:21:88:539:243:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Traditionally, there have been two approaches to increasing educational efficiency: (1) expand the scope
73:2298:223329:21:20:72:540:222:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:of available educational options in the hope that the market will drive out ineffective schools, or (2) directly
73:2299:223441:20:20:72:329:202:11:g_d0_f2:8:g_d0_f2:B:manipulate inputs to the educational production function.32
73:2300:223500:20:21:88:539:182:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:As our meta-analysis demonstrates,  market-based reforms such as school choice or school vouchers
73:2301:223597:21:20:72:540:161:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:have, at best, a modest impact on student achievement. This suggests that these approaches – implemented
73:2302:223701:20:20:72:540:141:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in their current form – are unlikely to significantly increase the efficiency of the public school system, subject
73:2303:223815:20:22:72:324:121:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to the important caveats discussed in the previous section.
73:2304:223874:22:14:84:539:99:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:32Increasing standards and accountability reflect a third approach to education reform. There is evidence that increased account-
73:2305:224003:14:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:ability via the No Child Left Behind Act had a positive impact on math test scores (though not reading test scores) and on wages
73:2306:224131:11:0:72:227:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:(Dee and Jacob 2011; Deming et al. 2013).
74:2307:224174:0:20:88:539:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Another approach is to inject the best practices known from the set of randomized field experiments
74:2308:224273:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:completed  to  date  –  along  with  the  correlates  gleaned  from  analyzing  the  inner-workings  of  successful
74:2309:224388:21:20:72:534:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:charter schools – in an experiment in traditional public schools. This is precisely the goal of Fryer (2014).
74:2310:224497:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Between the 2010-2011 and 2012-2013 school years, Fryer (2014) implemented important elements of
74:2311:224593:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the above education best-practices in twenty of the lowest performing schools (containing more than 12,000
74:2312:224699:21:20:72:196:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students) in Houston, Texas.
74:2313:224727:20:20:88:539:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To increase time on task, the school day was lengthened by one hour and the school year was lengthened
74:2314:224829:20:21:72:540:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:by ten days in the nine secondary (middle and high) schools. This was 21 percent more time in school than
74:2315:224934:21:20:72:540:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students in these schools spent in the pre-treatment year and roughly the same as achievement-increasing
74:2316:225038:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:charter schools in New York City.  In addition, students were strongly encouraged and even incentivized
74:2317:225141:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to attend classes on Saturday.  In the eleven elementary schools, the length of the day and the year were
74:2318:225246:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:not changed, but non-instructional activities (e.g.  twenty-minute bathroom breaks) were reduced.  This is
74:2319:225352:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:consistent with the correlations in Dobbie and Fryer (2013) and the randomized field trial reported in Meyer
74:2320:225460:20:21:72:184:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and Van Klaveren (2013).
74:2321:225484:21:20:88:539:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In an effort to improve the human capital available to teach students and lead schools, nineteen out of
74:2322:225587:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:twenty principals were removed and 46 percent of teachers left or were removed before the experiment
74:2323:225687:20:21:72:540:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:began.  Some teachers left because they believed the program was too disruptive.  Others were removed
74:2324:225788:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:because they were too resistant to the changes.  Any teacher, independent of skill level, who demonstrated
74:2325:225894:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a desire to implement the proposed changes with fidelity was retained.  As part of the turnaround efforts,
74:2326:226000:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:teachers received both managed professional development and frequent feedback as a part of a more holistic
74:2327:226106:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:evaluation system.  The managed professional development was similar to the Success for All treatment
74:2328:226207:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:described in Borman et al.  (2007).  The frequent feedback was similar to the quasi-experimental program
74:2329:226311:20:20:72:234:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:evaluated in Taylor and Tyler (2012).
74:2330:226348:20:21:88:539:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:To enhance student-level differentiation, all fourth, sixth and ninth graders received high-dosage math
74:2331:226451:21:20:72:540:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tutoring and extra reading or math instruction was provided to students in other grades who had previously
74:2332:226557:20:20:72:540:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:performed below grade level. Similar to the Chicago BAM experiment described above, the tutoring model
74:2333:226659:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:was adapted from the MATCH school in Boston – a charter school that largely adheres to the methods
74:2334:226757:21:20:72:239:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:described in Dobbie and Fryer (2013).
74:2335:226794:20:20:88:539:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In order to help teachers use interim data on student performance to guide and inform instructional prac-
74:2336:226899:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tice, schools were required to administer interim assessments every three to four weeks and provided with
74:2337:227004:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:three cumulative benchmark assessments, as well as assistance in analyzing and presenting student perfor-
74:2338:227109:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:mance data on these assessments.  Yet, as Rockoff et al.  (2012) and Dobbie and Fryer (2013) demonstrate,
75:2339:227216:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:data alone is not enough.  Dobbie and Fryer (2013) argue that the use of interim assessment data is only
75:2340:227320:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:correlated with achievement for schools who can articulate a precise plan of how they will change student
75:2341:227425:21:20:72:371:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:grouping or pedagogy or some other strategy in response to the data.
75:2342:227493:20:20:88:539:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, to instill a culture of high expectations and college access, we started by setting clear expecta-
75:2343:227600:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:tions for school leadership. Schools were provided with a rubric for the school and classroom environment
75:2344:227705:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and were expected to implement school-parent-student contracts.  Specific student performance goals were
75:2345:227809:20:20:72:540:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:set for each school and the principal was held accountable and provided with financial incentives based on
75:2346:227915:20:21:72:123:569:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:these goals.
75:2347:227927:21:20:88:539:548:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Such invasive changes were possible,  in part,  because eleven of the twenty schools (nine secondary
75:2348:228027:20:20:72:540:528:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:and two elementary) were either “chronically low performing” or on the verge of being labeled as such and
75:2349:228132:20:21:72:540:508:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:subject to takeover by the state of Texas. Thus, despite our best efforts, random assignment was not a feasible
75:2350:228243:21:20:72:540:487:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:option for these schools.  To round out our sample of twenty schools and provide a way to choose between
75:2351:228347:20:20:72:540:467:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:alternative quasi-experimental specifications, we randomly selected nine additional elementary schools (vis-
75:2352:228455:20:21:72:540:447:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:`a-vis matched-pairs) from eighteen low – but not chronically low – performing schools. One of the randomly
75:2353:228562:21:20:72:540:426:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:selected treatment elementary schools closed before the start of the experiment so we had to drop it and its
75:2354:228670:20:20:72:540:406:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:matched pair from our experimental sample. Thus, our final experimental sample consists of sixteen schools.
75:2355:228777:20:21:88:539:386:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In the sample of sixteen elementary schools in which treatment and control were chosen by random
75:2356:228873:21:20:72:540:365:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assignment, providing estimates of the impact of injecting charter school best practices in traditional public
75:2357:228983:20:20:72:540:345:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools is straightforward.   In the remaining set of schools,  we use three separate statistical approaches
75:2358:229091:20:20:72:540:325:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:to understand the impact of the intervention.   Treatment is defined as being zoned to attend a treatment
75:2359:229196:20:21:72:540:305:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school for entering grade levels (e.g.   sixth and ninth) or having attended a treatment school in the pre-
75:2360:229303:21:20:72:540:284:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment year for returning grade levels. “Comparison school” attendees are all other students in Houston.
75:2361:229410:20:20:72:540:264:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:We begin by using district administrative data on student demographics and,  most importantly,  previous
75:2362:229514:20:21:72:540:244:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:years’ achievement, to fit least squares models. We then present two empirical models that instrument for a
75:2363:229621:21:20:72:411:223:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:student’s attendance in a treatment school with original treatment assignment.
75:2364:229699:20:20:88:539:203:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:All  statistical  approaches  lead  to  the  same  basic  conclusions.   Injecting  best  practices  from  charter
75:2365:229813:20:21:72:540:183:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:schools into low performing traditional public schools can significantly increase student achievement in
75:2366:229917:21:20:72:540:162:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:math  and  has  marginal,  if  any,  effect  on  English  Language  Arts  (hereafter  known  simply  as  “reading”)
75:2367:230032:20:20:72:539:142:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement.  Students in treatment elementary schools gain around 0.184σin math per year, relative to
75:2368:230134:20:21:72:540:122:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:comparison samples.  Taken at face value, this is enough to eliminate the racial achievement gap in math
75:2369:230238:21:20:72:540:101:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in Houston elementary schools in approximately three years. Students in treatment secondary schools gain
75:2370:230342:20:0:72:540:81:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:0.146σper year in math, decreasing the gap by one-half over the length of the demonstration project.  The
76:2371:230449:0:20:72:482:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:impacts on reading for both elementary and secondary schools are small and statistically zero.
76:2372:230543:20:21:88:539:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In the grade/subject areas in which we implemented all five policies described in Dobbie and Fryer
76:2373:230641:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(2013) – fourth, sixth, and ninth grade math – the increase in student achievement is substantially larger
76:2374:230747:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:than  the  increase  in  other  grades.   Relative  to  students  who  attended  control  schools,  fourth  graders  in
76:2375:230866:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:treatment schools scored 0.331σ(0.104) higher in math, per year.  Similarly, sixth and ninth grade math
76:2376:230969:21:37:72:442:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:scores increased 0.608σ(0.093), per year, relative to students in comparison schools.
76:2377:231054:37:20:72:540:572:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:F:4.1    Simulating the Potential Impact of Implementing Best Practices in Education on Wage
76:2378:231144:20:28:98:150:552:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A:Inequality
76:2379:231154:28:20:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:An important question is how much of the initial gaps described in the introduction to this chapter might be
76:2380:231262:20:21:72:540:504:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:eliminated if state, local, and federal governments focused on the experiments proven most effective through
76:2381:231370:21:20:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomized trials. Answering this question is, by definition, speculative – as it relies on extrapolations from
76:2382:231481:20:20:72:540:463:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cross-sectional relationships and assumptions on how human capital propagates through an individual’s life.
76:2383:231588:20:21:72:449:443:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Still, the exercise may be informative and we include it here as an illustrative exercise.
76:2384:231678:21:20:88:539:422:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Data on long-term follow-ups is sparse.  Perry Preschool, the Abecedarian Project, and the Moving to
76:2385:231778:20:20:72:540:402:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Opportunity experiments are notable exceptions.  As described above, MTO revealed that despite having
76:2386:231879:20:21:72:540:382:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:no significant impacts on children’s academic outcomes, better neighborhoods had important impacts on
76:2387:231980:21:20:72:540:361:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the  adulthood  outcomes  of  children  –  treatment  MTO  children  who  were  younger  than  13  years  old  at
76:2388:232093:20:20:72:540:341:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomization had 31% higher income, had higher college attendance rates, were less likely to be single
76:2389:232196:20:21:72:540:321:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:parents, and lived in better neighborhoods relative to similar individuals in the control group.  At posttest,
76:2390:232306:21:20:72:540:300:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the famous early childhood programs Perry Preschool and the Abecedarian Project had large impacts on
76:2391:232406:20:20:72:540:280:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:children’s achievement scores.  At age 40, treatment students from Perry Preschool had higher high school
76:2392:232511:20:21:72:540:260:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:completion rates (77% vs. 60%), were more like to be employed (76% vs. 62%), had higher median annual
76:2393:232612:21:20:72:540:239:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:earnings ($20,800 vs. $15,300), were more likely to own a house (37% vs. 28%), were more likely to have a
76:2394:232717:20:20:72:540:219:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:savings account (76% vs. 50%), and had better crime outcomes, self-reported health, and family-outcomes
76:2395:232820:20:21:72:540:199:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:compared to the control group (Schweinhart et al.   2005).   Similarly,  at the age 30 follow-up,  treatment
76:2396:232928:21:20:72:540:178:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:students from the Abecedarian Project had significantly higher levels of educational attainment (13.46 years
76:2397:233036:20:20:72:540:158:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:versus 12.31 years), were 17 percentage points more likely to hold a bachelor’s degree (CM = 6%), were 22
76:2398:233141:20:21:72:540:138:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:percentage points more likely to work full-time (CM = 53%), and were six times less likely to receive public
76:2399:233249:21:20:72:520:117:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assistance for more than 10% of the preceding seven years than students who were assigned to control.
76:2400:233350:20:20:88:539:97:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:In the absence of more long term outcomes for the vast majority of randomized field trials, we follow
76:2401:233451:20:0:72:540:77:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the methods described in Winship and Owen (2013) and simulate a life-cycle model similar to the Social
77:2402:233555:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Genome Model (SGM).33The SGM is a useful tool to simulate how shocks in a given life-stage may carry
77:2403:233655:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:over to later life outcomes. For example, one can simulate how much increasing reading test scores in early
77:2404:233762:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:childhood by 0.4σwould impact income at age 40.  We can thus use this simulation – coupled with data
77:2405:233862:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on treatment effects from the meta-analysis – to investigate what sort of income benefits might accrue if
77:2406:233967:20:21:72:540:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:we simply implement best practices. Winship and Owen (2013) provide evidence that the SGM reasonably
77:2407:234067:21:20:72:540:609:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:replicates key adult impacts of the Perry Preschool experiment, the Abecedarian Project, and the Chicago
77:2408:234171:20:36:72:310:589:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Child-Parent Centers program. We find similar results.
77:2409:234225:36:28:72:403:553:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:4.1.1    Interpreting the Literature Through A Simple Life-Cycle Model
77:2410:234295:28:20:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The model draws from the vast literature of human capital formation and assumes that cognitive and non-
77:2411:234398:20:21:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cognitive skill formation varies across an individual’s lifetime and is dependent on the stock of skills in pre-
77:2412:234510:21:20:72:540:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:vious stages of life.  Specifically, Winship and Owen (2013) define six different life-stages:  circumstances
77:2413:234619:20:20:72:540:464:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:at birth (CAB), early childhood (EC), middle childhood (MC), adolescence (AD), transition to adulthood
77:2414:234721:20:21:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(TTA), and adulthood (AH). The empirical model uses linear structural equations to describe the dependen-
77:2415:234826:21:20:72:540:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:cies between the outcomes in a given stage and all revealed outcomes from the stages preceding it. Formally,
77:2416:234934:20:20:72:539:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:given a vector of circumstances at birth,CAB, for individuali, each outcome in the vector of early childhood
77:2417:235042:20:21:72:198:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes,EC, is modeled as
77:2418:235068:21:30:222:389:362:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:?:EC Outcomei=βec0+βeccabCABi+εeci.
77:2419:235101:30:36:71:279:332:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Similarly, each of theMCoutcomes is given by
77:2420:235145:36:37:197:414:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:?:MC Outcomei=βmc0+βmccabCABi+βmcecECi+εmci.
77:2421:235187:37:37:71:233:259:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:For the adolescent life-stage we have
77:2422:235224:37:37:177:434:222:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:?:AD Outcomei=βad0+βadcabCABi+βadecECi+βadmcMCi+εadi.
77:2423:235275:37:36:71:300:185:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Outcomes when transitioning to adulthood would be
77:2424:235324:36:28:150:461:149:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:?:T T A Outcomei=βtta0+βttacabCABi+βttaecECi+βttamcMCi+βttaadADi+εttai.
77:2425:235393:28:14:84:539:121:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:33Due to there being no source code available – even upon request – and limited description in the SGM guide, we constructed
77:2426:235517:14:11:72:540:107:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:the model using our own assumptions about the cleaning, creation, and merging of the data. This leads to a final dataset used for the
77:2427:235650:11:11:72:540:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:simulations that is different from the one described in Winship and Owen (2013). However, when comparing the simulated impacts
77:2428:235776:11:11:72:540:85:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:reported in published papers using SGM to estimated impacts of the simulations, they are quite similar.  We provide the code and
77:2429:235904:11:0:72:169:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:data in an online appendix.
78:2430:235933:0:37:72:261:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:And finally, adult outcomes are modeled as
78:2431:235975:37:37:130:481:674:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:?:AH Outcomei=βah0+βahcabCABi+βahecECi+βahmcMCi+βahadADi+βahttaT T Ai+εahi.
78:2432:236048:37:20:88:539:637:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Whereβλψare  the  partial  correlations  of  realized  outcomes  from  theψlife-stage  (“0”  represents  an
78:2433:236155:20:20:71:323:617:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:intercept) with the given LHS outcome in theλlife-stage.
78:2434:236211:20:21:88:539:597:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:With a rich enough dataset, one can obtain the correlations linking all CAB, EC, MC, AD, TTA, and
78:2435:236308:21:20:71:539:576:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:AH outcomes together and investigate the indirect and direct impacts of varying one outcome on another.
78:2436:236411:20:20:71:539:556:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Importantly,  we  could  then  use  the  structural  equations  of  this  model  to  predict  how  a  shock  in  earlier
78:2437:236531:20:36:71:297:536:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:life-stages will propagate to outcomes in adulthood.
78:2438:236583:36:28:71:276:500:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:4.1.2    Simulating the Social Genome Model
78:2439:236626:28:20:71:539:472:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Unfortunately, as discussed by Winship and Owen (2013), there is not yet a reliable dataset that follows
78:2440:236730:20:21:71:539:452:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:an  individual  from  birth  through  adult  outcomes.   Therefore,  in  order  to  conduct  simulations  using  the
78:2441:236846:21:20:71:539:431:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:above model, we combine two well known public datasets: the National Longitudinal Survey of Youth 1979
78:2442:236948:20:20:71:539:411:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:(NLSY79) and the NLSY79 Child and Young Adult survey (CNLSY). From the CNLSY, we observe CAB,
78:2443:237041:20:21:71:539:391:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:EC, MC and AD outcomes. From the NLSY79, we observe TTA and AH outcomes. See Table 3 for a list of
78:2444:237139:21:20:71:539:370:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the specific variables that were used for each life-stage. The variables include a mix of cognitive skills (e.g.
78:2445:237251:20:20:71:539:350:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:standardized test scores), non-cognitive skills (e.g. self esteem and hyperactivity indices), and important life
78:2446:237363:20:21:71:299:330:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes (e.g. teen birth, drug use, and graduation).
78:2447:237416:21:20:88:539:309:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Using  these  two  datasets  and  the  equations  above,  we  are  able  to  estimate  the  coefficients  for  each
78:2448:237531:20:20:71:539:289:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outcome in a life-stage.  However, an issue arises in linking the life-stages across these two data sources.
78:2449:237639:20:21:71:539:269:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:Due to the age of respondents at first interview in the NLSY79, the data from earlier life stages is not as
78:2450:237746:21:20:71:539:248:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:rich as in the CNLSY. Therefore, the NLSY79 does not contain all of the CAB, EC, MC, and AD variables
78:2451:237847:20:20:71:540:228:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that the CNLSY has. In order to overcome this, we define a set of linking variables,LINK, that contains all
78:2452:237954:20:21:71:539:208:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes that are available in both the NLSY79 and the CNLSY. We can then estimate the following two
78:2453:238054:21:34:71:451:187:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:equations in the NLSY79 dataset to obtain coefficients for each TTA and AH outcome:
78:2454:238137:34:23:190:363:153:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f4:?:T T A Outcomei=βtta0+βttalinkLINKi+εttai
78:2455:238177:23:31:196:422:130:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:?:AH Outcomei=βah0+βahlinkLINKi+βahttaT T Ai+εahi.
78:2456:238225:31:20:88:539:99:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Using all of the coefficients generated from these estimations and the CNLSY data, we can then build
78:2457:238325:20:0:71:539:79:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:a  synthetic  baseline  dataset  of  birth  to  age  40  outcomes  for  the  CNLSY  sample.   Given  the  impact  of
79:2458:238443:0:20:72:540:711:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:an intervention at some life-stage,  we can then use the same coefficients to propagate the effects of the
79:2459:238549:20:21:72:540:691:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:intervention through the life-stages of these individuals.  Comparing a post-intervention estimation of an
79:2460:238655:21:20:72:540:670:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:outcome  to  the  baseline  estimation  would  then  provide  us  with  an  estimated  impact  of  the  intervention
79:2461:238771:20:20:72:540:650:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:on the given outcome.   See Winship and Owen (2013) and our Online Appendix B for a more in depth
79:2462:238868:20:37:72:232:630:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:discussion of the estimation process.
79:2463:238905:37:27:72:247:593:11:g_d0_f3:11:g_d0_f3:C:4.1.3    Simulating Impacts on Income
79:2464:238942:27:21:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:As mentioned,  our simulations are,  at best,  illustrative.   Relying on cross-sectional correlations,  making
79:2465:239053:21:20:72:540:545:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:important (untestable) assumptions on the law of motion of human capital development, and assuming that
79:2466:239156:20:20:72:540:525:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the variation induced by experiments would largely be consistent across groups and time are necessary for
79:2467:239261:20:21:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:our exercise. If, as Cunha and Heckman (2010) argue, “skills beget skills and abilities beget abilities” these
79:2468:239371:21:20:72:540:484:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:assumptions are overly restrictive and will bias our estimates downward.   If on the other hand,  as many
79:2469:239476:20:20:72:540:464:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:economists might find natural, there are diminishing marginal returns to interventions, then the forthcoming
79:2470:239584:20:21:72:172:444:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:estimates are too large.
79:2471:239608:21:20:88:539:423:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:If public policy were to implement the most successful math and reading interventions when children
79:2472:239707:20:20:72:540:403:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f8:B:are in early childhood, middle childhood, and adolescence, the expected test score increase would be 1.192σ
79:2473:239814:20:21:72:539:383:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in math and 2.449σin reading.34  35Using the model, the math impact would translate into a 8.28% increase
79:2474:239919:21:20:72:540:362:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:in income at age 40 and the reading impact would translate into a 25.06% increase.36Table 4 presents the
79:2475:240023:20:20:72:540:342:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:average successful impact for each category-life-stage and the estimated impact on income at age 40 if only
79:2476:240130:20:20:72:288:322:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:an intervention with that effect was implemented.
79:2477:240179:20:21:88:539:302:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:Whether or not the cumulative impact is enough to eliminate racial wage inequality depends on one’s
79:2478:240278:21:20:72:540:281:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:ability to “tag” (in the sense of Akerlof 1978) minorities among other things. We won’t hazard a quantitative
79:2479:240387:20:20:72:540:261:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:guess,  but  qualitatively  it  seems  clear  that  adhering  to  the  best  practices  gleaned  from  the  literature  on
79:2480:240509:20:21:72:540:241:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:randomized field trials discussed in this chapter would significantly reduce, if not eliminate, much of the
79:2481:240616:21:33:72:455:220:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:gap between racial groups in wages and other important economic and social outcomes.
79:2482:240700:33:14:84:539:187:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:34For the time being, there are no RCTs that estimate effects on children’s math and reading abilities during the circumstances
79:2483:240827:14:11:72:540:173:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:at birth life-stage.  Potential studies that focused on infants that our search returned were mostly excluded from our meta-analysis
79:2484:240959:11:8:72:262:162:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:for not using standardized math or reading measures.
79:2485:241011:8:14:84:539:154:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:35As  to  not  give  too  much  weight  in  this  exercise  to  any  one  study,  we  approximate  the  impact  of  the  “most  successful”
79:2486:241150:14:11:72:540:140:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:intervention for each life-stage as the average of the three largest statistically significant impacts from each category. If there were
79:2487:241286:11:11:72:540:129:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:no significant studies for a given category-life-stage,  we assign an impact of zero.   The cumulative impacts stated are the sum
79:2488:241415:11:11:72:540:118:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:of the five averages from the category-life-stages – early childhood, home (middle childhood), school (middle childhood), home
79:2489:241541:11:11:72:540:107:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:(adolescence), and school (adolescence).  This simple approximation assumes impacts are linearly additive one-time shocks and
79:2490:241666:11:8:72:189:96:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:experiments are externally valid.
79:2491:241699:8:14:84:539:88:7:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f8:F:36Using the cross-sectional estimates generated by Chetty et al.  (2014), the expected income gain at age 28 from a 1.192σ
79:2492:241821:14:0:72:492:74:9:g_d0_f2:9:g_d0_f2:F:increase in standardized math scores is 15.62% and from a 2.449σincrease in standardized reading scores is 32.08%.
80:2493:241937:0:32:72:162:711:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:C:5    Conclusion
80:2494:241952:32:20:72:540:679:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:The review of 196 randomized field experiments designed to increase human capital production unearthed
80:2495:242054:20:20:72:540:659:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:several facts. Early childhood investments, on average, significantly increase achievement. Yet, experiments
80:2496:242162:20:21:72:540:639:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:that attempt to alter the home environment in which children are reared in have shown very little success at
80:2497:242270:21:20:72:540:618:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:increasing student achievement.  Among school experiments, high-dosage tutoring and ‘managed’ profes-
80:2498:242371:20:20:72:540:598:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:sional development for teachers have shown to be effective. Ironically, high-dosage tutoring of adolescents
80:2499:242478:20:21:72:540:578:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:seems to be as effective – if not more effective – than early childhood investments.  This argues against
80:2500:242583:21:20:72:540:557:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:the growing view that there is a point at which investments in youth are unlikely to yield significant re-
80:2501:242689:20:20:72:540:537:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:turns (Carniero and Heckman 2003; Cullen et al. 2013). Lastly, charter schools can be effective avenues of
80:2502:242795:20:21:72:540:517:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:achievement-increasing reform, though the evidence on other market-based approaches such as vouchers or
80:2503:242898:21:20:72:273:496:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:school choice have less demonstrated success.
80:2504:242943:20:20:88:539:476:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:These facts provide reason for optimism.  Through the systematic implementation of randomized field
80:2505:243042:20:21:72:540:456:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:experiments designed to increase human capital of school-aged children, we have substantially increased
80:2506:243145:21:20:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:our knowledge of how to produce human capital and have assembled a canon of best practices.  And, in an
80:2507:243248:20:20:72:540:415:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:illustrative simulation exercise, we demonstrate that focusing on what we know has the potential to increase
80:2508:243356:20:20:72:255:395:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:income and reduce racial wage inequality.
80:2509:243397:20:21:88:539:375:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:A:The question is:  do we have the courage to implement, at scale, human capital policies based on best
80:2510:243498:21:43:72:322:354:11:g_d0_f2:11:g_d0_f2:B:practices developed from these randomized experiments?
